Accokeek v. PSC of Md.


No. 26, September Term, 2016


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


451 Md. 1; 150 A.3d 856; 2016 Md. LEXIS 839


November 7, 2016, Argued 
December 16, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Case No. 24-C-14-003896/AA.)
Accokeek, Mattawoman, Piscataway Creeks Cmtys. Council, Inc. v. Md. PSC, 227 Md. App. 265, 133 A.3d 1228, 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 32 (2016)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; PETITIONER TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Maryland Public Service Commission (PSC) properly issued a certificate of public convenience and necessity under Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 7-207(c) and (d) to the owner and operator of a liquefied natural gas terminal to build an electric generating station to support an expansion of its facility because an intervenor satisfied the test for standing in Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 3-202(a) (it was a party to the PSC proceeding and it was certainly dissatisfied with the PSC order), the exactions imposed by the conditions were primarily regulatory under Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 7-208(f)(1) and did not constitute taxes, the order complied with Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 3-113, and many of the impacts could not be separated from the larger project or be evaluated on a stand-alone basis.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

2 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Colvin v. State


No. 8, September Term, 2016


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


450 Md. 718; 150 A.3d 850; 2016 Md. LEXIS 817


September 7, 2016, Argued 
December 15, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Case Nos. 18906104, 18906105, 18906106.), Michael A DiPietro, JUDGE.
Colvin v. State, 226 Md. App. 131, 126 A.3d 814, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 164 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT TO DISMISS THE APPEAL; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-That the jury foreperson was not polled individually after she announced the jury's verdicts was a procedural error that was not cognizable under Md. R. 4-345(a), which permitted the court to correct an illegal sentence at any time but which had a narrow scope, because defendant did not allege any substantive error such that no sentence should have been imposed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was vacated.

 

3 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Spencer v. State


No. 94, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


450 Md. 530; 149 A.3d 610; 2016 Md. LEXIS 797


September 8, 2016, Argued 
November 29, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Dorchester County. Case No. 09-K-13-15062.), Brett W. Wilson, JUDGE.
Spencer v. State, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 401 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Oct. 2, 2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR DORCHESTER COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT FOR A NEW TRIAL. RESPONDENT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in granting the prosecution's Batson challenge, as defense counsel provided valid, race neutral explanations for his strikes of white panel members, and the court improperly relied on counsel's pattern from prior trials in finding that his explanations were a pretext for racial discrimination, because it in doing so it went outside of the record, precluding appellate review of its findings of fact; [2]-Defendant's conviction of attempted second-degree murder could not stand because the evidence did not establish that he formed the specific intent to kill the cyclist he hit with his car, since his actions could be wholly explained by his trying to flee the police, and the death of the cyclist was not a probable consequence of defendant's recklessly driving away from the police.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

 

4 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Washington v. State


No. 5 September Term, 2016


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


450 Md. 319; 148 A.3d 341; 2016 Md. LEXIS 725


September 1, 2016, Argued 
November 1, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DNA direct appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Case No.: 107164029), Charles J. Peters, JUDGE.
Washington v. State, 416 Md. 275, 6 A.3d 906, 2010 Md. LEXIS 686 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court properly dismissed defendant's petition for postconviction DNA testing for lack of standing because the State's duty to preserve DNA evidence postconviction under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. §§ 8-201(j) and 14-101 was never implicated where conspiracy to commit murder was not a crime of violence, defendant failed to obtain DNA testing of the evidence against him at the time of his trial, defendant's claim neither implicated a fundamental right nor a suspect class under Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24 and the postconviction DNA testing statute did not violate the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

 

5 of 744 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adams-Bey


No. 105, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


449 Md. 690; 144 A.3d 1200; 2016 Md. LEXIS 567


June 2, 2016, Argued 
August 25, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Criminal Case No. 02-K-10-002057. Postconviction Case No. 21,155. E. Mackell Childs, JUDGE.
State v. Adams-Bey, 446 Md. 290, 132 A.3d 193, 2016 Md. LEXIS 172 (2016)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Only the circuit court had discretion pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 7-104 (2001, 2008 Repl. Vol.) to determine whether it was in the interests of justice to grant an inmate's motion to reopen a postconviction proceeding (PCP), based on the unambiguous statutory language under the Postconviction Procedure Act; [2]-However, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 7-109, the Court of Special Appeals was authorized to reverse that decision upon finding that the circuit court committed an abuse of discretion; [3]-The circuit court's denial of an inmate's motion to reopen his PCP was an abuse of discretion because the jurors were given advisory only instructions, which constituted structural error that entitled him to a new trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

6 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Balt. Cnty. v. FOP


No. 25, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


449 Md. 713; 144 A.3d 1213; 2016 Md. LEXIS 568; 207 L.R.R.M. 3156


November 9, 2015, Argued 
August 25, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). Case No. 03-C-08-008643 OC CA. Michael J. Finifter, JUDGE.
Balt. County FOP, Lodge No. 4 v. Balt. County, 425 Md. 395, 41 A.3d 570, 2012 Md. LEXIS 223 (2012)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A county's no-appropriation argument with respect to enforcement of an arbitration decision in favor of county police officers, arising from a dispute over fixed subsidy of health insurance costs for retired officers, was precluded by the law of the case, as the courts previously considered the validity of the arbitration award (AA) and ruled in favor of the officers' union for enforcement of the award, and none of the exceptions to the doctrine applied; [2]-Moreover, the AA was not contrary to public policy based on the county's executive budget process because the Baltimore County, Md., Charter and Code provided for collective bargaining and binding interest arbitration to resolve an impasse in that bargaining, and the award was enforceable because there was a source of funds appropriated for the category of benefits under the award.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

7 of 744 DOCUMENTS


United Ins. Co. of Am. v. Md. Ins. Admin.


No. 101, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


450 Md. 1; 144 A.3d 1230; 2016 Md. LEXIS 569


June 1, 2016, Argued 
August 25, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Case No. 02-C-13-179785. William C. Mumford, II, JUDGE.
United Ins. Co. v. Md. Ins. Admin., 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 480 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Oct. 14, 2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONERS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court of Special Appeals properly affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of the insurers' action challenge to Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 16-118 (2011 Repl. Vol., 2015 Supp.) (effective October 1, 2013) for failure to exhaust administrative remedies in Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 2-210 (2011 Repl. Vol., 2015 Supp.) because, inter alia, the insurers' claim was predicated upon the Insurance Commissioner's "threat" that the Maryland Insurance Administration (MIA) would retroactively enforce the requirements of § 16-118 against the insurers' in-force policies, including those issued prior to the statute's effective date, the MIA viewed its jurisdiction over the insurers' claim as primary, and the insurers do not challenge § 16-118 as a whole, but only retroactive enforcement as applied only to their in-force policies.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

8 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Wicomico Cnty. Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. B.A.


No. 46, September Term, 2014


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


449 Md. 122; 141 A.3d 208; 2016 Md. LEXIS 439


June 3, 2015, Argued; December 3, 2015, Reargued 
July 12, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Wicomico County). Case No. 22-C-12-001286. W. Newton Jackson, JUDGE.
Wicomico Co. Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. B.A., 439 Md. 328, 96 A.3d 143, 2014 Md. LEXIS 514 (2014)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A martial arts instructor did not commit child sexual abuse, despite engaging in inappropriate communications with a 15-year-old student, because the sexually explicit communications occurred at the student's home and not while the student was in class or in the instructor's presence and, as such, the instructor did not have temporary care or custody or responsibility for the supervision of a 15-year-old student at the time of the communications, Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-701(x); there was a clear temporal break between the instructor-student relationship; [2]-There was insufficient evidence that the instructor engaged in "grooming" behavior during class; [3]-Substantial evidence supported the ALJ's determination that the local department of social services needed to modify its finding of child abuse from "indicated" to "ruled out."


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Grant v. State


No. 65, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


449 Md. 1; 141 A.3d 138; 2016 Md. LEXIS 443


March 4, 2016, Argued 
July 12, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Frederick County). Case No. 10-K-13-053987. Julie Stevenson Solt, JUDGE.
Grant v. State, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 497 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., July 24, 2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IS REVERSED WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY. COSTS TO BE PAID BY FREDERICK COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A deputy's search exceeded the scope of the traffic stop under U.S. Const. amend. IV by inserting his head into the vehicle's passenger window because the deputy did not detect the odor before his head crossed the passenger window, and he did not have probable cause or reasonable articulable suspicion that defendant was in possession of a controlled substance; there was no activity beyond the speeding violation, and defendant did not delay in stopping his vehicle or attempt to maneuver a detour.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Allen v. State


No. 92, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


449 Md. 98; 141 A.3d 194; 2016 Md. LEXIS 438


May 4, 2016, Argued 
July 12, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 17, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court of Wicomico County). Leah J. Seaton, JUDGE.
Allen v. State, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 384 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Oct. 7, 2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS ARE AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In defendant's sexual abuse case, the sentencing court did not err by imposing a condition of probation under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 6-221 that prohibited unsupervised contact with minors, including defendant's son, because, notwithstanding the disparities in gender and blood relation between the victim and defendant's son, the no-unsupervised-contact condition was reasonably related to the protection of minors, including the son.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Allmond v. Dep't of Health & Mental Hygiene


No. 34, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


448 Md. 592; 141 A.3d 57; 2016 Md. LEXIS 436


December 3, 2015, Argued 
July 11, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Howard County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case Nos. 13C14101885 & 13C15101923. Lenore R. Gelfman, JUDGE.
Allmond v. Md. State Dep't of Health & Mental Hygiene, 442 Md. 743, 114 A.3d 710, 2015 Md. LEXIS 302 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that although Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 10-708(g) permits involuntary medication without a showing of dangerousness within the facility, it does not, on its face, violate the substantive due process guarantee of Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24; [2]-However, in order for an authorization of involuntary medication under the statute to be constitutional, there must be, in addition to medical appropriateness, an overriding justification for administering the treatment, such as a need to render the pretrial detainee competent for trial; [3]-The Court held that the State may not medicate defendant against his will without convening another clinical review panel, which, had to comply with the standards it set forth in its opinion in order to apply the statute constitutionality.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Conover v. Conover


No. 79, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


450 Md. 51; 141 A.3d 31; 2016 Md. LEXIS 813


April 5, 2016, Argued 
July 7, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected on September 30, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY: Circuit Court for Washington County. Case No.: 21-C-13-046273 DA. Certiorai to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Washington County). Daniel P. Dwyer JUDGE.
Conover v. Conover, 448 Md. 548, 2016 Md. LEXIS 433 (2016)
Conover v. Conover, 224 Md. App. 366, 120 A.3d 874, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 107 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that de facto parents have standing to contest custody or visitation and need not show parental unfitness or exceptional circumstances before a trial court can apply a best interests of the child analysis; [2]-In so ruling, the Court overruled Janice M. v. Margaret K., 404 Md. 661 (2008) because it is clearly wrong and has been undermined by the passage of time; [3]-The Court held that in light of its differentiation in McDermott, between pure third parties and those persons who are in a parental role, the Court now makes explicit that de facto parents are distinct from other third parties.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to lower appellate court with instructions to remand case to trial court for further proceedings.

 

13 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. State


No. 50 September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


448 Md. 318; 139 A.3d 936; 2016 Md. LEXIS 368


January 11, 2016, Argued 
June 23, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Maryland. Criminal Case No. 122148. Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). Mary Beth McCormick JUDGE.
Hall v. State, 444 Md. 638, 120 A.3d 766, 2015 Md. LEXIS 625 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY MONTGOMERY COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was insufficient to support defendant's conviction of criminal child neglect in violation of Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 3-602.1, because her conduct in leaving her difficult to control three-year-old son in the overnight care of his 14-year-old sister, evaluated objectively, did not create a substantial risk of harm, as the sister was deemed an age-appropriate caregiver for the boy under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-801(a); although defendant was negligent in not responding to phone calls from the sister and the police after her son escaped from the home, she was not guilty of criminal child neglect.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

 

14 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Brutus 630, LLC v. Town of Bel Air


No. 67 September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


448 Md. 355; 139 A.3d 957; 2016 Md. LEXIS 370


March 7, 2016, Argued 
June 23, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected on September 30, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Harford County. Case No. 12-C-13-2116. Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Harford County). William O. Carr JUDGE.
Brutus 630 v. Town of Bel Air, 445 Md. 125, 126 A.3d 3, 2015 Md. LEXIS 811 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE MARYLAND TAX COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that a person who has paid a sewer connection fee imposed by a municipality and alleges that the fee is illegal or miscalculated may seek a refund from the municipality under Md. Local Government Code Ann. § 20-113 et seq., and that the voluntary payment doctrine did not bar such a refund claim; [2]-The court further held that the Maryland Tax Court has jurisdiction under Md. Local Government Code Ann. § 20-117 of an administrative appeal of a denial of such a refund claim; [3]-As such, the court held that the taxpayer may pursue its refund claim under the refund statute, Md. Local Government Code Ann. § 20-113 et seq., that its claim was not barred by the voluntary payment doctrine, and that the Maryland Tax Court has jurisdiction to consider the appeal.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to lower appellate court with instructions to remand case to trial court with instructions to remand case to Maryland Tax Court for further proceedings.

 

15 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Assateague Coastal Trust, Inc. v. Schwalbach


No. 59, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


448 Md. 112; 136 A.3d 866; 2016 Md. LEXIS 295


February 9, 2016, Argued 
May 23, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Worcester County. Case No. 23-C-13-1617.
Assateague Coastal Trust, Inc. v. Schwalbach, 223 Md. App. 631, 117 A.3d 606, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 86 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The lower courts properly upheld a decision by a county board of zoning appeals that granted a variance to an owner under Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-1808 and Worcester County, Md., Natural Resources Code § 3-111 because, inter alia, without the variance, the owner would suffer an unwarranted hardship--i.e., he would not be able to exercise the riparian rights associated with the property, a reasonable and significant use that could not be exercised elsewhere on the entire property, the granting of the variance would not adversely affect water quality or the fish, wildlife, or plant habitat within the Critical Area, and the owner rebutted the presumption of non-conformity of the proposed variance.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Seenath


No. 82, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


448 Md. 145; 136 A.3d 885; 2016 Md. LEXIS 291


April 5, 2016, Argued 
May 23, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Case No. 405656V.
Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Seenath, 446 Md. 218, 130 A.3d 507, 2016 Md. LEXIS 54 (2016)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE. RESPONDENT TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-As applied challenge by a detained driver to Motor Vehicle Administration Advice of Rights form under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1 (1977, 2012 Repl. Vol., 2015 Supp.) lacked merit, as there was no indication that the driver was misled by it or that he was prejudiced by his decision to consent to take the alcohol concentration test (ACT); [2]-The driver's facial challenge to the form also failed, as upon balancing the interests of the detained driver and the State, it was not misleading as to a commercial driver's license holder's eligibility for a restrictive license due to his failed ACT while driving a non-commercial vehicle because he was adequately advised pursuant to the statute, and additional warnings as to every possibility were not required.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; matter remanded with instruction to affirm decision of administrative law judge.

Merchant v. State


Misc. No. 16 and No. 81, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


448 Md. 75; 136 A.3d 843; 2016 Md. LEXIS 293


March 7, 2016, Argued 
May 23, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Merch. v. State, 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 533 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., July 14, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Case No. CT00-0536X, Case No. CT10-0648X.
Stoddard v. Dep't of Health & Mental Hygiene, 445 Md. 487, 128 A.3d 51, 2015 Md. LEXIS 891 (Dec. 18, 2015)



DISPOSITION: IN CASE MISC. NO. 16, CERTIFIED QUESTIONS OF LAW ANSWERED. COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN THE PARTIES. IN CASE NO. 81, JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in finding that Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 3-114 et seq., governing the granting or revoking of a committed person's conditional release, violated the separation of powers, because it provided for mandatory judicial review of the ALJ's decision, and the substantial evidence standard of review of did not impermissibly delegate judicial authority to the executive branch; [2]-In revoking committee one's conditional release, the trial court erred in holding an evidentiary hearing and finding he had not met his burden of proof, as it found that the ALJ's recommendation that he be conditionally released was supported by sufficient evidence; [3]-As committee two had requested the administrative procedure under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 3-119(b), the trial court erred by holding its own hearing and in declining to consider the ALJ's report.


OUTCOME: The high court answered the intermediate appellate court's certified questions in the affirmative.

19 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Garrity v. Md. State Bd. of Plumbing


No. 35, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


447 Md. 359; 135 A.3d 452; 2016 Md. LEXIS 276


December 4, 2015, Argued 
April 26, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Specail Appeals (Circuit Court for Wicomico County) Donald C. Davis JUDGE.
Garrity v. Md. State Bd. of Plumbing, 221 Md. App. 678, 110 A.3d 769, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 30 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that the amount of the fine imposed against a plumber did not transform the civil penalty into criminal punishment and did not place him in jeopardy for purposes of the Double Jeopardy Clause, U.S. Const. amend. V, because the plumber committed over 7,000 violations and engaged in a pattern of deceit against hundreds of Maryland homeowners over the course of several years and the extensive number of violations did not transform the large monetary penalty into a criminal punishment; [2]-The court further held that principles of judicial economy and fairness are served by application of offensive non-mutual collateral estoppel in the case of two administrative proceedings where the second agency could not have joined the first agency's proceeding and the same facts support violations of the respective agency's statutes.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

20 of 744 DOCUMENTS


State v. Graves


No. 57, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


447 Md. 230; 135 A.3d 376; 2016 Md. LEXIS 215


February 8, 2016, Argued 
April 22, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 11, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Maryland. Criminal Case No. K-2012-001807.
Graves v. State, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 1016 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., June 23, 2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-As the assistant public defender (APD) who represented defendant indicated to the trial court that defendant wanted a postponement in order to hire private counsel that he had retained in the past, which clearly implicated Md. R. 4-215(e), the trial court should have sought an explanation from defendant for his request to discharge the APD, or else ensure that defendant agreed that the reasons advanced by the APD were accurate and/or complete; [2]-The trial court's denial of defendant's postponement request before permitting him to explain his reasons for his request did not comply with the "precise rubric" outlined in Rule 4-215(e), as the trial court's reliance on the APD's explanation was not sufficient.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

21 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Reliable Contr. Co. v. Md. Underground Facilities Damage Prevention Auth.


NO. 47, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


446 Md. 707; 133 A.3d 1112; 2016 Md. LEXIS 108


January 8, 2016, Argued 
March 28, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 22, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County) William C. Mulford, III, Judge. Case No. 02-C-13-182390AA.
Reliable Contr. Co. v. Md. Underground Facilities Damage Prevention Auth., 222 Md. App. 683, 114 A.3d 303, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 58 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY WITH INSTRUCTIONS FOR THAT COURT TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE MARYLAND UNDERGROUND DAMAGE PREVENTION AUTHORITY FOR REASSESSMENT OF THE CIVIL MONETARY PENALTY CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because the Maryland Underground Damage Prevention Authority was an administrative agency that exercised quasi-judicial powers that were subject to judicial review, its enabling law, Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 12-101 et seq., was not contrary to either the Judicial Vesting Clause of Md. Const. art. IV, § 1 or the Separation of Powers Clause of Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 8; [2]-Because the Authority was an administrative agency in the executive branch of state government, Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-1001 provided the necessary guidelines for the exercise of its discretion in assessing civil penalties.


OUTCOME: Judgment of Court of Special Appeals vacated and remanded.

 

22 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Gonce


No. 38, September Term, 2015


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


446 Md. 100; 130 A.3d 436; 2016 Md. LEXIS 4


December 7, 2015, Argued 
January 22, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Case No. 03-C-14-011601. Nancy M. Purpura, JUDGE.
Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Gonce, 443 Md. 234, 116 A.3d 474, 2015 Md. LEXIS 414 (2015)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE. RESPONDENT TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: The court held that under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(b)(2) and (3), a driver is subject to an automatic license suspension for a refusal to take a drug test where the driver has taken an alcohol concentration test and a law enforcement officer has reasonable grounds to believe that the driver was driving while impaired by drugs or a combination of drugs and alcohol; [2]-The court held that based on § 16-205.1's plain language, a driver may be asked to submit to both an alcohol concentration test and a drug test, and the driver cannot have an automatic license suspension overturned on the basis that § 16-205.1 permits a law enforcement officer to request only one test; the court emphasized that § 16-205.1 authorizes law enforcement officers to request an alcohol concentration test and a drug test, without any explicit language indicating that the tests are mutually exclusive.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to trial court with direction.

Litz v. Md. Dep't of the Env't

McClanahan v. Wash. Cnty. Dep't of Soc. Servs.


No. 79, September Term, 2014


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


445 Md. 691; 129 A.3d 293; 2015 Md. LEXIS 868


September 9, 2015, Argued 
December 22, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Washington County. Case No.: 21-C-11-42484-AA. Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Washington County). Donald E. Beachley JUDGE.
McClanahan v. Wash. County Dep't of Soc. Servs., 218 Md. App. 258, 96 A.3d 917, 2014 Md. App. LEXIS 77 (2014)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT OF WASHINGTON COUNTY, AND DIRECT THAT COURT TO REVERSE.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The limitation on the exculpatory scope of Md. Code Regs. 07.02.07.12C(2)(a)(i) for accidental injury to alleged abusers (AA) causing physical injury was unenforceable as Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law §§ 5-701(b) (2012) and 5-706 did not justify a distinction between physical and mental injury; [2]-To be included as a child abuser (CA) in the central registry (CR), one had to intend to injure the child (C) or act in reckless disregard of the C's welfare; [3]-Even if a mother intended to gain an advantage in a custody battle by taking her C for vaginal examinations based on claims of the father's sexual abuse, inclusion on the CR as a CA was not proper unless she intended to harm the C or acted in reckless disregard of the C's welfare; [4]-Where the AA's conduct could benefit the C, as medical treatment did, there had to be evidence that the AA was reckless as to the C's health.


OUTCOME: Appellate court's judgment reversed. Case remanded with direction.

State v. Waine, 441 Md. 61, 105 A.3d 489, 2014 Md. LEXIS 935 (2014)

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-There was no cause to deviate from the doctrine of stare decisis with respect to the holding in Unger v. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Fuller v. Republican Cent. Comm.


No. 92, September Term, 2014


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


444 Md. 613; 120 A.3d 751; 2015 Md. LEXIS 568


March 2, 2015, Argued 
August 21, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case No. 06-C-15-068169. Fred S. Hecker, JUDGE.
Fuller v. Republican Cent. Comm., 442 Md. 150, 110 A.3d 703, 2015 Md. LEXIS 115 (2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred in denying the petition of members of a political party's central committee for a writ of mandamus and a TRO enjoining the committee from submitting more than one name to the governor to fill a vacancy in the House of Delegates. HOLDINGS: [1]-The case was justiciable, as the issue--whether Md. Const. art. III, § 13 required the central committee to submit only one name to the governor--admitted of judicial resolution and could be decided by the high court without intruding on the authority and discretion of the committee or the governor; [2]-The central committee had the authority to determine its own procedures, and § 13 did not impose on a duty on the committee to submit only one name to the governor; the sole duty set forth in § 13 was on the governor to appoint a person from any name or names submitted in writing by the central committee.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cooper v. Rodriguez


No. 87, September Term, 2014


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


443 Md. 680; 118 A.3d 829; 2015 Md. LEXIS 488


June 3, 2015, Argued 
July 24, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Case No. 24-C-06-004331), Sylvester B. Cox, JUDGE.
Rodriguez v. State, 218 Md. App. 573, 98 A.3d 376, 2014 Md. App. LEXIS 90 (2014)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. PETITIONER TO PAY COSTS IN THIS COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-It was error for the trial court to strike a jury's finding of gross negligence in an action against a correctional officer (CO), arising from an inmate's murder by another prisoner while riding on a prison transport bus, as the CO was not entitled to immunity under the Maryland Tort Claims Act, Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 12-105 and Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-522(b) (1973, 2013 Repl. Vol.), because the evidence showed he was aware of the prisoner's attack on the inmate, yet intentionally failed to perform his duty to protect him; [2]-The CO was not entitled to common law public official immunity because the exception for gross negligence applied; [3]-The special relationship exception was a limitation on the public duty doctrine and did not govern the determination of whether the CO was entitled to common law public official immunity.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Anne Arundel Cnty. v. Bell


No. 29, September Term, 2014


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


442 Md. 539; 113 A.3d 639; 2015 Md. LEXIS 285


December 5, 2014, Argued 
April 21, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 23, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Case No.: C-11-163163), Nancy Davis-Loomis, JUDGE.
Bell v. Anne Arundel County, 215 Md. App. 161, 79 A.3d 976, 2013 Md. App. LEXIS 155 (2013)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Taxpayer standing, not property owner standing, applied to judicial challenges to comprehensive zoning legislation; [2]-The challengers to an Anne Arundel County comprehensive zoning ordinance did not allege taxpayer standing where two of them were incorporated and assumed to be taxpayers and they alleged that the adoption of the county's zoning reclassifications constituted illegal spot zoning as they did not allege that the illegal action would result in a pecuniary loss or an increase in taxes; [3]-Frustration with increased traffic, annoyance with increased noise, and violations of a right (if any) to participate in zoning changes were not the sort of harms with which taxpayer standing was concerned; [4]-Even if these harms were within the purview of taxpayer standing, they were not unique to the challengers, as opposed to the general public.


OUTCOME: Appellate court's judgment reversed. Case remanded to appellate court with directions to affirm trial court's judgment.

Jacome de Espina v. Jackson

442 Md. 311; 112 A.3d 442; 2015 Md. LEXIS 168

March 30, 2015, Filed

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. PETITIONERS TO PAY COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-With respect to claims arising from a police officer's fatal shooting of the decedent in violation of the state constitution, application of the damages cap under Md. Rights arts. 19 and 24 because the LGTCA cap did not eviscerate the remedy, it was a reasonable restriction, and it did not operate to impair the cause of action; [2]-Wrongful death claims were considered collectively as one individual claim, such that the wrongful death claims of the decedent's son and surviving spouse were aggregated with the survival claim of the decedent's estate, and constituted "an individual claim" to which the damages cap applied.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Circuit Court retained jurisdiction for a reasonable time to decide the timely-filed application to extend the 2006 Order of Conditional Release, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 3-122 because the Maryland General Assembly did not intend to place a finite deadline by which courts had to rule on timely-filed applications to extend conditional release; [2]-A decision on a timely-filed extension request rendered after the expiration of an order of conditional release did not ipso facto violate due process, when decided within a reasonable time and where no undue prejudice was shown during the time it took to decide the application; [3]-There was no indication of undue prejudice or that the Circuit Court delayed for an unreasonable time before ruling on the State's application for an extension on the patient's conditional release.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the court of appeals affirmed.

441 Md. 673; 109 A.3d 1147; 2015 Md. LEXIS 26

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The State's Attorney had discretion to charge defendant with a violation of Md. Code Ann., Pub. Safety § 5-133(c)(1)(ii), Md. Code Ann., Crim. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

McCree v. State


No. 20, September Term, 2014


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


441 Md. 4; 105 A.3d 456; 2014 Md. LEXIS 869; 113 U.S.P.Q.2D (BNA) 1844


November 6, 2014, Argued 
December 18, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County) Case No. 17-K-10-007592. Thomas G. Ross, JUDGE.
McCree v. State, 214 Md. App. 238, 76 A.3d 400, 2013 Md. App. LEXIS 128 (2013)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. PETITIONER TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the intermediate appellate court, in affirming defendant's conviction of violating the trademark counterfeiting statute, Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 8-611, erred in approving the trial court's ruling that § 8-611 was neither facially overbroad nor facially void for vagueness. HOLDINGS: [1]-Section 8-611 was not facially overbroad because it did not criminalize the display or distribution of goods that had no retail value and were not meant to be sold; thus, it did not criminalize conduct that U.S. Const. amend. I's Free Speech Clause indisputably protected, such as the mere display of signs or distribution of pamphlets; [2]-Section 8-611 was not facially void for vagueness because its prohibitions of acts involving "intellectual property" were clearly defined, and there was no need to guess at § 8-611's meaning or to differ as to its application.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Appellee sex offender did not have to involuntarily register as a sex offender in Maryland under the Sex Offender Registration and Notification Act (SORNA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 16901 et seq. & 18 U.S.C.S. § 2250, because, under Md. Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Deering


No. 52, September Term, 2013


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


438 Md. 611; 92 A.3d 495; 2014 Md. LEXIS 357


January 9, 2014, Argued 
May 21, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to theCircuit Court for Somerset County. Case No. 19-C-015606. D. William Simpson, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SOMERSET COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE PRESIDING OVER RESPONDENT'S LICENSE SUSPENSION HEARING. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Case law recognized a qualified due process right of a detained driver to consult with counsel before deciding whether to take a breath test, but even if such a right might require the suppression in a criminal case, that does not necessarily require exclusion in an administrative proceeding; [2]-The court confirms the dicta in Najafi v. Motor Vehicle Administration that a violation of this right does not require suppression of the test result or refusal in proceedings concerning the administrative suspension of the driver's license; [3]-Even if a suspected drunk driver is denied the opportunity to consult counsel before deciding whether to take a test, the driver remains subject to the administrative license suspension that Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1 assigns to a test refusal or a particular test result, and the suspension in this case was properly upheld.


OUTCOME: Circuit court judgment reversed, case remanded with directions.

February 26, 2014, Filed

Costs and fees proceeding at State v. Braverman, 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 58 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., June 1, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case No. 02-C-07126810. Paul F. Harris, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE STATE OF MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-402.3 (2010) was unconstitutional under Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24 and Md. Const. art. III, § 40. HOLDINGS: [1]-The statute was unconstitutional because it eliminated a ground lease holder's right to seek a judicial remedy on a tenant's default without fair notice; [2]-It was unconstitutional because the holder's right to re-enter upon a default was part of the holder's vested bundle of rights, which the statute impaired after the right vested; [3]-The statute was unconstitutional because a holder's right of reentry was not a remedy the legislature could switch out, and the right was a vested part of the bundle of rights essential to the nature of these leases; [4]-The statute was unconstitutional because its foreclosure-and-lien remedy did not adequately replace ejectment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

FOP Lodge 35 v. Montgomery County


No. 132, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


436 Md. 1; 80 A.3d 686; 2013 Md. LEXIS 901; 197 L.R.R.M. 2733



December 2, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: FOP Lodge 35 v. Montgomery County, 427 Md. 522, 50 A.3d 8, 2012 Md. LEXIS 457 (2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether all the signatures of registered voters collected by an affiant, who, in completing the affidavit to an election referendum petition pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-204 (2003, 2010 Repl. Vol.), provided partially incorrect zip code information, were invalidated. HOLDINGS: [1]-Minor errors in the circulator affidavit did not invalidate petition signatures that were already certified by the appropriate administrative body; [2]-Having one or two digits of a circulator's zip code misstated did not defeat that purpose of attaching the circulator's affidavit to petition signatures, so that the circulator of the petition could be identified, located, and served a subpoena; [3]-The circulators still could be identified, as the addresses provided were more than adequate for their intended purposes, and the correct zip code was easily discoverable and available.


OUTCOME: Ruling reversed and decision of county board of elections upheld.

Miles v. State


No. 36, September Term, 2012


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


435 Md. 540; 80 A.3d 242; 2013 Md. LEXIS 834



November 25, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
DEATH PENALTY APPEAL, Thomas G. Ross JUDGE.
Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County. Case No. 17-K-97-004789.
Miles v. State, 365 Md. 488, 781 A.2d 787, 2001 Md. LEXIS 614 (2001)



DISPOSITION: DENIAL BY THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR QUEEN ANNE'S COUNTY OF MOTION TO CORRECT ILLEGAL SENTENCE AFFIRMED. APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to correct his illegal sentence on the ground that the death penalty statute violated Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 16; [2]-Death was the common law penalty for murder, and the sanguinary laws clause applied to legislative action and had never been triggered by any Maryland statutory modifications of the common law relating to the types of murders to which the death penalty could apply or by the statutes modifying the method of executing the death penalty; [3]-If the sanguinary laws clause of Article 16, as originally adopted, was retroactive and self-executing, as to existing common law, the clause was not intended to exclude death, per se, as a possible penalty for murder; [4]-There was no indication that Article 16 was intended to change pre-existing law.


OUTCOME: Denial of motion to correct illegal sentence affirmed.

OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether an indigent criminal defendant was entitled to state-furnished counsel at an initial appearance before a district court commissioner pursuant to Md. R. 4-213(a). HOLDINGS: [1]-Under the due process component of Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24, an indigent defendant had a right to state-furnished counsel at an initial appearance before a district court commissioner because the defendant was in custody and, absent release, would remain so until a review hearing before a judge, appointing counsel at the review hearing did not cure the constitutional defect of denying counsel at the initial appearance, and incarcerating a defendant as a result of a hearing at which the defendant was unrepresented, absent a waiver of counsel, was fundamentally unfair.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated.

Kendall v. Howard County


No. 50, September Term, 2012


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


431 Md. 590; 66 A.3d 684; 2013 Md. LEXIS 298



May 21, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Howard County. Case No. 13-C-09-079522OC), Timothy J. McCrone, JUDGE.
Kendall v. Howard County, 204 Md. App. 440, 41 A.3d 727, 2012 Md. App. LEXIS 38 (2012)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONERS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents were granted certiorari to challenge the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the dismissal of their case against defendant county by a trial court. Plaintiffs brought a declaratory judgment action claiming that defendant violated the county charter by taking certain actions by resolution or administrative decision instead of passing an original bill, as required by the charter.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had granted defendant's motion to dismiss, ruling, in part, that plaintiffs lacked standing. The Court of Special Appeals affirmed the judgment of dismissal, holding that plaintiffs failed to show a concrete injury to their voting rights and thereby lacked standing. The Court upheld the dismissal , finding that while plaintiffs took great pains to characterize their grievance as a deprivation of the right to referendum, the right to vote, and related free speech and association rights, at its core, their complaint was grounded in one thing and one thing only: the allegation that defendant's methods for accomplishing certain decisions violated its own Charter. As such, the Court held that plaintiffs' claim amounted to nothing more than an abstract, generalized interest in defendant's compliance with its Charter, which was shared by all members of the general public in the county. On that ground alone, plaintiffs were held to have failed to establish standing.


OUTCOME: The Court affirmed the judgment.

 

63 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr. Servs.


No. 125, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


430 Md. 535; 62 A.3d 123; 2013 Md. LEXIS 142



March 4, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Certification granted by, Decision reached on appeal by Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr. Servs. v. Doe, 2014 Md. LEXIS 417 (Md., June 30, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Washington County), John H. McDowell, JUDGE.
Doe v. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr. Servs., 425 Md. 227, 40 A.3d 39, 2012 Md. LEXIS 161 (2012)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WASHINGTON COUNTY AND TO DIRECT THE CIRCUIT COURT TO ENTER A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. RESPONDENT TO PAY THE COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner registrant filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that he not be required to register as a sex offender under the Maryland sex offender registration statute (SORS), Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 11-701 et seq. (Cum. Supp. 2012), and that he be removed from the Maryland Sex Offender Registry. After a transfer, the trial court denied the requested relief. The Maryland Court of Special Appeals affirmed.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court issued a writ of certiorari. A plurality of the state's highest court analyzed the ex post facto issue under Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 17. The registrant committed an underlying child sex offense during the 1983-84 school year. SORS was enacted in 1995. The registrant was charged in 2005, and was required to register as a sex offender under the 2009 and 2010 amendments' retroactive application of the SORS. The disadvantage analysis applied to ex post facto issues under art. 17. The registrant could not have had fair warning of any legally imposed sanctions beyond those provided for at the time of his crime. Imposing registration upon the registrant changed the consequences of the registrant's crime to his disadvantage. The application of the SORS to the registrant in 2009 was the equivalent of imposing the additional criminal sanction of probation or parole for the registrant's prior commission of a sex crime in the 1980's. Under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 11-707(a)(4) (Cum. Supp. 2012), the registrant had to register for life. The dissemination of the registrant's information pursuant to the SORS was tantamount to shaming for life and was punitive.


OUTCOME: In a plurality opinion, the judgment of the appellate court was reversed. The case was remanded to the appellate court with directions to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to direct the trial court to enter a declaratory judgment consistent with the opinion.

Md. State Comptroller of the Treasury v. Wynne


No. 107, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


431 Md. 147; 64 A.3d 453; 2013 Md. LEXIS 17



January 28, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by, Stay granted by, Clarified by Md. State Comptroller of the Treasury v. Wynne, 431 Md. 147, 64 A.3d 453, 2013 Md. LEXIS 290 (2013)
Later proceeding at Comptroller of the Treasury v. Wynne, 134 S. Ct. 982, 187 L. Ed. 2d 771, 2014 U.S. LEXIS 585 (U.S., 2014)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by Comptroller of the Treasury v. Wynne, 134 S. Ct. 2660, 189 L. Ed. 2d 208, 2014 U.S. LEXIS 3745 (U.S., 2014)
Affirmed by Comptroller of the Treasury of Md. v. Wynne Et Ux, 2015 U.S. LEXIS 3404 (U.S., May 18, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Howard County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Appeals. Louis A. Becker, III, JUDGE.


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY AFFIRMED WITH DIRECTION TO REMAND TO THE TAX COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE SHARED EQUALLY BY THE PARTIES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maryland State Comptroller of the Treasury appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which reversed a tax court decision and invalidated an assessment that had not allowed a credit against the county income tax portion of the Maryland individual income tax for income generated by a Subchapter S corporation outside Maryland.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, a married couple, owned stock in a Subchapter S corporation that did business in multiple states. They reported pass-through income of the corporation on their Maryland tax return and claimed their pro rata share of income taxes paid by the corporation to other states as a credit pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 10-703(c) against their Maryland individual income tax. Pursuant to § 10-703(a), no credit was allowed against the county tax for income taxes paid by the corporation to other states. The court held that the application of the county tax without a credit for pass-through S corporation income taxed in other states discriminated against interstate commerce and thus violated the dormant Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. Although the county income tax was not directed at interstate commerce, its application without a credit for S corporation income taxed in other states could affect the interstate market for capital and business investment by causing Maryland residents to invest only in Maryland businesses. The county tax without a credit was not fairly apportioned because it lacked both internal consistency and external consistency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded for further proceedings in the tax court.

Frazier v. Castle Ford, Ltd.


No. 93, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


430 Md. 144; 59 A.3d 1016; 2013 Md. LEXIS 16



January 24, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). Joseph Aloysius Dugan, Jr., JUDGE.
Frazier v. Castle Ford, Ltd., 200 Md. App. 285, 27 A.3d 583, 2011 Md. App. LEXIS 103 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED IN PART AND AFFIRMED IN PART. THIS CASE IS REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner customer sued respondent car dealer, alleging unfair and deceptive trade practices under the Maryland Consumer Protection Act, and common law fraud. After the dealer extended the customer's warranty, the trial court granted the dealer's motion to deny class certification, granted in part its motion for summary judgment, and awarded the customer attorney's fees. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The customer alleged that the dealer misrepresented the term of an extended manufacturer's warranty that he purchased for his car. The customer alleged that he brought the problem to the dealer's attention, but the dealer took no action to remedy it. Once the class action was filed, the dealer tendered individual damages to the customer, and argued that the customer could not prosecute a class action. The first issue before the court of appeals was whether the tender required the court to deny class certification. The court of appeals concluded that it did not, holding that a tender of individual relief to the putative class representative did not moot a class action if the individual plaintiff did not have a reasonable opportunity to seek class certification, including any necessary discovery. The court of appeals also concluded that punitive damages were not foreclosed by the tender of individual compensatory damages. Finally, the court of appeals concluded that the award of attorney's fees was not limited to fees incurred before the tender, as the court considered the dealer's correction of warranties purchased by other customers as within "the results obtained" by counsel.


OUTCOME: The order granting the dealer's motion to deny class certification was reversed and case was remanded for reconsideration of that issue, as well as the award of punitive damages. The award of attorney's fees was affirmed.

Bourgeois v. Live Nation Entm't


Misc. No. 8, September Term, 2012


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


430 Md. 14; 59 A.3d 509; 2013 Md. LEXIS 10



January 18, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Bourgeois v. Live Nation Entm't, Inc., 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 83423 (D. Md., June 14, 2012)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] QUESTIONS ANSWERED AS HEREIN SET FORTH; COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLANTS AND ONE-HALF BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the District of Maryland certified four questions to the court in plaintiff consumers' class action suit alleging that defendants, a licensed exhibitor and several entities that sold tickets to the exhibitor's events, had violated Baltimore City ordinances regulating the sale of tickets to entertainment and sports events.


OVERVIEW: A consumer purchased a ticket through an online ticket agency and paid a service charge exceeding the 50-cent fee specified in Baltimore, Md., City Code art. 15, § 21-2. The ticket agency's agreement with the exhibitor authorized the ticket agency to make original sales of tickets as the exhibitor's agent. The licensing requirement of Baltimore, Md., City Code art. 15, § 21-1(a) did not apply to the ticket agency because it was acting as the exhibitor's agent. Section 21-1(b), when read in conjunction with Baltimore, Md., City Code art. 15, § 21-3, did not allow the exhibitor to authorize anyone to charge more than the established price. The prohibition against scalping in Baltimore, Md., City Code art. 19, § 55-1(a) applied not only to the resale of tickets, but also to original sales by an exhibitor or its agent. Only a licensed ticket agency was exempted under § 55-1(b) from the prohibition, and only to the extent of collecting the 50-cent fee. A common law action for money had and received could be maintained to recover money paid under an executory illegal contract, under an illegal contract that had been fully executed as to which the parties were in pari delicto.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the ticket agency did not have to be licensed to sell tickets as the exhibitor's agent, but it could sell them only at the established price; that the prohibition against scalping was not limited to the resale of tickets; that only a licensed ticket agency could collect a service charge; and that a common law action for money had and received could be maintained if the ticket sale agreement remained executory.

State v. Ray


No. 23, September Term, 2012


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


429 Md. 566; 57 A.3d 444; 2012 Md. LEXIS 837



December 18, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Harford County). Thomas E. Marshall, JUDGE.
Adams v. State, 204 Md. App. 418, 41 A.3d 572, 2012 Md. App. LEXIS 8 (2012)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE HARFORD COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT'S DENIAL OF MOTION TO DISMISS CHARGES AND REMAND FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN PETITIONER AND RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversing the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss charges for first-degree attempted murder and lesser included offenses. Defendant had previously been found incompetent to stand trial, committed to the Department of Health and Mental Hygiene, had the charges dismissed under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 3-107 (2001, 2008 Rep. Vol., 2012 Cum. Supp.), and been re-indicated.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the State could re-institute criminal charges against a defendant who succeeded in having those charges dismissed under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 3-107, without some showing that the defendant regained competency. Defendant argued that the State should not be allowed to continue to confine him by simply re-indicting him on the same charges that were required to be dismissed under § 3-107. The State argued that re-institution of charges initially dismissed under § 3-107 was supported by the fact hat the legislature specifically stated that dismissal under § 3-107 was "without prejudice." The court of appeals held that in order to hold a detainee after a § 3-107 dismissal, the State must show that the detainee was restorable, but nothing in the incompetency statutes required the State to make a restorability showing when it reindicted a defendant. Since neither defendant's counsel, the State, nor the trial court brought up the issue of whether defendant was restorable after nine years of unsuccessful incompetent-to-stand-trial commitment, that determination was to be made on remand.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was vacated and the case was remanded to that court to affirm the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the charges and remand the case to the trial court to make a required restorability determination.

Tinsley v. Wash. Metro. Area Transit Auth.


No. 1, No. 25, September Term, 2012


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


429 Md. 217; 55 A.3d 663; 2012 Md. LEXIS 684



October 26, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Maureen M. Lamasney, JUDGE.
Wash. Metro. Area Transit Auth. v. Tinsley, 202 Md. App. 115, 32 A.3d 75, 2011 Md. App. LEXIS 156 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IN CASE NO. 1 AFFIRMED; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER. JUDGMENT NOTWITHSTANDING THE VERDICT GRANTED BY THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY IN CASE NO. 25 AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two cases, petitioners customers sued respondent Washington Metropolitan Area Transit Authority (WMATA) for personal injuries. In one case, the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed the trial court's judgment for the customer. In the other case, the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) granted WMATA's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. Both customers appealed.


OVERVIEW: A customer fell on a subway station floor after it was cleaned, and another customer fell on such a floor where water accumulated. The court of appeals held WMATA was immune, under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 10-204(80) (2008), because (1) the claims contested how maintenance functions were done, but showed no violation of a mandatory directive, as they involved discretionary decisions about when to clean the floors, based on economic and policy considerations balancing ensuring safe conditions against not impeding pedestrian traffic, creating a cleaning schedule against WMATA's budget, and the most efficient maintenance methods, and (2) the controlling inquiry was whether a decision was inherently expected to be based on policy considerations. WMATA did not waive immunity in Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 10-204(75) (2008), requiring it to follow laws of signatories to the WMATA Compact, Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 10-201 et seq., because it had to comply with laws regulating use of streets, highways, other vehicular facilities, and laws regulating traffic control, zoning, signs, and buildings, but did not have to comply with laws governing the use of buildings, signs, or zoning laws.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the Court of Special Appeals and the trial court were affirmed.

Hodge v. Wash. Metro. Area Transit Auth.


No. 1, September Term, 2012, No. 25, September Term, 2012


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


2012 Md. LEXIS 747



October 26, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Leo E. Green, Jr., JUDGE.
Hodge v. Wash. Metro. Area Transit Auth., 426 Md. 430, 44 A.3d 423, 2012 Md. LEXIS 326 (2012)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IN CASE NO. 1 AFFIRMED; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER. JUDGMENT NOTWITHSTANDING THE VERDICT GRANTED BY THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY IN CASE NO. 25 AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, two pedestrians and a spouse, filed slip and fall actions against the Washington Metropolitan Area Transit Authority (WMATA). In the first case, a jury returned a verdict for petitioners; in the second, the Prince County, Maryland, Circuit Court granted WMATA judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The Maryland Court of Special Appeals reversed the judgment in the first case, ruling that WMATA had immunity. Petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both pedestrians slipped and fell on water on the floor of WMATA's metro-rail stations. The high court held that WMATA's decision in the first case to clean the entire station floor, and in the second, to allow water to evaporate instead of mopping it up, were based on policy and economic decisions related to the most efficient method for conducting maintenance operations. Therefore, pursuant to § 80 (Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 10-204(80)) of the WMATA Compact, WMATA had immunity because its determinations were based on economic and policy considerations. Section 75 (Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 10-204(75) (2008)) of the WMATA Compact required WMATA to comply with the laws regulating the use of streets, highways, and all other vehicular facilities, as well as the laws regulating traffic control, zoning, signs, and buildings. It did not require WMATA to comply with laws governing the use of buildings, the use of signs, or the use of zoning laws. Accordingly, § 75 did not act to waive WMATA's immunity in the second case.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court in the second case and of the intermediate appellate court in the first case were affirmed.

Atkinson v. Anne Arundel County


No. 111, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


428 Md. 723; 53 A.3d 1184; 2012 Md. LEXIS 615; 194 L.R.R.M. 2561



September 28, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Case No. C-11-160504, Paul G. Goetzke, JUDGE.
Atkinson v. Anne Arundel County, 424 Md. 291, 35 A.3d 488, 2012 Md. LEXIS 19 (2012)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED FOR THE ENTRY OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH THE OPINION OF THIS COURT. COSTS TO BE PAID BY ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY, MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, county employees and their unions, sought a declaratory judgment in the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) that respondent county's ordinance violated a charter amendment. The county counterclaimed for a declaratory judgment that, if the ordinance violated the charter, a charter amendment violated Md. Const. art. XI-A, § 3. The trial court held the charter provision unconstitutional, and petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: After county voters, in Anne Arundel County, Md., Charter § 812, directed implementation of binding arbitration to resolve labor disputes with certain county employees, the county council amended the implementing ordinance, Anne Arundel County, Md., Code § 6-4-111, to provide (1) council did not have to appropriate funds to implement an award and, (2) if part of the amendment were held invalid, the entire ordinance was invalid. The court of appeals held the charter provision was not unconstitutional, under Md. Const. art. XI-A, § 3, because it simply required the council to implement an award in the next year's budget. The charter provision did not violate Md. Const. art. XI-A by including an entire statute in the charter because it left fleshing out of its directive to the county council. The voters' directive to implement binding arbitration in the budget process was not unconstitutional, under Md. Const. art. XI-A, § 3, because it did not implicate the council's law-making power. The amendment's attempted repeal of the implementing ordinance was invalid because it violated Anne Arundel County, Md., Charter § 812, mandating an ordinance adopting binding arbitration.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for the entry of a declaratory judgment that the charter provision was not unconstitutional and that an ordinance rendering the provision non-binding or repealing its implementing ordinance was invalid.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. McMillan


No. 60, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


428 Md. 560; 53 A.3d 340; 2012 Md. LEXIS 607



September 24, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Cecil County. Case No. 07-C-09-000467. Dexter M. Thompson, Jr., JUDGE
MVA v. McMillan, 415 Md. 114, 999 A.2d 179, 2010 Md. LEXIS 315 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CECIL COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Motor Vehicle Administration (MVA) appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Cecil County (Maryland), which reversed a decision of an administrative law judge (ALJ). The ALJ had found that a driver had refused to take a breath test under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1, and she imposed mandatory driver's license suspensions.


OVERVIEW: The driver's vehicle was stopped for speeding and due to his appearance and failure on a field sobriety test, he was arrested. He agreed to submit to an alcohol concentration test but did not produce a reading despite seven attempts to blow into the Intoximeter. A hearing was held before the ALJ, who determined that the test technician (TT) established a prima facie case of refusal under § 16-205.1, and that the driver did not testify to any medical problems that might have affected the test. She found the TT more credible than the driver, and concluded that he had refused to take the test. The trial court reversed the ALJ's determination, finding that there was insufficient evidence of test refusal. On further review, the court found a lack of substantial evidence under Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-222(h) (1957, 2009) to support the trial court's decision. It held that the TT's certification of the driver's refusal, together with evidence that the testing procedure had been explained to him and that the driver appeared to be in good health, established prima facie proof of a refusal. The driver failed to overcome the refusal presumption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter with instructions to affirm the decision of the ALJ.

Corbin v. State


No. 48, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


428 Md. 488; 52 A.3d 946; 2012 Md. LEXIS 476



August 22, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Somerset County. Case No. 19-K-04-007569), Daniel M. Long, JUDGE.
Corbin v. State, 420 Md. 463, 23 A.3d 895, 2011 Md. LEXIS 486 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. PETITIONER TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress DNA evidence, defendant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. Defendant's petition for certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of his motion to suppress, claiming that, as a DWI probationer who had previously declined police requests to seize and test his DNA, he did not voluntarily surrender his breath for DNA testing when state officers seized his DNA on the false pretense of testing only his blood alcohol. The court of appeals held that defendant, as person on probation from a drunken driving offense, had a significantly diminished expectation of privacy, even when the new crime under investigation for was not related to the one that led to probation. Defendant forfeited much of his right to privacy, if only for a limited time, by accepting probation for his earlier sentence. It was a key factor that defendant's DNA was collected during his regular, probation-mandated testing for alcohol abuse. Defendant also challenged the sufficiency of the evidence against him. The court of appeals found sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction, noting that defendant's semen was found inside the victim's vagina and anus, permitting an inference he was the last one to have sex with her, she remained in a supine position after he violated her, and thus, he killed her.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed.
