Sumpter v. Sumpter


No. 120, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


427 Md. 668; 50 A.3d 1098; 2012 Md. LEXIS 465



August 21, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by, Decision reached on appeal by Sumpter v. Sumpter, 436 Md. 74, 80 A.3d 1045, 2013 Md. LEXIS 906 (Md., Dec. 9, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Case No. 24-D-10-000898.
Sumpter v. Sumpter, 424 Md. 629, 37 A.3d 317, 2012 Md. LEXIS 97 (2012)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT NEITHER AFFIRMED NOR REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO ABIDE THE RESULT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee father filed for an absolute divorce from appellant mother, and the trial court awarded custody of the parties' children to the father over the mother's objection that the parties were not allowed adequate access to a custody evaluation. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed, and the mother sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The mother said the parties were told, one week before a custody hearing, that a custody evaluation (1) could be viewed at the court clerk's office, and (2) could not be copied. The court of appeals held this policy's viability could not be conclusively determined, requiring remand, because (1) the record did not show its full contours, how it was applied, or when and why it was enacted, and (2) the mother's appeals were unopposed, and no potentially interested person moved to participate as amicus curiae. The policy's lack of justification was significant because (1) the report was a "case record," under Md. R. 16-1001(c)(1)(A) and (e)(3), so Md. R. 16-1009(d)(2) required certain findings before limiting access to it, and (2) the record showed no balancing of interests, whether less restrictive alternatives were considered, or any reasons to bar counsel from receiving a copy of it. The policy impeded counsel's ability to know the evidence and contest it because counsel (1) could access the report pre-hearing only in the clerk's office during public hours, (2) could not make verbatim notes of extensive passages from it, and (3) could not make or receive copies of any part of it.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was neither affirmed nor reversed, and the case was remanded to that court with instructions to remand the case to the trial court for further proceedings for supplementation of the record.

 

74 of 744 DOCUMENTS



Shepherd v. Burson


No. 110, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


427 Md. 541; 50 A.3d 567; 2012 Md. LEXIS 461



August 20, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Thomas P. Smith, JUDGE.
Shepherd v. Burson, 424 Md. 291, 35 A.3d 488, 2012 Md. LEXIS 25 (2012)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY IS AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee lender filed a foreclosure action in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) against appellant borrower. The trial court denied the borrower's motion to dismiss the action, a foreclosure sale was held and ratified, and the borrower appealed.


OVERVIEW: The borrower said dismissal was required because the lender's Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 7-105.1(c) notice of intent to foreclose did not state all secured parties. The court of appeals held, in general, the notice should list all secured parties because the statutory purpose to give a borrower advance notice and information to negotiate an alternative to foreclosure was best served by identifying all secured parties, particularly any sharing in the proceeds of a foreclosure sale. Under the facts, the notice's failure to disclose a secured party did not require dismissal because the borrower was not deceived or otherwise treated unfairly, as (1) advance warning of foreclosure proceedings was given over four months before the foreclosure action was filed, (2) the notice let her seek loan modification, (3) the undisclosed secured party's loan ownership was disclosed nearly 18 months before the foreclosure sale, and she did not move to dismiss due to this party's absence from the notice of intent to foreclose for over a year after disclosure of its loan ownership, and (4) Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 7-105.1(c) was ambiguous on whether disclosure of this secured party was required.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.


 

75 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Greco v. State


No. 86, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


427 Md. 477; 48 A.3d 816; 2012 Md. LEXIS 384



June 26, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 29, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Case No. 03-K-81-074022.
State v. Greco, 199 Md. App. 646, 24 A.3d 135, 2011 Md. App. LEXIS 90 (2011)



DISPOSITION: SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT OF BALTIMORE COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. TWO-THIRDS OF THE COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE FULL COSTS IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the trial court granted defendant postconviction relief by vacating his first degree premeditated murder conviction and leaving his convictions for felony murder and first degree rape in place, the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed and reinstated the first degree murder conviction, defendant and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said the Court of Special Appeals could not hear the State's appeal because it did not appeal an order providing relief. The court of appeals disagreed because a later order only clarified the order the State appealed. Excluding mental impairment evidence did not entitle him to postconviction relief because (1) a case used to exclude the evidence did not bar all such evidence, so later cases admitting such evidence established no new "rule," under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 7-106(c)(2)(i) (2008), and, (2) he did not show the earlier case prejudiced him in a way the later cases would have ameliorated, under Md. R. 4-402(a)(3) and (4). His first-degree murder sentence of life, suspend all but 50 years, converted by operation of law into a 50-year term-of-years sentence, was illegal because the minimum sentence was life imprisonment. The trial court had to impose life imprisonment, all but 50 years suspended, followed by probation, because it was limited by the maximum legal sentence that could have been imposed. His 50-year rape sentence was not illegal for exceeding his life expectancy because it ended at the end of his life.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was affirmed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Lipella


No. 80, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


427 Md. 455; 48 A.3d 803; 2012 Md. LEXIS 377



June 25, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 26, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Washington County. Case No. 21-C-09-36042AA, Daniel P. Dwyer, JUDGE.
Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Lipella, 415 Md. 607, 4 A.3d 512, 2010 Md. LEXIS 549 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WASHINGTON COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent driver sought judicial review in the Circuit Court for Washington County (Maryland) of the suspension of his driver's license, under Md. Code Ann., § 16-205.1(b)(1)(i)(2)(A) (2009). The trial court reversed the suspension, finding a form DR-15A stated insufficient grounds for stopping the driver's vehicle, and petitioner Motor Vehicle Administration sought further review, under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-305 (2006).


OVERVIEW: An administrative law judge (ALJ) suspended the driver's license because a DR-15A form stating why an officer suspected intoxicated driving and an official blood alcohol test constituted a prima facie case. The court of appeals held it was error to reverse that decision when the DR-15A form did not state why the driver was stopped because (1) the form and blood test were prima facie evidence of a violation of Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1 (2009), and (2) the form, based on the statute, only required the officer to state why he reasonably believed the driver was intoxicated, which he sufficiently did. An alcohol influence report was admissible at an administrative hearing as corroborative evidence, under Md. Code Regs. 11.11.02.10(A) (2012), because it (1) was a probative document used in conducting a reasonable police officer's duties, and (2) made it more likely the officer reasonably believed the driver drove while intoxicated. The ALJ could rely on this belief because the driver did not show the officer's bad faith by (1) seeking a subpoena for the officer or (2) presenting other evidence of bad faith.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to that court with instructions to affirm the decision of the administrative law judge.

Burruss v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 99, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


427 Md. 231; 46 A.3d 1182; 2012 Md. LEXIS 380



June 25, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Frederick County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, John H. Tisdale, JUDGE.
Burruss v. Bd. of County Comm'rs, 424 Md. 54, 33 A.3d 981, 2011 Md. LEXIS 852 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY IS AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners prospective charter board members sued respondents, a board of county commissioners, a county board of elections (board), and a county election director, in the Circuit Court for Frederick County (Maryland), under Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-209 (2010), to declare the board incorrectly invalidated charter board nominating petition signatures. The trial court judge affirmed the board's decision, and the members appealed.


OVERVIEW: The members said a "sufficient cumulative information" standard applied to find if enough petition signatures were submitted. The court of appeals disagreed because (1) the requirements of Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-203(a) (2010) were mandatory, and (2) no "sufficient cumulative information" standard had been adopted. This standard did not bind respondents under the offensive non-mutual collateral estoppel doctrine because (1) Maryland did not recognize the doctrine, (2) a judgment applying the standard was inconsistent with precedent, and (3) it was unfair to bind respondents to this incorrect judgment. Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-203(a) (2010) and Md. Code Regs. 33.06.03.06(B)(1) did not violate Md. Const. Decl. Rights arts. 7 and 24 because (1) a rational basis test applied, given a minimal burden on voters, and (2) they were reasonable, nondiscriminatory measures designed to prevent fraud and identify petition signers. They did not violate Md. Const. art. XI-A, §§ 1A and 7 because their requirements (1) reasonably furthered Md. Const. art. XI-A, § 7's purposes to prevent fraud, and (2) were not inconsistent with the language or spirit of Md. Const. art. XI-A, §§ 1A and 7.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Unger v. State


No. 111, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


427 Md. 383; 48 A.3d 242; 2012 Md. LEXIS 295



May 24, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Washington County), Donald E. Beachley, JUDGE.
Unger v. State, 411 Md. 355, 983 A.2d 431, 2009 Md. LEXIS 1086 (2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] MOTION TO DISMISS DENIED. JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WASHINGTON COUNTY. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition under the Maryland Uniform Postconviction Procedure Act, Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 7-101 et seq. The postconviction court vacated the inmate's convictions and granted him a new trial. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) granted the State's application for leave to appeal and vacated the postconviction court's order. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of certiorari. The State filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The State claimed that the court of special appeals' denial of the inmate's application for leave to appeal brought the case within Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-202 (1) (1974, 2006 Repl. Vol.). The court of appeals disagreed, noting that the inmate's cross-application for leave to appeal was improper and, even if such an application were necessary, the judgment of the court of special appeals would not come within the ambit of § 12-202. As for the merits of the issue before it, the court of appeals held that the trial court's instructions at the inmate's trial, telling the jury that all of the court's instructions on legal matters were "merely advisory," were clearly in error, at least as applied to matters implicating federal constitutional rights. The opinions in Stevenson v. State, 289 Md. 167, 423 A.2d 558 (1980) and Montgomery v. State, 292 Md. 84, 89, 437 A.2d 654, 657 (1981) set forth a new interpretation of Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 23, and established a new constitutional standard. Thus, counsel's failure to object to the advisory nature of the judge's instructions did not amount to deficient representation at the time of the inmate's trial.


OUTCOME: The State's motion to dismiss was denied. The judgment of the court of special appeals was reversed. The case was remanded to the court of special appeals with instructions to affirm the judgment of the postconviction court.

Mulligan v. Corbett


No. 43, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


426 Md. 670; 45 A.3d 243; 2012 Md. LEXIS 292



May 23, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Corbett v. Mulligan, 198 Md. App. 38, 16 A.3d 233, 2011 Md. App. LEXIS 32 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent putative father filed a complaint for paternity, child support, and visitation. Petitioner mother moved to dismiss for failure to state a claim. The trial court denied the request for paternity testing and ordered that the mother's former husband was the legal father. The putative father appealed. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed and remanded the case. The Court of Appeals of Maryland granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The child at issue was conceived after the mother and her husband separated but before they were divorced, during a time when the mother and the putative father were engaged in a sexual relationship, and was born after the mother and the husband were divorced. At the time the child was born, the mother and the putative father were no longer in a relationship and the husband informed the mother that he wanted to be the baby's father and he took on that role. The issue before the court of appeals was whether a man who claimed to be the father of a child conceived while the mother was married to another man, but born after the mother and her husband divorced, had an unconditional right to genetic testing to determine whether he is the biological father. The court of appeals held that, under the facts given, the trial court did not err or abuse its discretion by considering the best interests of the child when rejecting the requested blood testing. Merely claiming to be the father did not overcome the presumption of legitimacy based on the time of conception.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was vacated and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Forster v. Office of Pub. Defender


No. 92, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


426 Md. 565; 45 A.3d 180; 2012 Md. LEXIS 289; 34 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 282



May 22, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Case No. 24-C-005942.
Forster v. Office of Pub. Defender, 424 Md. 54, 33 A.3d 981, 2011 Md. LEXIS 859 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee filed a wrongful discharge action against appellee State. The Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) granted the State's motion to dismiss the complaint. The employee appealed to the Court of Special Appeals. The Court of Appeals of Maryland issued a writ of certiorari on its own initiative.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the employee, who was terminated as Maryland's State Public Defender, maintained that the trial court erroneously granted the State's motion to dismiss because, under its jurisprudence regarding wrongful discharge, the employee pleaded properly the elements of that cause of action, including that the Board of Trustees's demands of her for action were ultra vires and illegal. The court of appeals concluded that the employee's complaint was barred by the doctrine of administrative exhaustion. The employee failed to exhaust the available and primary administrative remedy provided to at-will executive service State employees under Md. Code Ann., State Pers. & Pens. § 11-305 (1994, 2009 Repl. Vol.). Contrary to the employee's claim, the State was not required to provide the employee with written notice of the availability of the administrative remedy. In addition, the employee's argument that her termination was illegal and unconstitutional was asserted too late and in the wrong forum.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


426 Md. 541; 45 A.3d 166; 2012 Md. LEXIS 290



May 22, 2012, Filed

Circuit Court for Howard County. Case No. 13-K-08-048572.
Bazzle v. State, 423 Md. 450, 31 A.3d 919, 2011 Md. LEXIS 789 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted second-degree murder, attempted armed carjacking, and first-degree assault, after his request for an instruction on voluntary intoxication was denied. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed, and defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said it was error to deny his voluntary intoxication instruction request. The court of appeals held it was not an abuse of discretion to deny the request because (1) evidence of his alcohol consumption, blood alcohol content, memory loss, testimony that he was "almost about to pass out," and the illogical way his crime was committed did not let a jury rationally conclude he was so severely impaired that he could not form the intent necessary to constitute his crimes, as evidence he was drunk was not also evidence he was unable to form the required specific intent, and (2) some of his actions on the night in question were inconsistent with an intoxication defense, including an ability to speak intelligibly, his design in planning the crimes, and his incomplete memory loss. His objection to testimony of an identifying witness's level of certainty was not preserved for review, under Md. R. 5-103(a) or 4-323, because (1) the trial court gave him a chance to provide specific grounds for the objection, stating the objection would be overruled without them and giving him notice the objection would not be preserved without them, and (2) he declined to offer such grounds.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Md. State Bd. of Elections v. Libertarian Party


No. 79, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


426 Md. 488; 44 A.3d 1002; 2012 Md. LEXIS 287



May 21, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Md. Bd. of Elections v. Libertarian Party, 422 Md. 353, 30 A.3d 193, 2011 Md. LEXIS 703 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY IS VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR ENTRY OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee political parties sought a declaratory judgment that appellant State Board of Elections incorrectly applied Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-203 (2002, 2010 Repl. Vol.) regarding validation of petition signatures necessary to regain their ballot access privileges. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) granted the political parties' motion for summary judgment. The State Board of Elections appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 4-102, the political parties enjoyed ballot access privileges for nearly four years when they were unable to show that their respective memberships consisted of at least one percent of registered Maryland voters or that their nominees for Governor received at least one percent of the total vote. Thus, the political parties undertook to obtain 10,000 petition signatures to regain their ballot access privileges. The State Board of Elections found that many of their submitted signatures were invalid under Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-203. The trial court adopted a sufficient cumulative information standard from which a petition signatory could be identified as a registered voter. However, the trial court misconstrued applicable case law in establishing the new standard; rather, the requirements for petition signatures under § 6-203(a) were mandatory and applied to petitions in both the referendum and new party petition contexts. Lastly, in accordance with the plain and unambiguous language of § 6-203(b), the State Board of Elections appropriately refused to validate and count duplicate signatures of individuals who previously signed the same petition.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court for entry of a declaratory judgment consistent with its opinion.

Davis v. State


No. 59, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


426 Md. 211; 43 A.3d 1044; 2012 Md. LEXIS 263



May 2, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Case No. 114288C.
Davis v. State, 199 Md. App. 273, 21 A.3d 181, 2011 Md. App. LEXIS 72 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, defendant was convicted of possession marijuana with an intent to distribute it, in violation of Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 5-602(2) (1957, 2002). Defendant appealed. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. Defendants' petition for a writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to an ex parte order allowing officers to intercept a mobile phone communication, officers intercepted a call leading to the seizure of controlled substances from defendant. The issue before the court of appeals was whether the court of special appeals erred in affirming the denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized after the police intercepted defendant's phone call from his Virginia phone to a Virginia phone line, in violation of the Maryland Wiretapping and Electronic Surveillance Act, Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 10-401 et seq. The court of appeals concluded that the interception of a wire, oral, or electronic communication, for the purposes of the Maryland wiretap statute, occurs where law enforcement officers capture or redirect first the contents of the communication overheard by the wiretap and where they heard originally the communication. Therefore, since the "listening post" was located within the territorial jurisdiction of the court issuing the ex parte wiretap order, neither the physical location of the mobile phone at the time the call was placed and during the communication or the recipient of the call were material.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed.

120 W. Fayette St., LLLP v. Mayor of Baltimore


No. 81, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


426 Md. 14; 43 A.3d 355; 2012 Md. LEXIS 255



April 27, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 10, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, John Philip Miller, JUDGE.
120 W. Fayette St., LLLP v. Mayor of Baltimore, 2011 Md. Cir. Ct. LEXIS 24 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought a declaration of rights interpreting a Memorandum of Agreement (MOA) and declaring a letter from appellee Trust's Director to be ultra vires, ab initio. The property owner appealed the dismissal of its complaint by the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) basedon arguments by appellee city, the Trust, and others, that it was not a party to, or an intended beneficiary of, the MOA.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an Urban Renewal Plan. The MOA required the city to submit redevelopment plans to the Trust for review and approval. The Trust's Director and the State Historic Preservation Officer, provided conditional approval of the fifth set of plans. The city agreed to those conditions. The Trust decided not to challenge the conditional approval. The appellate court held that the property owner's current argument was not the same as its claims at issue in two earlier cases. The MOA was not a land use decision with attendant principles extending standing to nearby aggrieved landowners. Thus, the property owner could not rely on the principles that extended standing to an adjoining landowner. It was left only with principles of contract law to establish its entitlement to press a claim for declaratory relief. Therefore, the trial court properly applied principles of contract law. As the property owner was not a party to the MOA and it did not claim a direct right to compensation from the MOA, it was, at best an incidental beneficiary to the MOA. Hence, it could not file a suit requesting declaratory judgment that interprets and enforces an agreement to which it has no part.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Tracey v. Solesky


No. 53, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


427 Md. 627; 50 A.3d 1075; 2012 Md. LEXIS 253



April 26, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 8, 2012.
Amended by, On reconsideration by, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Tracey v. Solesky, 427 Md. 664, 50 A.3d 1075, 2012 Md. LEXIS 467 (Md., Aug. 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County), Timothy J. Martin, JUDGE.
Solesky v. Tracey, 198 Md. App. 292, 17 A.3d 718, 2011 Md. App. LEXIS 47 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED FOR THE REASONS HEREIN STATED; THAT COURT IS DIRECTED TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE TRIAL COURT FOR A RETRIAL CONSISTENT WITH THE NEW COMMON LAW PRINCIPLES HEREIN ADOPTED; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, a minor's parents, sued appellant landlord in the trial court for the minor's injuries due to an attack by a pit bull owned by the landlord's tenant. The trial court granted judgment for the landlord, but the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed. The landlord appealed, and the parents cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held the evidence was insufficient, under then applicable common law, to present the issue of negligence to a jury, but the Court of Special Appeals held the evidence was sufficient. The court of appeals held a retrial was necessary because (1) the applicable common law was modified to provide that the landlord could be held strictly liable for the injuries if it were proved that the landlord knew or should have known that the dog was a pit bull or a pit bull mix, and (2) this modification applied to the parents' suit, as well as to all future such suits. It was necessary to modify the common law because extensive evidence showed pit bull dogs and cross-bred pit bull dog mixes were responsible for a disproportionate number of serious and often fatal attacks on humans.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was affirmed, and the case was remanded to that court with directions to remand the case to the trial court for a retrial.

King v. State


No. 68, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


425 Md. 550; 42 A.3d 549; 2012 Md. LEXIS 211



April 24, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 2, 2012. As Corrected July 10, 2012.
Stay granted by Maryland v. King, 133 S. Ct. 1, 183 L. Ed. 2d 667, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 5018 (U.S., 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by Maryland v. King, 133 S. Ct. 594, 184 L. Ed. 2d 390, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 8698 (U.S., 2012)
Reversed by Md. v. King, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 4165 (U.S., June 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Case No. 22-K-09-000807, Kathleen L. Beckstead, JUDGE.
King v. State, 422 Md. 353, 30 A.3d 193, 2011 Md. LEXIS 697 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WICOMICO COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE STATE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland) of first-degree rape after his motion to suppress DNA evidence seized from him pursuant to the Maryland DNA Collection Act (Act), Md. Code Ann., Pub. Safety § 2-501 et seq., was denied. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: DNA evidence was involuntarily seized from defendant, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Pub. Safety § 2-504(a)(3) (2011), after his arrest, but before his conviction, on assault charges, and it was used to convict him of the rape. The court of appeals held the statute was unconstitutional, under the Fourth Amendment, as applied to defendant because, given his status as an arrestee entitled to a presumption of innocence, his reasonable expectation of privacy against warrantless, suspicionless searches outweighed the State's interest in assuring his proper identification, since (1) other valid means of identifying him were available, (2) he did not attempt to conceal or alter his identity, and (3) he did not abandon the DNA evidence. Defendant's facial challenge to the statute failed because there were conceivable scenarios where the use of DNA evidence would be needed to identify an arrestee who tried to conceal his or her identity. A subsequent DNA sample obtained from defendant was suppressible as fruit of the poisonous tree because the first sample was used to show probable cause to obtain an order for the second sample.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to that court for a new trial.

 

87 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 76, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


425 Md. 292; 40 A.3d 428; 2012 Md. LEXIS 147



March 21, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Carroll County, Case No. 06-K-09-38696), J. Barry Hughes, JUDGE.
Smith v. State, 422 Md. 353, 30 A.3d 193, 2011 Md. LEXIS 709 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of driving without a license. Defendant appealed. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. Defendant's petition for certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court of appeals was whether the State was required to prove all three parts of Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-101(a) (1977, 2008 Repl. Vol.), as elements of the offense of driving without a license. Defendant argued that the State was required to prove, beyond a reasonable doubt, that (1) he did not have a Maryland driver's license; (2) he was not expressly exempt from the licensing requirements; and (3) he was not specifically authorized to drive vehicles of the class that he was driving. The State countered that the offense was defined by § 16-101(a)(1), and the subsequent exceptions had be raised by defendant as affirmative defenses. The court of appeals held that § 16-101(a)(1) defined the offense, and § 16-101(a)(2) and (a)(3) were not so incorporated into the offense as to constitute part of it. The exceptions outlined in the latter two parts were affirmative defenses that a defendant must raise. Because defendant railed to raise those affirmative defenses and the State's evidence was sufficient to support his conviction, defendant was not entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed.

 

88 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Grandison v. State


No. 117, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


425 Md. 34; 38 A.3d 352; 2012 Md. LEXIS 78



February 22, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Grandison v. Md., 2013 U.S. LEXIS 567 (U.S., Jan. 7, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Death Penalty Appeal (Circuit Court for Somerset County, Case No. 4010), Daniel M. Long, JUDGE.
Grandison v. State, 390 Md. 412, 889 A.2d 366, 2005 Md. LEXIS 748 (2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SOMERSET COUNTY AFFIRMED. APPELLANT TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland) dismissed an inmate's motions to reopen postconviction proceedings; to correct an illegal sentence; for a new resentencing hearing or, alternatively, to file a belated appeal; and for a new trial. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to the inmate's various claims, the court of appeals held, inter alia, that the inmate did not have a right to counsel during his collateral motions and thus, the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the inmate to discharge his attorneys of his own volition. Next, the court of appeals concluded that the inmate's failure to raise a claim of racial discrimination with respect to peremptory strikes in any number of prior proceedings constituted a knowing, intelligent waiver of the issue. Since Crawford was a procedural rule and needed not be applied retroactively, the inmate's challenge to the admission of certain evidence failed. The inmate was not entitled to resentencing or a belated appeal to litigate the admissibility of a latter he wrote, as he made no mention of the challenged letter in his direct appeal and the postconviction court summarily denied his claim relating to that exhibit. The inmate's failure to object to a challenged jury instruction in a timely fashion, combined with his failure to even address the waiver argument before the court of appeals, persuaded the court of appeals to affirm the dismissal of his motion on that question.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

89 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. 37, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


425 Md. 1; 38 A.3d 333; 2012 Md. LEXIS 77



February 22, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County, No,. CAL07-31846), Cathy H. Serrette, JUDGE.
State v. Jones, 197 Md. App. 638, 14 A.3d 1223, 2011 Md. App. LEXIS 28 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT, THE STATE OF MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner alleged injured party (party) sued respondent, the State of Maryland (State), in the trial court for, inter alia, negligent retention, supervision and training of two deputy sheriffs. A jury returned a verdict for the party, and the trial court denied the State's motions for judgment and judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed, and the party sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The deputies forcibly entered the party's home to execute an arrest warrant for a non-resident. The court of appeals held the public duty doctrine did not bar the State's liability because the party alleged harm the officers' acts, not an external force. No expert testimony was required because jury instructions explained the standard established by the Fourth Amendment, so the jury could use its common knowledge to find if a breach occurred. Legally sufficient evidence showed a breach because (1) the governing standard barred entering the home of a third party not named in the arrest warrant, absent consent or exigent circumstances, which were not present, and (2) the deputies' testimony let a jury find they were trained that an arrest warrant let them enter a third party's home listed on an arrest warrant based only on a belief that the arrestee was there, contrary to controlling Fourth Amendment interpretation. The party showed the State's breach proximately caused her injury because the deputies' negligent training was, more likely than not, a substantial factor in producing an altercation leading to her injuries, since it was a foreseeable result of the improper training.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was reversed, and the case was remanded to that Court with directions to affirm the trial court's judgment.

Communications Workers of Am. v. PSC


No. 39, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


424 Md. 418; 36 A.3d 449; 2012 Md. LEXIS 21



January 25, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Evelyn Omega Cannon, JUDGE.
Communs. Workers v. PSC, 420 Md. 463, 23 A.3d 895, 2011 Md. LEXIS 635 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant union sought judicial review in the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) of an order of appellee Public Service Commission (PSC) approving, under Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 4-301 (2008), a settlement adopting an alternative form of regulation (AFOR) for appellee telephone company (company). The trial court affirmed the order, and the union sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The union said the PSC did not meet Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 4-301(b)(1)(ii)'s (2008) goal to ensure service quality because the PSC said the AFOR did not assure such quality. The court of appeals held the PSC's decision was not affected by an error of law because (1) it found the AFOR consistent with the public interest and the statutory standard for AFORs, (2) an AFOR could be goal oriented, so the PSC could set goals without dictating how the company met them, and (3) it was not intended that the PSC be absolutely certain an AFOR would reach its goals. Substantial evidence supported the PSC's order because (1) PSC staff said it was in the public interest and met Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 4-301 (2008), (2) the company's statistics supported it, and (3) the company's expert showed it met objections to a prior proposal. A claim that the PSC misrepresented the union's position was irrelevant because the union's consent was not required. It was no error, under Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 4-301 (2008), to balance the company's interests with those of customers and the state because requiring it to deliver its service at fair price necessitated such balancing.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Carpenter


No. 44, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


424 Md. 401; 36 A.3d 439; 2012 Md. LEXIS 14



January 25, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 3, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Cecil County, Maurice W. Baldwin, Jr., JUDGE.
MVA v. Carpenter, 420 Md. 463, 23 A.3d 895, 2011 Md. LEXIS 457 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CECIL COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An administrative law judge (ALJ) suspended the driver's license of respondent driver for refusal to submit to a chemical breath test. The Circuit Court for Cecil County (Maryland) reversed. Petitioner Motor Vehicle Administration appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court of appeals was whether a police officer's testimony that the driver had been driving a vehicle involved in a collision, based on the officer's post-crash investigation that included witness statements that the detained suspect had been traveling at a high rate of speed and had struck the car, was sufficient to establish reasonable grounds to request an alcohol content test under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(b)(2) (1977, 2009 Repl. Vol.). The court of appeals held that, pursuant to § 16-205.1(b)(2), the ALJ's determination that the police officer had reasonable grounds to detain the driver was supported by substantial evidence and was not premised upon an erroneous conclusion of law. The officer testified that the driver's truck had been involved in a collision, that the driver was present at the scene of the accident, and the driver admitted to traveling between to points after drinking two beers. Thus, it was reasonable to infer that the driver had been driving his truck, which was involved in an accident.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court with directions to affirm the decision of the ALJ.

Stop Slots Md 2008 v. State Bd. of Elections


No. 87, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


424 Md. 163; 34 A.3d 1164; 2012 Md. LEXIS 3



January 6, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Ronald A. Silkworth, JUDGE
Stop Slots MD 2008 v. State Bd. of Elections, 406 Md. 135, 956 A.2d 715, 2008 Md. LEXIS 513 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners filed a complaint challenging a proposed constitutional amendment and related legislation. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) held that the contingent legislation was constitutional and the ballot language summarizing the proposed amendment was sufficient. Petitioners challenged that decision.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners challenged the subject legislation and constitutional amendment, under which video slot machines would be legalized and their revenue would be appropriated and distributed, arguing that the General Assembly improperly delegated its legislative power to Maryland voters and created legislation that was contingent on the passage of the amendment. The Court of Appeals of Maryland found no merit in petitioners' arguments. Among other things, the court of appeals held that the Legislature's decision to accomplish its objective by amending the Maryland Constitution, rather than enact legislation, did not violate any constitutional provision governing its authority to amend the constitution. In addition, the General Assembly did not refer the amendment proposed to votes, but rather placed the matter on the ballot for voter ratification. The Court of Appeals also concluded that the ballot language and prior notice given were sufficient. Voters were provided with reasonable notice of, and access to, the full language of the legislation, and the question posed accurately and unambiguously apprised voters of the true nature of the legislation.


OUTCOME: The ruling of the trial court was affirmed.

 

93 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Md. Ins. Comm'r v. Cent. Acceptance Corp.


No. 7, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


424 Md. 1; 33 A.3d 949; 2011 Md. LEXIS 776



December 20, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). W. Michel Pierson, JUDGE
Md. Ins. Comm'n v. Cent. Acceptance Corp., 418 Md. 586, 16 A.3d 977, 2011 Md. LEXIS 254 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM IN PART AND REVERSE IN PART THE DECISION OF THE MARYLAND INSURANCE COMMISSION, CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY, AND EQUALLY DIVIDED AMONG, RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents premium finance companies (PFCs) sought judicial review of petitioner Maryland Insurance Commissioner's (Commissioner) cease-and-desist order to the PFCs to bar charging interest on loans to pay insurance premiums in excess of the maximum in Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 23-304 (2011). The trial court remanded the matter for a new hearing, and the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. The Commissioner and a PFC sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The lower courts held it was error to delegate the administrative hearing to an associate deputy insurance commissioner (ADIC). The court of appeals disagreed because a "command influence" theory did not apply, and the delegation was proper, as (1) the hearing was not identical to the process leading to the cease-and-desist order (order), (2) the ADIC only decided questions of law, so judicial review would cure any error, (3) nothing showed the ADIC was arbitrary or capricious, (4) Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 2-210(d) (2011) let the Commissioner delegate the hearing to the ADIC, and (5) nothing showed the ADIC participated in the order or that the Commissioner influenced the ADIC. The order was properly issued without rulemaking because it applied existing law. The Commissioner had authority to issue the order because his authority to compel compliance with Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 23-304 was implied from the regulatory scheme. The order met procedural requirements because any noncompliance did not impair the PFCs' substantial rights. The order correctly interpreted Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 23-304 (2011) because it required a finance charge computation meeting plain statutory requirements.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was vacated, and the case was remanded to that court with directions to vacate the trial court's judgment and remand the case to the trial court with directions to affirm the Maryland Insurance Commission's decision in part and to reverse the decision in part.

Freilich v. Upper Chesapeake Health Sys.


No. 4, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


423 Md. 690; 33 A.3d 932; 2011 Md. LEXIS 773; 33 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 910



December 19, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Harford County). Emory A. Plitt. Jr., JUDGE
Freilich v. Upper Chesapeake Health Sys., 418 Md. 586, 16 A.3d 977, 2011 Md. LEXIS 253 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctor sued defendants, a corporation and hospital board members, for breach of contract, misapplication of bylaws, and declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial court granted the defense motion for summary judgment on all counts. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. The doctor's petition for certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The doctor argued that the complaints against her were made in retaliation for her legitimate reporting of substandard medical care and efforts to improve the hospital, but the doctor offered no evidence of retaliatory motive. The court of appeals concluded that the decision declining to renew the doctor's privileges was supported by the evidence. The hospital investigated the doctor's conduct for over two years, holding at least 12 hearings, and the investigation garnered enough evidence to support a reasonable belief that the doctor disrupted hospital caregivers with her unprofessional conduct. Moreover, the doctor provided no evidence that the board did not act in the reasonable belief that the action was in the furtherance of quality health care. Although the doctor alleged retaliation generally, she did not connect it to the board's decision to terminate her privileges. Thus, the doctor failed to produce evidence sufficient to convince a rational trier of fact that the hospital failed to satisfy the standards for immunity in the Health Care Quality Improvement Act of 1986, 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 11101-11152.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed.

Pautsch v. Md. Real Estate Comm'n


No. 9, September Term, 2011


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


423 Md. 229; 31 A.3d 489; 2011 Md. LEXIS 668



October 28, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Pautsch v. Md. Real Estate Comm'n, 418 Md. 587, 16 A.3d 977, 2011 Md. LEXIS 258 (2011)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner real estate broker sought judicial review of the decision of respondent Maryland Real Estate Commission (Commission) to revoke his real estate licenses, under Md. Code Ann., Bus. Occ. & Prof. § 17-322(b)(24)(i) (2004), based on his child abuse convictions. The trial court affirmed the decision, as did the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), and the broker sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The broker said no substantial evidence showed his convictions' nexus to his position as a broker, under Md. Code Ann., Bus. Occ. & Prof. § 17-322(d)(2) (2004), because nothing showed how a lock box system relied on to find his access to unsupervised children worked. The court of appeals held the Commission understood the system because five of its members were real estate professionals. It was no error to find a nexus between his convictions and professional activities because the Commission relied on substantial evidence. Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 1-209 (2009 Supp.), requiring a "direct relationship" between criminal convictions and a revoked occupational license, did not bar revocation because (1) it was not in effect when the licenses were revoked, and a presumption against retroactivity was not rebutted, and (2) it only applied to nonviolent crimes, and the broker's crimes were crimes of violence. Revocation was not arbitrary and capricious because (1) Md. Code Ann., Bus. Occ. & Prof. § 17-322(b)(24)(i) (2004) allowed it, and (2) the broker sexually abused minors for 15 years, showing a lack of responsibility, maturity, and trustworthiness.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was affirmed.

 

96 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Muskin v. State Dep't of Assessments & Taxation


No. 140, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


422 Md. 544; 30 A.3d 962; 2011 Md. LEXIS 644



October 25, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Case No. 24-C-10-004437, pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Stuart R. Berger, JUDGE.
Muskin v. State Dep't of Taxation, 418 Md. 190, 13 A.3d 798, 2011 Md. LEXIS 96 (2011)



DISPOSITION: JUDGEMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO GRANT THE PARTIES' SUMMARY JUDGMENT MOTIONS IN PART AND DENY IN PART, AND ENTER A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT AND INJUNCTIVE RELIEF, ALL AS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner ground lease owner sued respondent State Department of Assessments and Taxation (SDAT) in the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) to declare Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-701 et seq. (2010), unconstitutional and enjoin SDAT from issuing extinguishment certificates. The trial court declared the statute was constitutional. The owner's petition for a writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-701 et seq. (2010) made ground lease owners register their leases, absent which their interests were extinguished and transferred to tenants. The court of appeals held extinguishment and transfer provisions, in Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-708 (2010), violated Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24 because they retrospectively abrogated vested rights, as they (1) retroactively impacted owners' reasonable reliance and settled expectations, since SDAT had to reach back in time to divest the owners' reversionary interests, and (2) removed all remedies and extinguished the interests completely. They violated Md. Const. art. III, § 40 because they took owners' private property without just compensation by transferring the owners' property to tenants without compensation. Registration requirements in Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-704 (2010) were not an unconstitutional regulatory taking because (1) the minimal registration fee, under Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-704(c) (2010), did not interfere unreasonably with the owner's investment-backed expectations, and (2) they appropriately used the state's police power to regulate private property.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to that court with instructions to grant the parties' summary judgment motions in part and deny them in part and enter a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, pursuant to the Court of Appeals' opinion.

Jackson v. Dackman Co.


No. 131, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


422 Md. 357; 30 A.3d 854; 2011 Md. LEXIS 639



October 24, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City), Gale E. Rasin, JUDGE.
Jackson v. Dackman Co., 181 Md. App. 546, 956 A.2d 861, 2008 Md. App. LEXIS 107 (2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENTS AND CROSS-PETITIONERS, THE DACKMAN COMPANY, et. al.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenants filed an action against defendants, the property owners and others, alleging claims for negligence and deceptive practices in violation of the Maryland Consumer Protection Act, Md. Code Ann., Com. Law tit. 13 (2005). The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed. The tenants' petition and defendants' cross-petition for a writ of certiorari were granted.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue before the court concerned the Reduction of Lead Risk in Housing Act, Md. Code Ann., Envir. §§ 6-801 through 6-852 (2011 Supp.), which grants the owners of certain rental properties, under specified conditions, immunity from personal injury suits based upon a child's or pregnant woman's ingestion of lead. Among other things, the Act required the owners to register the properties and renew such registrations by the end of each calendar year. The parties stipulated that, in the instant case, the renewals were mailed by defendants on or before December 31 of each year but were not received until January of each of the following years. On appeal, the tenants argued that the Act's immunity provisions violated Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 19. The court of appeals held that the immunity provisions of the Act were invalid under Article 19. The substituted remedy under the Act for a permanently brain damaged child, being a maximum of $ 17,000, was totally inadequate and unreasonable. The appellate court also concluded that although the immunity provisions of the Act were invalid, they were severable from those remaining portions of the Act, which could be given effect.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with directions to reverse the judgment of the trial court and remand to that court for further proceedings.

Briscoe v. State


No. 4, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


422 Md. 384; 30 A.3d 870; 2011 Md. LEXIS 640



October 24, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City), David Ross, JUDGE.
Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Case No. 107199019, 021.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, a jury convicted defendant of possessing a regulated firearm after having been convicted of a disqualifying crime; wearing, carrying, or transporting a handgun in a vehicle; possessing cocaine; and driving on a suspended license. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. Defendant's petition for writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court of appeals was whether, incident to defendant's arrest, the police searched the locked glove compartment in objectively reasonable reliance on then-binding Maryland appellate precedent. The court of appeals held that the search was not a valid inventory search. Even assuming that the officer's references to a "procedure" sufficed to establish the existence of a sufficiently routinized, general department inventory, the officer's testimony gave no indication that the supposed policy provided standardized criteria governing the search of closed or locked containers and, if so, that the search in this case was done according to that policy. The court of appeals further held that the good-faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied to what, at the time, was a lawful search of the glove compartment, under Belton. The officer acted in objectively reasonable reliance on that authority when he searched the locked glove compartment; thus, the good-faith rule of Davis applied and the suppression court correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress the handgun found there.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed.

 

99 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Frey v. Comptroller of the Treasury


No. 62, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


422 Md. 111; 29 A.3d 475; 2011 Md. LEXIS 626



September 29, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Frey v. Comptroller of Treasury of Md, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 2523 (U.S., Mar. 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (In the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, C-06-115498), Paul A. Hackner, JUDGE.
Frey v. Comptroller of the Treasury, 184 Md. App. 315, 965 A.2d 923, 2009 Md. App. LEXIS 19 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT OF ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AND TO DIRECT THAT COURT TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE TAX COURT TO THE EXTENT IT IS INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE TAX COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. FOUR-FIFTHS OF THE COST OF THIS APPEAL TO BE PAID IN EQUAL SHARES BY THE PETITIONERS/CROSS-RESPONDENTS AND ONE - FIFTH BY RESPONDENT/CROSS-PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners taxpayers sought judicial review of a Tax Court decision upholding respondent Comptroller of the Treasury's (Comptroller) assessment for unpaid Special Nonresident Taxes (SNRT). The trial court upheld the assessment, but held the Tax Court had discretion to waive interest. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed, and both the taxpayers and the Comptroller sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held the SNRT facially discriminated because it did not apply to residents. It met the compensatory tax doctrine because it (1) compensated for services to nonresidents, (2) did not exceed an intrastate burden it compensated for, and (3) taxed income, like county income taxes, and equally taxed Maryland income earners. It did not offend equal protection, under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because it (1) did not tax nonresidents more than residents, and (2) rationally distinguished between the two. It did not offend the privileges and immunities clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, cl. 1, because it (1) did not tax nonresidents more than residents' county income taxes, (2) compensated for local services, (3) was tied to nonresidents' Maryland relationship, and (4) did not cause a "tax war." It did not violate Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24 because it was related to equalizing nonresidents' and residents' taxes. The Tax Court could abate interest, under Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 13-606 (2004), because (1) Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 13-510(a)(1) (2004) allowed appeals of such assessments to it, and (3) Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 13-528 (2004) let it modify the assessments.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was affirmed, and the case was remanded to that court with directions to remand the case to the trial court and direct that court to reverse the Tax Court's judgment finding it could not modify an assessment of interest and to remand the case to the Tax Court for further proceedings.

Bernstein v. State


Misc. No. 1, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


422 Md. 36; 29 A.3d 267; 2011 Md. LEXIS 580; 113 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 781



September 22, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Dismissed by Bernstein v. Maryland, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 122594 (D. Md., Oct. 24, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Bernstein v. Maryland, 674 F. Supp. 2d 703, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 126942 (D. Md., 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] CERTIFIED QUESTIONS ANSWERED AS ABOVE SET FORTH. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY THE APPELLANT AND ONE-HALF BY THE APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sued appellees, the State of Maryland, the Governor, and the General Assembly, in the United States District Court for the District of Maryland, contesting his mandatory retirement. The federal court certified certain questions to the Maryland Court of Appeals.


OVERVIEW: The judge said Md. Const. art. IV, § 3 only required circuit judges turning 70 while in office to retire so that a person 70 or older could be appointed to the office, showing the provision violated equal protection. The court of appeals disagreed because Md. Const. art. IV, § 3 unambiguously and when read in context with the rest of Md. Const. art. IV barred retaining, appointing, or electing a person over 70 as a Maryland circuit judge, as (1) it did not only prescribe a retirement age for sitting judges but referred to an entire category of judges, including all who were, or would seek to become, members of the category, and (2) the eligibility requirements for circuit judges in Md. Const. art. IV, § 5 implied a judicial candidate's age was a qualification for office. If Md. Const. art. IV, § 3, in the context of Md. Const. art. IV, were ambiguous, the judge's construction conflicted with the intent of the Maryland Constitution's framers because (1) that intent was to exclude persons over 70 from judicial office, and (2) the legislature did not change the longstanding practice of not letting judges remain regular members of the bench after age 70.


OUTCOME: The certified questions were answered.

 

101 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Miles v. State


No. 120, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


421 Md. 596; 28 A.3d 667; 2011 Md. LEXIS 570



September 20, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Miles v. Maryland, 132 S. Ct. 1743, 182 L. Ed. 2d 535, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 2153 (U.S., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Death Penalty (Motion to Correct Illegal Sentence) -- Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County. Frederick Price, JUDGE
Miles v. State, 365 Md. 488, 781 A.2d 787, 2001 Md. LEXIS 614 (2001)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] DENIAL OF MOTION TO CORRECT ILLEGAL SENTENCE AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of first-degree felony murder and related offenses, and sentenced defendant to death. The Court of Appeals affirmed defendant convictions and sentence. The United States Supreme Court denied defendant's petition for writ of certiorari. Defendant moved to correct illegal sentence. The Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County (Maryland) denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was entitled to a new sentencing hearing on the ground that the jury should have been instructed that a death sentence could not be imposed unless every juror was persuaded beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances. According to defendant, his sentence became illegal when the United States Supreme Court decided Cunningham, because Cunningham rendered invalid, on Sixth Amendment grounds, every state capital sentencing procedure that did not require the jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances, and the new standard established in Cunningham had to be applied retroactively. The court of appeals found no error, concluding that, even if Cunningham and Ring applied retroactively, defendant was not entitled to a new sentencing hearing. The Maryland statute already required that the finding of aggravating circumstances be made by a jury beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's motion to correct illegal sentence was affirmed.

Furda v. State


No. 100, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


421 Md. 332; 26 A.3d 918; 2011 Md. LEXIS 519



August 17, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 22, 2011
Motion denied by Furda v. Maryland, 132 S. Ct. 1781, 182 L. Ed. 2d 527, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 2311 (U.S., 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Furda v. Maryland, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 3437 (U.S., May 14, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgonery County). Ronald B. Rubin, JUDGE.
Furda v. State, 194 Md. App. 1, 1 A.3d 528, 2010 Md. App. LEXIS 109 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of perjury and false information in a firearm application. In separate appeals, defendant appealed his convictions and an order denying his motion for the return of his weapons. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed the order denying defendant's motion fore return of his weapons but affirmed the convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After responding to a domestic altercation, police seized defendant's weapons and transported him to a hospital for a mental health evaluation. Upon his release, he requested return of his weapons, which a judge denied. On an application to purchase a new firearm, defendant certified, under penalty of perjury, that he had not been committed to a mental institution. The issue before the court of appeals was whether defendant's conviction for perjury and false information in a firearm application could be founded upon his failure to disclose a court order that was later reversed. The court of appeals first noted that the application question asking if defendant had been adjudicated a mental defective or committed to a mental institution was not ambiguous. The court of appeals also concluded that defendant was obligated to answer "yes," despite his ongoing dispute with the order denying his request for a return of his firearms for having been committed to a mental institution. Evidence of defendant's intent to provide false information was shown by the fact that he conferred with counsel and the fun shop on the issue of whether the denial order prevented him for purchasing a firearm.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

103 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Breslin v. Powell


No. 134, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


26 A.3d 878; 2011 Md. LEXIS 518



August 16, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at, Petition granted by Powell v. Breslin, 425 Md. 396, 41 A.3d 571, 2012 Md. LEXIS 240 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City), Case No. 24-C-04-007801, Kaye A. Allison, JUDGE.
Powell v. Breslin, 195 Md. App. 340, 6 A.3d 360, 2010 Md. App. LEXIS 150 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent personal representative sued petitioner physician for medical malpractice. The trial court granted the physician's summary judgment motion, finding the personal representative's certificate of merit (certificate) did not meet Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-2A-02 (2010 Supp.). The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed, holding dismissal without prejudice was the proper remedy. The physician sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The personal representative's certificate's author was unqualified, under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-2A-02 (2010 Supp.). The court of appeals held the proper remedy was dismissal without prejudice, rather than summary judgment, because (1) Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-2A-02 (2010 Supp.) was read together with Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-2A-04 (2010 Supp.), providing for dismissal without prejudice when a certificate of merit did not meet that statute's requirements, (2) the legislature added the qualifications in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-2A-02 (2010 Supp.) knowing Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-2A-04 (2010 Supp.) required dismissal without prejudice for lack of a proper certificate, and (3) the words "in addition to any other qualifications" in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-2A-02(c)(2)(ii) (2010 Supp.) showed a legislative intent to read the two statutes' qualifications together. Dismissal without prejudice supported the legislative purpose because it required a qualified expert while giving a plaintiff a chance to re-file if a qualified expert attested to departures from the standard of care and causation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was affirmed.

Arthur v. State


No. 90, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


420 Md. 512; 24 A.3d 667; 2011 Md. LEXIS 440



July 13, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Frederick County). Julie Stevenson Solt, JUDGE
Arthur v. State, 193 Md. App. 446, 997 A.2d 899, 2010 Md. App. LEXIS 106 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT FOR A NEW TRIAL ON BOTH COUNTS. COSTS DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN PETITIONER AND RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of failure to obey a lawful order and resisting arrest. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. Both sides petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the appellate court's conclusion that there was sufficient evidence to support his convictions. The court of appeals found the issue unpreserved, as neither of his motions for judgment of acquittal were made on the basis argued on appeal. Both parties attacked the court of special appeals' decision regarding defendant's proposed jury instruction. Defendant submitted that the court of special appeals erred by condoning the trial court's failure to instruct the jury as to the long recognized privilege to resist an unlawful arrest, while the State protested the holding that the issue of an unlawful arrest was factually generated. The court of appeals agreed with the court of special appeals that the issue of an unlawful arrest was generated. The court of appeals further concluded that the court of special appeals erred in determining that an instruction on resisting arrest was not necessary. Because the evidence presented at trial generated the issue of whether the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant, the only way for defendant to have a fair trial was for the jury to understand the law concerning his right to resist and unlawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was reversed. The case was remanded to the court of special appeals with directions to vacate the judgment of the trial court and remand the case to that court for a new trial.

Stephens v. State


No. 114, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


420 Md. 495; 24 A.3d 105; 2011 Md. LEXIS 434



July 12, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Case No. K-08-646, Paul A. Hackner, JUDGE.
Stephens v. State, 418 Md. 592, 17 A.3d 143, 2011 Md. LEXIS 206 (2011)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the trial court denied defendant's request for a pre-trial hearing on whether the State could meet its burden under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 2-202(a)(3) (2010 Supp.), the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) denied the State's motion to dismiss defendant's appeal, after which the Court of Appeals granted certiorari, on its own initiative, before argument in the Court of Special Appeals.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said the collateral order doctrine let him immediately appeal the trial court's order. The court of appeals disagreed because the order (1) was not completely separate from the merits of the underlying case, as the evidence the State would have to produce at the hearing defendant sought was intimately tied to whether he was guilty of a charged murder and whether, if convicted, he was subject to the death sentence, and (2) was not effectively unreviewable if appellate review were delayed until after a final judgment, as his right to insist upon the State's compliance with the statute by producing statutorily required evidence was not hindered by awaiting final judgment for appellate review, and, if successful, any death sentence imposed would be vacated, so the justification for an immediate appeal was not strong enough to overcome the usual benefits of deferring an appeal until the case ended.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

106 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Loane


No. 52, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


420 Md. 211; 22 A.3d 833; 2011 Md. LEXIS 373



June 22, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Paul Garvey Goetzke, JUDGE
MVA v. Loane, 415 Md. 40, 997 A.2d 791, 2010 Md. LEXIS 425 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE MOTOR VEHICLE ADMINISTRATION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Motor Vehicle Administration (MVA) appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) which reversed the decision of an administrative law judge (ALJ) to suspend respondent driver's operator's licence. The issue was whether suspension of the driver's license hinged on proof by the MVA at the show cause hearing that the driver was stopped on a highway or private property used by the public.


OVERVIEW: The driver was stopped by a police officer for failing to obey lane directions. The officer detected an odor of alcohol on the driver's breath,. The driver failed to complete sobriety tests or submit to a chemical breath test, as authorized by Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(b)(2). The driver was informed of the resulting administrative sanctions if he refused. A Form DR-15A was submitted which included a pre-printed certification containing a statement that the stop occurred on a highway or private property that was used by the public in general. The ALJ found that the officer had reasonable grounds to detain the driver and suspended his license for 120 days. The trial court reversed the decision of the ALJ. The appellate court held that § 16-205.1 did not preclude suspension if a motorist was detained somewhere other than on a highway or private property used by the public in general. The Statute did not require the MVA to prove at the show cause administrative hearing that the officer stopped the driver on a highway or private property used by the public in general. The ALJ made all the findings required by § 16-205.1(f)(8)(i) before suspending the driver's license to drive.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded with directions to affirm the decision of the MVA.
