County Council of Prince George's County v. Billings


No. 46, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


420 Md. 84; 21 A.3d 1065; 2011 Md. LEXIS 370



June 20, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Case No. CAL-07-32022.
Billings v. County Council, 190 Md. App. 649, 989 A.2d 1170, 2010 Md. App. LEXIS 31 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent citizens sought review of petitioner district council's decision to withdraw its election to review zoning approvals granted to petitioner developer by local agencies. The trial court dismissed the action. On appeal, the Maryland Court of Special Appeals reversed and remanded the matter to the council with directions to resume review of the agency decisions. Petitioner's request for certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought approvals from the local agencies to expand a gas station; the citizens opposed the expansion. After holding hearings, the agencies granted both zoning approvals. The council "elected to review" both zoning decisions, but, before any review proceedings, summarily withdrew its election to review and declared the agency decisions "final." This suit followed. The high court held that the citizens had standing to seek judicial review, petitioners' claim to the contrary notwithstanding, as they were taxpayers of the county and at least one of them participated at each administrative hearing. The citizens exhausted their administrative remedies by appearing and testifying at the agency hearings. Once the council elected to review the decisions, the citizens were not required to file an independent request for review. The council could not summarily withdraw its election to review and finalize the local agency decisions without following the statutory procedure for review set out in the Prince George's County, Md., Code. The council had to justify its decision with written findings and conclusions and follow any other applicable procedural requirements.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

Doe v. Roe


No. 95, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


419 Md. 687; 20 A.3d 787; 2011 Md. LEXIS 303



May 23, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Calvert County). Marjorie L. Clagett, JUDGE
Roe v. Doe, 193 Md. App. 558, 998 A.2d 383, 2010 Md. App. LEXIS 113 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent granddaughter filed a complaint against petitioner grandfather alleging claims for, inter alia, battery, false imprisonment, and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The circuit court dismissed the claims as time-barred. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed. The grandfather filed a timely petition for writ of certiorari, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: Five years after attaining the age of majority, the granddaughter filed a complaint against the grandfather alleging that the grandfather raped the granddaughter on two separate occasions, once when she was six or seven years of age and a second time when she was eight years of age. At the time the granddaughter reached the age of majority the limitations period for the alleged acts was three years. The applicable statute was amended prior to the end of the three-year period to allow for such actions to be brought within seven years of the date the victim, the granddaughter, attained the age of majority. The issue before the court of appeals was whether Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-117 (2006), expressly to extend from three years to seven years the statute of limitations for civil claims stemming from alleged child sexual abuse, applied retroactively. The court of appeals held that § 5-117 was a procedural or remedial statute, and accordingly, it could be given retrospective application to claims that were not yet barred by the previously applicable three-year limitations period as of the extended period's effective date.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed.

Smith v. County Comm'rs


No. 2, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


418 Md. 692; 18 A.3d 16; 2011 Md. LEXIS 213



April 25, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Kent County) J Frederick Price, JUDGE
Smith v. Kent County, 411 Md. 740, 985 A.2d 538, 2009 Md. LEXIS 966 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS THE APPEAL, VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR KENT COUNTY, AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS THAT IT DISMISS PETITIONERS' PETITION FOR JUDICIAL REVIEW; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONERS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner residents sued a county, challenging an amendment to the county's local critical area plan under the regulatory scheme of the Chesapeake and Atlantic Coastal Bays Critical Area Protection Program, Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-1801 et seq. (2007 Repl. Vol.). The trial court affirmed the county's action. Petitioners appealed; the Maryland Court of Special Appeals dismissed the appeal. Petitioners sought a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: To implement the county's approval of a developer's growth allocation application, the county decided to amend its local Critical Area Plan. The county proclaimed that its decision was not effective until approved by the Chesapeake Bay Critical Area Commission. Apparently while consideration of the county's local growth allocation approval was pending before the Commission, petitioners filed their appeal. The trial court affirmed the action of the county; the intermediate appellate court dismissed petitioners' subsequent appeal as premature. The high court held that as the county's growth allocation policy stated that no local approval action was effective until approved by the Commission, and as the Commission, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-1809, might ultimately override the county's decision to approve the growth allocation request, the county's approval of that request was not a final and appealable action. Therefore, the intermediate appellate court properly dismissed petitioners' appeal, but should have also vacated the trial court's judgment on the merits affirming the county's approval of the request.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was vacated. The case was remanded to that court with directions to dismiss the appeal, vacate the judgment of the trial court, and remand the case to the trial court with directions that it dismiss the petition.

Prince George's County v. Longtin


No. 35, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


419 Md. 450; 19 A.3d 859; 2011 Md. LEXIS 214



April 25, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Prince George's County). C.Philip Nichols. Jr. JUDGE
Prince George's County v. Longtin, 190 Md. App. 97, 988 A.2d 20, 2010 Md. App. LEXIS 9 (2010)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AND THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accused sued defendants, a county police department, the county, and individual officers for various state tort and constitutional claims, based on his detention after police had evidence excluding him as a perpetrator. A jury awarded the accused damages of $ 6.2 million, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-303(b)(1) (2006), and the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. Defendants sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendants said the accused gave untimely notice of his claims, under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-304 (2006). The court of appeals disagreed because, (1) as to his false arrest and imprisonment claims, sound policy began the notice period when he was released after being held for trial but not tried, and (2) this resolved the issue for the other claims, as they shared an accrual date for limitations purposes with false arrest and imprisonment or did not accrue until his release. The damages cap in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-303(a)(1) (2006) did not limit the accused's award because retroactively applying a statute to limit the award deprived him of a vested right, contrary to Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24 and Md. Const. art. III, § 40. The accused properly recovered under a claim that the county had a "pattern or practice" of unconstitutional police policies because (1) Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24 protected individuals against municipalities' unconstitutional "patterns or practices," and (2) the accused proved the unconstitutional actions committed against him and that this was not an isolated incident.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court and the Court of Special Appeals were affirmed.

Headen v. Motor Vehicle Admin.


No. 42, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


418 Md. 559; 16 A.3d 196; 2011 Md. LEXIS 151



March 28, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Charles County. Amy J. Bragunier, JUDGE
Headen v. Motor Vehicle Admin., 408 Md. 487, 970 A.2d 892, 2009 Md. LEXIS 699 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CHARLES COUNTY AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISIONS OF THE MOTOR VEHICLE ADMINISTRATION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver sought judicial review in the Circuit Court for Charles County (Maryland) of decisions of respondent Motor Vehicle Administration (MVA) denying (1) the driver a hearing on whether he was precluded from licensure in Maryland and (2) his request for expungement of his driving record. The trial court held he was entitled to a hearing but that he was not entitled to expungement. Both the driver and the MVA sought further review.


OVERVIEW: After granting the driver a "Maryland only" license, due to prior drunk driving convictions in Maryland and Florida, the MVA summarily denied his request to renew the license, and he sought expungement of his driving record. The court of appeals held he was properly denied expungement because, reading Md. Code Ann., Transp. §§ 16-117.1 and 12-111 (2009) together, once the MVA exercised its discretion in Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 12-111 (2009) to classify his convictions as "confidential," the records of the convictions were not subject to expungement under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-117.1 (2009). It was error to order the MVA to provide the driver a hearing to determine if he should be issued a license, even though he had mistakenly been issued a "Maryland only" license, because he was barred, as a matter of law, under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-103.1(1) (2009), from obtaining a Maryland license, as (1) the statute barred the MVA from issuing a license to anyone whose license was revoked in any state, (2) his license was permanently revoked in Florida, due to his drunk driving convictions, and (3) no statutory provision required that he be provided with a hearing.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment directing a remand for an administrative hearing was reversed, and the judgment was otherwise affirmed. The matter was remanded to the trial court with directions to enter an order affirming the summary denial of the driver's application to renew his license.

Najafi v. Motor Vehicle Admin.


No. 44, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


418 Md. 164; 12 A.3d 1255; 2011 Md. LEXIS 20



January 31, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Najafi v. MVA, 415 Md. 38, 997 A.2d 789, 2010 Md. LEXIS 413 (2010)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-222(a) (2009), petitioner driver sought judicial review in the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) of an administrative law judge's (ALJ) decision suspending his driver's license for refusing to submit to a chemical breath test after being detained for driving under the influence of alcohol. The trial court affirmed the ALJ's decision, and the driver's petition for a writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: After an officer asked the driver to submit to a chemical breath test, the driver asked to consult counsel and was allowed to call his attorney, but was unable to reach counsel, after which the officer certified that the driver refused the test. The driver said his right to consult counsel before deciding to submit to the test was violated when he was not given privacy to consult counsel. The court of appeals held due process was satisfied when the driver was advised of possible administrative sanctions by having a chance to read a form advising him of his rights. It was unnecessary to decide if a right to consult counsel before deciding whether to submit to the test applied in the administrative context because the driver had a chance to contact counsel, and no right of privacy applied to his unsuccessful attempt to contact counsel. Substantial evidence supported the ALJ's finding that the driver refused to submit to the test because the ALJ could find the officer's certification that the driver refused the test more credible than the driver's testimony that the officer did not ask him to choose whether to take the test after he unsuccessfully tried to consult counsel.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Aiken


No. 69, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Mary Beth McCormick, JUDGE
MVA v. Aiken, 409 Md. 47, 972 A.2d 861, 2009 Md. LEXIS 544 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE MOTOR VEHICLE ADMINISTRATION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent driver sought judicial review in the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) of the decision of an administrative law judge (ALJ) suspending the driver's license. The trial court reversed the ALJ's decision, and petitioner Motor Vehicle Administration (MVA) filed a petition for a writ of certiorari, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: The driver said her license could not be suspended without evidence that a "qualified person," as defined in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(b)(3)(vii) (2009) to show a prima facie case, and (2) these officers' certifications on a Form DR-15A met these requirements, as they certified the driver's test result showed a blood alcohol concentration of over 0.08 and produced a 0.16 blood alcohol concentration. Language in Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(a)(2) (2009) that the driver consented, subject to Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 10-302 through 10-309 (2009), to the test did not require more to suspend the driver's license because Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(f)(7)(ii) did not require compliance with Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 10-302 through 10-309 (2009).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded to that court with directions to affirm the decision of the Motor Vehicle Administration.

Md. State Bd. of Physicians v. Eist


No. 110, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


417 Md. 545; 11 A.3d 786; 2011 Md. LEXIS 3



January 21, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 17, 2011
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Eist v. Md State Bd. of Physicians, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 6817 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County) Durke G. Thompson, JUDGE
Md. State Bd. of Physicians v. Eist, 176 Md. App. 82, 932 A.2d 783, 2007 Md. App. LEXIS 123 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE MARYLAND STATE BOARD OF PHYSICIANS. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Maryland State Board of Physicians, found respondent doctor violated Md. Code Ann., Health Occ. § 14-404(a)(33) and reprimanded the doctor for failing to comply with a subpoena in a timely manner. In an action under the Maryland Administrative Procedure Act, a circuit court reversed the Board's decision and the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed. The Board's petition for certiorari review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The Board received a complaint against the doctor, a licensed psychiatrist, that he was overmedicating four patients. In response to the complaint, the Board issued a subpoena on April 18, 2001, commanding the doctor to produce a copy of the patients' medical records. Although privacy rights were initially invoked, the records were forwarded on March 20, 2002. The doctor was absolved of the overmedication allegation. Nevertheless, the Board found the doctor failed to cooperate with the investigation. The Board's decision to reprimand the doctor and impose a fine was legally correct because neither the doctor nor the patients took any appropriate action to challenge the subpoena as required by Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. §§ 4-306 and 4-307. As such, the doctor failed to comply with the subpoena in a timely manner and did not cooperate in the investigation. The Board did not have the burden of instituting a judicial action to enforce the subpoena. If the patients and/or the doctor believed there were grounds for not producing the records, the patients or the doctor had to file a motion to quash the subpoena or a motion for a protective order pursuant to Md. R. 2-403 or 2-510.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with directions to reverse the judgment of the circuit court and remand the case to the circuit court with directions to affirm the Board's decision.

 

115 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


No. 16, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


417 Md. 479; 10 A.3d 1167; 2011 Md. LEXIS 1



January 5, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Williams v. Md., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 6615 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County). Sean D. Wallace, JUDGE.
Williams v. State, 188 Md. App. 691, 982 A.2d 1168, 2009 Md. App. LEXIS 169 (2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a handgun, in violation of Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 4-203(a)(1)(i) (2002). The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed, and the Court of Appeals granted certiorari to consider whether Maryland's regulatory scheme for handguns violated the right to "keep and carry arms" under the Second Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said the bar in Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 4-203(a) (2002) against wearing, carrying, or transporting a handgun without a permit and outside of one's home infringed his Second Amendment right "to keep and bear arms" and that Md. Code Ann., Pub. Safety § 5-301 et seq. (2003) and Md. Code Regs. tit. 29, subtit. 3, governing handgun permitting, impermissibly burdened this right. The court of appeals held he had no standing to contest the constitutionality of Md. Code Ann., Pub. Safety § 5-301 et seq. (2003) or Md. Code Regs. tit. 29, subtit. 3 because he did not seek a permit. He was properly convicted because (1) sufficient evidence showed he wore, carried, or transported a handgun in public, (2) he conceded he did not seek a permit, (3) the Second Amendment barred statutory prohibitions against home possession of firearms, and (4) Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 4-203(b)(6) (2002), allowing home possession, took Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 4-203 (2002) outside the scope of the Second Amendment, as it let a person wear, carry, or transport a handgun on real estate the person owned or leased or where the person resided, without registering or obtaining a permit.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Bayly Crossing, LLC v. Consumer Prot. Div.


No. 8, September Term, 2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


417 Md. 128; 9 A.3d 4; 2010 Md. LEXIS 700



November 22, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). John Martin Glynn, JUDGE
Bayly Crossing, LLC v. Consumer Prot. Div., 188 Md. App. 299, 981 A.2d 777, 2009 Md. App. LEXIS 151 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IS REVERSED IN PART AND AFFIRMED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER REMAND TO RESPONDENT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE SHARED EQUALLY BY PETITIONERS (50%) AND RESPONDENT (50%).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners principals sought review of respondent Maryland Consumer Protection Division's (Division) order finding they violated Maryland's (1) Home Builder Registration Act, Md. Code Ann., Bus. Reg. §§ 4.5-101 to 4.5-701 (2007 Supp.), and (2) Consumer Protection Act (CPA), Md. Code Ann., Com. Law §§ 13-101 to 13-501 (2009 Supp.). The trial court and Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed, and the principals sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The principals sought to add their defunct limited liability company as a petitioner after the Court of Special Appeals dismissed it. The Court of Appeals held they did not preserve the issue, under Md. R. 8-131(b)(1), by raising it in their petition for certiorari or in a subsequent motion. Their company did not have to register as a home builder, under Md. Code Ann., Bus. Reg. §§ 4.5-101 to 4.5-701 (Supp. 2007), because, while its contracts agreed to "sell and construct," as well as "complete," new homes, it was clear that the contracts in their entirety specified that actual construction would be done by a registered home builder, so competent, material, and substantial evidence did not support the Division's presumption that the company held itself out as a home builder. The company and the principals violated Md. Code Ann., Com. Law § 13-301(13) (Supp. 2009), by requiring buyers to release the company and principals from consequential damages in exchange for a limited warranty, because, while the releases said nothing about consequential damages, their language was sufficiently expansive to fall within the CPA's clear and unambiguous regulatory prohibition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals finding a violation of the Home Builder Registration Act was reversed, but the judgment finding a CPA violation was affirmed. The matter was remanded to the Court of Special Appeals with directions to reverse the trial court's judgment and remand the case to that court for further remand to the Division for further proceedings.

In re Adoption/Guardianship of Ta'Niya C.


No. 133, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


417 Md. 90; 8 A.3d 745; 2010 Md. LEXIS 702



November 22, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore). Dennis M. McHugh, JUDGE
In re Adoption/Guardianship of Ta'Niya C., 411 Md. 598, 984 A.2d 243, 2009 Md. LEXIS 877 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A department of social services (DSS) filed a petition for guardianship of petitioner child, seeking termination of respondent parent's parental rights. The trial court denied the petition, finding DSS did not show, by clear and convincing evidence, that the parent was unfit or that exceptional circumstances justified termination. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed, and the child sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found a prior Court of Appeals decision changed the law. The court of appeals held this was error because best interest of the child still governed. The trial court's judgment had to be vacated because, after finding no exceptional circumstances justified termination, it gave little, in any, weight to factors in Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-323(d)(4) (Supp. 2009) addressing termination from the point of view of the child's circumstances, focusing on the parent's circumstances, as it did not address the child's emotional ties to the parent, under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-323(d)(4)(i) (Supp. 2009), or the child's feelings about termination, under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-323(d)(4)(iii) (Supp. 2009), and, as to the impact of termination on the child, under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-323(d)(4)(iv) (Supp. 2009), it found the prior decision almost asked the court to ignore that. The court incorrectly found, in noting that another child had been returned to the parent, that a finding of exceptional circumstances was not unique to a particular child because this did not take into account circumstances particular to an individual child.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was reversed, and the matter was remanded to that court with instructions to vacate the trial court's judgment and remand the matter to that court for further proceedings under the correct standard.

Wal Mart Stores, Inc. v. Holmes


No. 141, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


416 Md. 346; 7 A.3d 13; 2010 Md. LEXIS 620



October 25, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Martin P. Welch, JUDGE.
Holmes v. Wal Mart Stores, Inc., 187 Md. App. 690, 979 A.2d 744, 2009 Md. App. LEXIS 142 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY. RESPONDENT TO PAY THE COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent surviving spouse filed a petition for judicial review of Maryland Workers' Compensation Commission's determination that he was ineligible to claim benefits under Md. Code Ann., Lab. & Empl. § 9-632(d) (2008). The circuit court granted petitioner employer's motion for summary judgment and affirmed the order of the Commission. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Court of Special Appeals agreed with the spouse that his deceased wife, who had a claim for workers' compensation benefits, had "a legal obligation to support" him during their marriage On appeal, the employer challenged that court's interpretation of Md. Code Ann., Lab. & Empl. § 9-632. The spouse contended that a "legal obligation to support" a surviving spouse was inherent in the marital relationship and continued until given up, either voluntarily or by court order. The court of appeals held that, for purposes of § 9-632(d), "a legal obligation to support" a surviving spouse did not arise by virtue of the marital tie alone, but arose from a legally enforceable contract, decree, or order from a court of competent jurisdiction. The court of appeals found that at the time of the wife's death, the spouse, under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 10-201 (2006), had no legally enforceable rights and the wife had not corresponding legally enforceable duties. Because the spouse failed to introduce any evidence of the existence of a legal duty to support him on the part of his wife, the wife's right to receive compensation benefits did not pass to the spouse under § 9-632(d).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was reversed. The case was remanded to the Court of Special Appeals with directions to affirm the judgment of the circuit court.

Stachowski v. State


No. 52, September Term, 2008, No. 16, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


416 Md. 276; 6 A.3d 907; 2010 Md. LEXIS 622



October 22, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Stockstill v. State, 424 Md. 630, 37 A.3d 319, 2012 Md. LEXIS 126 (2012)
Later proceeding at Stachowski v. State, 2013 Md. App. LEXIS 90 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Aug. 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
In the Circuit Court for Somerset County. Case No. 19-K-008089; Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Case No. CT80-459.
Stockstill v. State, 404 Md. 659, 948 A.2d 70, 2008 Md. LEXIS 262 (2008)
Stachowski v. State, 405 Md. 348, 952 A.2d 224, 2008 Md. LEXIS 497 (2008)



DISPOSITION: WRITS OF CERTIORARI IN BOTH NUMBERS 16 AND 52 DISMISSED. COSTS TO ABIDE THE RESULT IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court of appeals issued writs of certiorari and directed defendants to file briefs on the issue of whether it had jurisdiction to decide two cases in light of Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-202 (2006). First defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland) on a bad check conviction. Second defendant appealed a revocation of probation order by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland).


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the writs of certiorari should be dismissed for lack of jurisdiction, because Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-202 (2006) was an extremely broad limitation upon the court of appeals' certiorari jurisdiction, covering every case where appellate court of the intermediate appellate court was by application for leave to appeal, and, alternatively, because § 12-202 deprived the court of appeals of jurisdiction where the intermediate appellate court simply denied or granted the application for leave to appeal without resolving or deciding any of the legal or factual merits of the application. The court of appeals rejected the broad limitation argument advanced by the State, noting that it adhered to a long line of cases which essentially supported the State's alternative argument, under which the jurisdictional limitation is narrow.


OUTCOME: The writs of certiorari were dismissed.

DRD Pool Serv. v. Freed


No. 104, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


416 Md. 46; 5 A.3d 45; 2010 Md. LEXIS 530



September 24, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Nancy Davis-Loomis JUDGE
Freed v. D.R.D. Pool Serv., 186 Md. App. 477, 974 A.2d 978, 2009 Md. App. LEXIS 104 (2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. PETITIONER AND CROSS-PETITIONERS TO DIVIDE THE COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS EQUALLY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a survival and wrongful death case, petitioner pool company's motion for summary judgment on the issue of pain and suffering was granted. A $ 4,006,442 jury award was reduced under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 11-108 (2008). The trial court denied the parents' motion to alter or amend judgment. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed the grant of summary judgment and denial of motion to alter or amend. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first issue before the court of appeals was whether a jury could consider a claim for conscious pain and suffering when there was a reasonable inference of consciousness prior to the decedent's death, but the length of that consciousness and evidence of pain and suffering during the drowning process were based on expert testimony rather than on eyewitness testimony. The court of appeals agreed with the parents' argument that once a reasonable inference arose from expert testimony, the jury should decide whether the decedent experienced conscious pain and suffering. While no eyewitnesses saw the decedent drown, the evidence showed that he likely was conscious when entering the water. In addition, expert testimony was presented that, to a medical degree of certainty, the decedent consciously experienced pain and suffering. Thus, the issue should have been presented to the jury. Next, the court of appeals upheld the denial of the parents' motion to alter or amend judgment, finding that the cap in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 11-108 (2008) had been previously upheld as constitutional and affirming that holding under the principle of stare decisis.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed.

Tyler v. City of College Park


No. 126, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


415 Md. 475; 3 A.3d 421; 2010 Md. LEXIS 343



August 25, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Case No. CAE06-23501.
Tyler v. College Park, 411 Md. 599, 984 A.2d 244, 2009 Md. LEXIS 1120 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, landlords and a tenant, sued appellees, the City of College Park, Md., mayor and council, in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), alleging a rent control program (1) violated Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24, (2) violated housing anti-discrimination laws, (3) was impermissible zoning, and (4) was confiscatory. The trial court granted appellees summary judgment, and the Maryland Court of Appeals granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The program applied to single-family homes, duplexes, triplexes, and quadraplexes, while exempting apartment buildings. The court of appeals held it did not offend due process or equal protection, under Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24, because (1) its goals were not illegitimate governmental ends, and (2) a perceived nexus between it and the goals of encouraging housing availability for households of all incomes and preserving, maintaining, and improving existing housing had a rational basis. It did not offend housing anti-discrimination provisions in Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 20-705 (2009) or Prince George's County (Md.) Code § 2-210(a) (Supp. 2005) because it distinguished between rental units in single-family neighborhoods and those in apartment buildings, so it did not distinguish between groups based on a group characteristic. It was not de facto zoning, unauthorized under Md. Ann. Code art. 28, § 7-103(b), because it did not divide the city into districts, define lot sizes, or mandate uses. It was not impermissibly confiscatory because (1) it gave a landlord a way to obtain a fair return on an investment, and (2) nothing showed it unreasonably limited return rates.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

McHale v. DCW Dutchship Island, LLC


No. 123, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


415 Md. 145; 999 A.2d 969; 2010 Md. LEXIS 283



July 22, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Case No. 02-C-08-134861.
McHale v. Dutchship Island, 411 Md. 598, 984 A.2d 243, 2009 Md. LEXIS 1119 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Chair of the Maryland Critical Area Commission for the Chesapeake and Atlantic Coastal Bays filed a complaint against defendant landowner for restoration and mitigation pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-1815(a)(2)(i)(1). Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the complaint. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) granted the motion to dismiss, with prejudice. The chair appealed.


OVERVIEW: The subject property was an island in a limited development area and lying within either the buffer or expanded buffer of the critical area. The landowner demolished the existing development and built a new home, sheds, gazebo, boat ramp, driveway, sidewalks, pool, and deck, without the necessary permits and variances. The issue before the court of appeals was whether amended Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-1808(c)(4) (Supp. 2009) applied to the variance application filed three and one half years before the statute was amended and where the object of the application was to cure violations of the Chesapeake and Atlantic Coastal Bays Critical Area Protection Program (Critical Area Law), Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. §§ 8-1801 to 8-1817 (Supp. 2009). The court of appeals concluded that the amended provision did not apply retrospectively to the variance application. The Legislature intended for the amendments to be applied prospectively to situations where an underlying violation of the Critical Area Law pre-deated the amendment. The Legislature included an effective date and also expressed that the Act was not have not effect on the Critical Area Law violations originating before that date.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Shea


No. 133, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


415 Md. 1; 997 A.2d 768; 2010 Md. LEXIS 269



June 23, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Case No. 03-C-07-14718.
Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Shea, 406 Md. 744, 962 A.2d 370, 2008 Md. LEXIS 771 (2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO ABIDE THE RESULT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the implied consent law, Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1 (2009), an administrative law judge (ALJ) suspended respondent motorist's license for 90 days; it stayed the suspension for one year, conditioned on his participation in the ignition interlock program. Respondent appealed; the Circuit Court for Baltimore County, Maryland, reversed. The Maryland Motor Vehicle Administration's petition for review was granted.


OVERVIEW: After stopping respondent for not wearing a seatbelt, the officer smelled a moderate odor of alcohol emanating from him. The officer conducted field sobriety tests (FSTs) and arrested him. Respondent took a breath test, which disclosed a blood alcohol concentration of 0.18. He challenged the test results and argued that under the implied consent law, the officer lacked grounds to request him to take the breath test. The trial court reversed the suspension, ruling that because the officer lacked a reasonable articulable suspicion that respondent was under the influence of alcohol, conducting the FSTs violated the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, and all actions taken thereafter were legally unsupportable. The high court disagreed. Neither the fruit of the poisonous tree doctrine nor the exclusionary rule applied to license suspension proceedings. Further, the trial court erred by employing a rationale for reversing the ALJ's decision that was not advanced by respondent and was not the basis of the ALJ's decision. Substantial evidence supported the ALJ's decision that the officer had reasonable grounds under § 16-205.1(b)(2) to request respondent to take a breath test.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was vacated and the case was remanded to that court with instructions to decide whether the ALJ improperly relied upon the results of the breathalyzer test in ordering the sanction of license suspension.

Nefedro v. Montgomery County


No. 84, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


414 Md. 585; 996 A.2d 850; 2010 Md. LEXIS 210



June 10, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Nefedro v. Montgomery County, 410 Md. 165, 978 A.2d 245, 2009 Md. LEXIS 666 (2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ENTRY OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner fortuneteller sued a county and its executive, seeking a declaratory judgment, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-406, stating that the fortunetelling ordinance, Montgomery County, Md., Code § 32-7 (1999), violated the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 40. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) granted summary judgment for the county. The fortuneteller appealed.


OVERVIEW: The fortuneteller wanted to open a fortuentelling business in the county. However, a county ordinance prohibited the acceptance of remuneration for fortunetelling. The fortuneteller claimed that the ordinance violated his right to freedom of speech under the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 40. The court of appeals agreed, noting that a restriction on remuneration for protected speech is a restriction on the speaker's First Amendment right to freedom of speech. By punishing speech when that speech was made in exchange for payment, the fortunetelling ordinance imposed a burden on that speech. The court of appeals declined to find, as the county suggested, that fortunetelling was inherently fraudulent and thus, should not receive First Amendment protection. The court of appeals also declined to find that fortunetelling was commercial speech merely because the fortuneteller might receive money in exchange for his services. Finally, the court of appeals concluded that the ordinance was not narrow tailored, as there was at least one less restrictive, effective means of combating fraud - laws making fraud illegal without respect to protected speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for entry of a declaratory judgment.

Wash. Suburban Sanitary Comm'n v. Phillips


No. 85, September Term, 2009, No. 154, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


413 Md. 606; 994 A.2d 411; 2010 Md. LEXIS 183; 109 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 526



May 10, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Case Nos. CAL04-12870, CAL07-30365, & CAL06-18780.
Sillers v. Wash. Suburban Sanitary Comm'n, 406 Md. 744, 962 A.2d 371, 2008 Md. LEXIS 776 (2008)
WSSC v. Phillips, 410 Md. 165, 2009 Md. LEXIS 1124 (2009)



DISPOSITION: PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY IN NO. 154 REVERSED; CASES REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE WSSC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three cases, respondent/petitioners employees sued petitioner/respondent employer in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) for employment discrimination, under former Md. Ann. Code art. 49B, § 42(a) (2003). In one case, the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed a ruling that the employer was a person, and it appealed. In the other cases, the Court of Appeals issued writs of certiorari, sua sponte, to review the issue.


OVERVIEW: The employer, the Washington Suburban Sanitary Commission (WSSC), said it was not a "person," under former Md. Ann. Code art. 49B, § 42(a) (2003), now Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 20-1202(a) (2009), so it could not be sued for employment discrimination under a county ordinance. The court of appeals disagreed because (1) Md. Ann. Code art. 49B, § 15's definitions applied to Md. Ann. Code art. 49B, § 42(a), as they were in pari materia, (2) the definition of "person" excluded the state but included local entities, and, (3) to further statutory purposes of eliminating employment discrimination and letting certain counties have their county codes' anti-discrimination provisions enforced in private civil actions, and to construe § 42(a) broadly for claimants, "person," as used in § 42(a), included WSSC as a local entity, due to its autonomy from state oversight and nearly exclusive level of control over employment decisions. The county ordinance was not an unconstitutional general law due to taxes imposed on another county's citizens to satisfy a judgment against WSSC under the ordinance because any extra-territorial effect was due to WSSC's decision about how to satisfy a judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed, and the judgments of the trial court were reversed, and the cases were remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Williamson v. State


No. 61, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


413 Md. 521; 993 A.2d 626; 2010 Md. LEXIS 175



April 22, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Williamson v. Maryland, 131 S. Ct. 419, 178 L. Ed. 2d 327, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 8288 (U.S., Oct. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Wiliamson v. State, 409 Md. 47, 972 A.2d 861, 2009 Md. LEXIS 374 (2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, a jury in the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) convicted defendant on two charges of rape and related offenses. Defendant appealed to the court of special appeals. The court of appeals granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained in violation of his statutory and Fourth Amendment rights. Defendant contended the police-created abandonment of a cup led to illegal and warrantless deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) testing. The court of appeals disagreed, finding that defendant unequivocally abandoned the cup after he was offered a meal, accepted it, and threw the debris on the floor. Defendant also argued that even if seizure of the cup was lawful, the testing of DNA on the cup was a separate search and it was unreasonable to conduct the test because defendant was being detained and had a reasonable expectation of privacy in his DNA. The court of appeals concluded that there was no Fourth Amendment violation, as defendant voluntarily abandoned the cup and thus, no unconstitutional seizure occurred. Next, the court of appeals concluded that the uploading of the DNA sample to a database and a query of that database did not violate defendant's rights. Finally, the court of appeals concluded that defendant's statement was admissible, as his arrest was based on probable cause and the statement was free of Fifth Amendment violations.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Office of the Pub. Defender v. State


No. 9, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


413 Md. 411; 993 A.2d 55; 2010 Md. LEXIS 143



April 16, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Cecil County. Case No. K-07-1715.
Public Defender v. State, 407 Md. 275, 964 A.2d 675, 2009 Md. LEXIS 227 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CECIL COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE JUDGMENT OF CONTEMPT ENTERED AGAINST JOHN K. NORTHROP; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE STATE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Officer of the State Public Defender (OPD) denied a criminal defendant's application for public representation. After the defendant requested appointed counsel, an attorney from the OPD was named to represent him. The attorney appealed, but did not seek to stay its effect and did not appear in the criminal matter. The Circuit Court for Cecil County (Maryland) found the attorney in direct contempt and fined him $ 10. The attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court of appeals was whether the trial court had the authority to appoint an attorney from a local OPD to represent a criminal defendant who qualified for public representation based on indigency, upon the court's finding that the local OPD previously and erroneously denied representation to the defendant. The court of appeals concluded that the trial court had such authority and did not exceed its authority when it appointed the attorney, the Deputy District Public Defender for Cecil County, or a member of his office, to represent the indigent defendant, to whom representation had been previously and wrongfully denied by the local OPD. By evaluating the defendant's application solely under the maximum net annual income and asset ceiling standard of Md. Code Regs. 14.06.03.05A and D(2), while ignoring wholly the statutorily-mandated indigency factors contained in former Md. Ann. Code art. 27A, § 7 (2003), and Md. Code Regs. 14.06.03.05A, the local OPD applied the incorrect standard for determining indigency and erred, both legally and factually, in concluding that the defendant did not qualify for public representation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to vacate the judgment of contempt.

 

128 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Dove


No. 40, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


413 Md. 70; 991 A.2d 65; 2010 Md. LEXIS 81



March 17, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Dove, 408 Md. 487, 970 A.2d 892, 2009 Md. LEXIS 702 (2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CALVERT COUNTY IS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE. RESPONDENT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent driver sought judicial review in the Circuit Court for Calvert County (Maryland) of the decision of an administrative law judge to suspend the driver's license for refusing a blood test to determine alcohol concentration. The trial court reversed the decision, and the State petitioned for a writ of certiorari, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: The driver refused an officer's request to submit to a blood test, and the officer refused his offer to submit to a breath test. The court of appeals held substantial evidence showed Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 10-305(a)(1)(ii) (2006) required a blood test because his injuries required his removal to a hospital. His offer to submit to a breath test did not mitigate his refusal because a blood test was mandatory. His fear of needles did not excuse his refusal because (1) he could refuse the test, under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(b)(1) (2009), and (2) he could choose to submit to it or have his license suspended. A breath test by hospital staff did not nullify his refusal because (1) he did not unequivocally withdraw his refusal under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(g) (2009), (2) he did not consent to the required blood test, and (3) the test did not comply with Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 10-304 (2006). The officer had a reasonable suspicion, under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(a)(2) (2009) that he drove under the influence because (1) he had an odor of alcohol on his person, (2) he had watery eyes, and (3) he was involved in a collision.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded with directions to affirm the administrative law judge's decision.

Md. Reclamation Assocs. v. Harford County


No. 143, September Term, 2008, No. 144, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


414 Md. 1; 994 A.2d 842; 2010 Md. LEXIS 75



March 11, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by, Corrected by Md. Reclamation Assocs. v. Harford, 414 Md. 1, 994 A.2d 842, 2010 Md. LEXIS 191 (Md., May 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Harford County. Case No. 12-C-02-1810 AA.
Md. Reclamation Assocs. v. Harford County, 382 Md. 348, 855 A.2d 351, 2004 Md. LEXIS 467 (2004)



DISPOSITION: DECISIONS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY IN BOTH CASE NO. 143 AND CASE NO. 144 ARE AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner appealed two judgment of the Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland), one which affirmed the Harford County Board of Appeals's denial of the owner's request for several variances and one which affirmed the Harford County Board of Appeals's interpretation of various zoning provisions applicable to the owner.


OVERVIEW: The owner sought to construct and operate a rubble landfill on the property. On appeal, the owner challenged various decisions which led to the denial of the necessary variances. Among other things the court of appeals held that the Board did not err in finding that granting the requested variances would be substantially detrimental to the adjacent property. Evidence showed, inter alia, that the landfill activities would be substantially detrimental to the historic church and graveyard that were next to the subject property. In addition, the community would be detrimentally affected, as the increase in air pollution was likely to result in worsening of asthma in children, cardio-respiratory difficulties in elderly persons, and increased truck traffic in areas where children played and boarded school buses. As for the second case, the court of appeals concluded, inter alia, that the county's right to enact and enforce zoning regulations was not preempted by the State statute governing landfills. The court also noted that the owner needed more than a state permit and site plan approval to have a vested right in an existing zoning use and neither equitable nor zoning estoppel applied.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court in both cases were affirmed.

 

130 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Shenker v. Laureate Educ., Inc.


No. 8, September Term, 2009


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


411 Md. 317; 983 A.2d 408; 2009 Md. LEXIS 837



November 12, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Case No. 24-C-07-000664.
Shenker v. Laureate, 407 Md. 275, 964 A.2d 675, 2009 Md. LEXIS 215 (2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED IN PART AND AFFIRMED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE IN PART AND AFFIRM IN PART THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY, CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION, AND TO REMAND THIS CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID 50% BY PETITIONERS AND 50% BY BOARD RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner shareholders appealed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed a trial court judgment dismissing their claims against respondents, a board of directors and investors, principally because the suit was seen as an impermissible direct shareholder suit. Petitioners asserted that respondents breached their fiduciary duties owed to petitioners with regard to a cash-out merger transaction.


OVERVIEW: On direct appeal, the Court of Special Appeals held that Md. Code Ann., Corp. & Ass'ns § 2-405.1 (1975, 2007 Repl. Vol.) barred all direct shareholder claims and affirmed the dismissal of petitioners' claims for civil conspiracy and aiding and abetting. The court held that the Court of Special Appeals erred in so holding and determined that, where corporate directors exercise non-managerial duties outside the scope of § 2-405.1(a), such as negotiating the price that shareholders will receive for their shares in a cash-out merger transaction, after the decision to sell the corporation already has been made, they remain liable directly to shareholders for any breach of those fiduciary duties. The court held that § 2-405.1(a) does not provide the sole source of directorial duties, and that other common law fiduciary duties of directors remain in place and may be triggered by the occurrence of appropriate events. As such, because the fiduciary duties of the board were owed directly to petitioners as shareholders, petitioners were permitted to proceed directly against the board.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, that part of the Court of Special Appeals's judgment that dismissed petitioners' direct claims against the board for the alleged breach of fiduciary duties of candor and maximization of shareholder value. The court affirmed, in part, the dismissal of petitioners' claims against the investors for civil conspiracy and aiding and abetting.

 

131 of 744 DOCUMENTS


In re Gloria H.


No. 15, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


410 Md. 562; 979 A.2d 710; 2009 Md. LEXIS 647



September 14, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Gloria H., 404 Md. 658, 948 A.2d 70, 2008 Md. LEXIS 287 (2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY, SITTING AS A JUVENILE COURT, VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in an Adult Truancy Petition alleging a violation of Md. Code Ann., Educ. § 7-301 based on her daughter's absence from school for 74 of 180 days. The Circuit Court of Prince George's County (Maryland), sitting as a juvenile court, placed defendant on unsupervised probation. Defendant appealed. Before the argument was presented, the state's highest court issued a writ of certiorari on its own initiative.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court noted that defendant and the daughter both testified that although the daughter arrived at her school on a regular basis, she rarely attended classes. It was reasonably concluded that the child did not attend school for more than 10 weeks, and that defendant had failed to see that the daughter attended school. This presumption was rebutted as it was based upon the impermissible inference that because defendant's incomprehensible testimony lacked credibility, the opposite of her exculpatory testimony was true. Although defendant was not entitled to a judgment in her favor as a matter of law, she was entitled to a new trial. Once the daughter entered the school building, she was in the care and custody of the school. Because a child who attended school was committed to the control of state and local authorities, evidence that a high school student was not in his or her homeroom when attendance was taken was sufficient to establish that the student did not attend school on that day. However, there was a fact issue as to whether the child was cutting class. A finding that defendant violated the § 7-301 required proof that the daughter did not attend school.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with the opinion.

 

132 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Lonaconing Trap Club v. Inc. Md. Dep't of the Env't


No. 139, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


410 Md. 326; 978 A.2d 702; 2009 Md. LEXIS 629



August 26, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Allegany County. Case No. 01-C-05-025244.
Lonaconing Trap Club, Inc. v. Md. Dep't of the Env't, 406 Md. 743, 962 A.2d 370, 2008 Md. LEXIS 765 (2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maryland Department of the Environment (MDE) sued a shooting sports club, seeking civil penalties and an injunction prohibiting the club from engaging in shooting activities on its property until it complied with noise regulations. The trial court granted the requested relief. The club appealed; the Maryland Court of Special Appeals affirmed. The club's petition for a writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Md. Code Ann., Envir. § 3-401(c)(6) (2007) exempted shooting sports clubs in certain counties, including the one where the club operated, from MDE noise regulations unless, as of 1 January 2005, they had been found to be non-compliant with an MDE noise regulation prohibiting sounds greater than 60 decibels to be heard on adjacent residential property during daylight hours. The club claimed that § 3-401(c)(6)(ii) violated Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24 and the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV by distinguishing arbitrarily between shooting sports clubs in different counties and against clubs that were not compliant with MDE regulations as of 1 January 2005. The high court disagreed. Section 3-401(c)(6) was related rationally to a legitimate interest in promoting local preferences. That the club was allegedly the only one affected by § 3-401(c)(6)(ii)'s exclusion of clubs deemed non-compliant as of 1 January 2005 did not violate equal protection, as the club did not explain how it was treated differently from similarly-situated clubs. The adoption of § 3-401(c)(6)(ii) was not a new grant of authority that required MDE to promulgate new noise regulations.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court and the intermediate appellate court were affirmed.

 

133 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Smigiel v. Franchot


No. 121, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


410 Md. 302; 978 A.2d 687; 2009 Md. LEXIS 630



August 26, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 27, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: Smigiel v. Franchot, 403 Md. 637, 943 A.2d 1260, 2008 Md. LEXIS 114 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state legislators and a business owner, sued respondents, the State and others, seeking a declaration that legislation enacted by the Maryland General Assembly during the extension of its adjournment was invalid. The Carroll County Circuit Court (Maryland) granted the State's motion to dismiss the case and held that the challenged legislation was valid. Petitioners' request for a writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted a law proposing for voter ratification a constitutional amendment authorizing slot machines and placing restrictions on their use. Petitioners argued that the legislature violated the state Constitution by making an appropriations bill contingent on voter approval, as this was an unconstitutional attempt to delegate to the public its duties of enacting legislation. The high court disagreed. Md. Const. art. XVI gave explicit authority to the legislature to propose, and for the voters to approve, constitutional amendments. The legislature had the power to enact general legislation before, and contingent on, the adoption of a constitutional amendment that it had proposed to the voters. As the sufficiency of a ballot question that had yet to be drafted was a hypothetical inquiry, if the high court ruled on the question, it would be improperly issuing an advisory opinion; therefore, this issue was not justiciable. As to petitioners's claim that the extension of the legislature's adjournment violated Md. Const. art. III, § 25, since this was an internal procedural issue for the legislature to resolve, it was a nonjusticiable political question.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Grasslands Plantation, Inc. v. Frizz-King Enters., LLC


No. 117, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


410 Md. 191; 978 A.2d 622; 2009 Md. LEXIS 626



August 25, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County. Case No. 17-C-06-012080 AA.
Grasslands Plantation, Inc. v. Frizz-King Enters., LLC, 406 Md. 579, 961 A.2d 553, 2008 Md. LEXIS 686 (2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR QUEEN ANNE'S COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE DECISION OF THE BOARD OF APPEALS OF QUEEN ANNE'S COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE BOARD FOR PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a protesting adjacent landowner, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County (Maryland), which upheld the decision of a county board of zoning appeals' approval of respondent developer's subdivision. The county's planning commission had approved the subdivision, which the board affirmed in a de novo appeal proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The developer owned 275 acres and obtained approval to construct a subdivision on that land. On appeal, the protestor contended that the board improperly placed the burden of proof on it, as the appellant in the review hearing, to challenge the planning commission's approval of the subdivision. The protestor asserted that the board engaged in a de novo review of the commission's decision and that in such a proceeding, the burden of proof remained with the applicant, the developer. The court agreed with the protestor and found that the Board erred in shifting the burden of proof from the developer, the subdivision applicant, to the protestor, the appellant in the board's de novo review proceeding. The court held that in a proceeding before the board, an entirely new hearing in which all specified issues on appeal should be heard anew as if no decision had been previously rendered, which required the burden to remain with the developer to establish facts necessary to obtain approval for its proposed subdivision. Additionally, the court held that the board or the commission had to apply the conformity and emergency service ordinances, which were enacted while the case was on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to vacate the decision of the board and remand the case to the board for further proceedings. In any further proceedings, the board and the commission were ordered to apply the county's new legislation enacted after the board's decision and while the case was on appeal.

Green v. N.B.S., Inc.


No. 94, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


409 Md. 528; 976 A.2d 279; 2009 Md. LEXIS 283



July 21, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court Case No. 24-C-02-003243.
Green v. N.B.S., Inc., 180 Md. App. 639, 952 A.2d 364, 2008 Md. App. LEXIS 84 (2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; PETITIONER TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner child's economic damages for her exposure to lead-based paint were capped at $ 515,000 under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 11-801. The Maryland Court of Special Appeals (intermediate court) held that § 11-801 applied to all actions for personal injury and wrongful death, that § 11-801 was constitutional under Md. Const. art. III, § 33, and that the cause of action arose after October 1, 1995, but before October 1, 1996.


OVERVIEW: The child's petition for a writ of certiorari was granted. The child's Maryland Consumer Protection Act (CPA), Md. Code Ann., Com. Law § § 13-301 et seq., claim was a personal injury action, and § 11-108 applied to proceedings in which a consumer asserted a claim for money damages to compensate for injuries sustained as a result of a CPA violation. The Maryland legislature, when it amended the cap statute, did not intend to expand the statute to cover wrongful death actions, but at the same time intend to narrow its application so it covered wrongful death actions and all actions for personal injury so long as the victims were injured as the result of common law torts. The trial court properly ruled that the cap statute applied to the child's claim for damages that arose, in part, out of a violation of the CPA. Section 11-108 applied to any action for damages for personal injury, and was a general law, not a special law under § 33. On the basis of the testimony of the child's expert, the child was lead poisoned as of September 26, 1996, and the cause of action arose prior to October 1, 1996. Thus, the verdict was properly capped at $ 515,000.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate court was affirmed.

Wilson v. State


No. 91, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


409 Md. 415; 975 A.2d 877; 2009 Md. LEXIS 277



July 20, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
In the Circuit Court for Washington County. Case No. 21-K-05-35663.
Wilson v. State, 176 Md. App. 7, 932 A.2d 739, 2007 Md. App. LEXIS 122 (2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WASHINGTON COUNTY AND REMAND TO THAT COURT FOR A NEW TRIAL. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY WASHINGTON COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petition for a writ of certiorari was granted allowing petitioner to challenge the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the judgment of conviction and the denial of his motion to suppress by the trial court. Petitioner was found guilty of second degree assault, resisting arrest, possession of marijuana, and disorderly conduct, following a jury trial and was sentenced to four years of incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was observed by a police officer lying in the middle of the street. Petitioner got up and started to walk away. The officer told petitioner that he was going to take him to the hospital as he thought petitioner was under the influence of a controlled substance. The officer attempted to handcuff petitioner at which time a struggle ensued, which led to his seizure and the seizure of the contraband on his person. Petitioner asserted that his warrantless arrest was unreasonable since probable cause that he was engaged in criminal activity was lacking, therefore, anything that flowed from the unlawful arrest must be suppressed. The court adopted the community caretaking doctrine and a test to ensure that the community caretaking function is conducted reasonably. The court held that the officer's decision to place petitioner in handcuffs and to transport him to the hospital in his police cruiser was not carefully tailored to the underlying justification for the seizure. Petitioner had committed no crime and was not suspected of criminal activity. If medical treatment was necessary, an ambulance could have been called instead of the officer seizing petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and remanded the case to that court with instructions for it to reverse the judgment of the trial court. The court further directed the lower court to remand the case to the trial court for a new trial.

Laurel Racing Ass'n v. Video Lottery Facility Location Comm'n

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted the cross-petitions for certiorari filed by appellant applicant and appellee, the Video Lottery Facility Location Commission and others, with regard to a decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) upholding the Commission's denial of a video lottery operation license to the applicant. McFarlin v. State


No. 119, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


409 Md. 391; 975 A.2d 862; 2009 Md. LEXIS 276



July 17, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: McFarlin v. State, 406 Md. 579, 961 A.2d 553, 2008 Md. LEXIS 652 (2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. PETITIONER TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought to introduce a letter written by defendant into evidence at defendant's trial for murder. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress and admitted the letter into evidence. The Court of Special Appeals of Maryland affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was serving a prison sentence for convictions unrelated to this case when he killed another inmate. While still in prison, defendant wrote a letter to his father in which he admitted to killing someone in prison. Prison officials intercepted the letter and provided a copy to State prosecutors. Defendant sought to suppress the letter. Defendant argued that a prisoner's right to correspond was a fundamental right protected by the First Amendment and that he had a Fourth Amendment right to privacy in the letter. The appellate court held that defendant's constitutional rights were not violated when prison officials inspected the letter and provided a copy to State officials. Defendant did not have an expectation of privacy in his letter to his father that was objectively reasonable. Even if defendant had an objectively reasonable expectation of privacy in his letter to his father, the seizure of the letter did not violate the Fourth Amendment because the seizure was justified by the prison's legitimate concern for security. The Inmate Orientation Manual did not support defendant's contention that he had an objectively reasonable expectation of privacy in his mail.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Master Fin., Inc. v. Crowder


No. 96, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


409 Md. 51; 972 A.2d 864; 2009 Md. LEXIS 194



June 9, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Crowder v. Master Fin., Inc., 176 Md. App. 631, 933 A.2d 905, 2007 Md. App. LEXIS 114 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED AS TO NON-HOLDER DEFENDANTS AND AS TO CLAIMS UNDER CONSUMER PROTECTION ACT BUT OTHERWISE REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM IN PART AND REVERSE IN PART THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND REMAND TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; 50% OF THE COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONERS AND 50% BY RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagors filed 19 suits, including 9 class action suits, alleging violations of the Maryland State Secondary Mortgage Loan Law (SMLL), Md. Code Ann., Com. Law § 12-401 et seq., the Maryland State Consumer Protection Act (CPA), Md. Code Ann., Com. Law tit. 13, and seeking a declaratory judgment against defendants, the lenders, the holders of the loans, and certain non-holders who purchased other loans. The actions were dismissed.


OVERVIEW: The Maryland Court of Special Appeals reversed as to the SMLL claims, and otherwise affirmed. Certiorari was granted. The state's highest court held that an action to recover civil penalties for SMLL violations was an other specialty under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-102(a)(6) and was subject to a 12-year limitations period. An action for damages under the CPA was subject to a three-year limitations period under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-101(3). The actions to declare the loans void or voidable due to SMLL violations were subject to a three-year limitations period under § 5-101. Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-107 did not apply. The named plaintiffs in the class action suits based on SMLL violations could sue the lenders who made the loans and persons who purchased the loans from those lenders but had no cause of action against persons who purchased other loans from the lenders, but who had no interest in or connection with the named plaintiffs loans. Md. R. 2-231(a) did not permit such an action based on a judicial link between those persons and the other defendants or between them and other putative members of the plaintiff class.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed as to non-holder defendants and as to claims under the CPA, but otherwise was reversed. The case was remanded to the appellate court with instructions to affirm in part and reversed in part the judgment of the trial court, and to remand to the trial court for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion. The appellate costs were to be paid equally by the parties.

Rogers v. Eastport Yachting Ctr., LLC


No. 123, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


408 Md. 722; 971 A.2d 322; 2009 Md. LEXIS 63



May 14, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Rogers v. Eastport Yachting Ctr., LLC, 406 Md. 744, 962 A.2d 371, 2008 Md. LEXIS 713 (Md., Dec. 19, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; PETITIONER TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner resident challenged a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-302 (1974, 1998 Repl. Vol.), dismissed for lack of jurisdiction his appeal of the decision of a city board of port wardens to approve of respondent company's application to replace a pier and bulkhead. The court of appeals granted the resident's petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The company submitted an application to the city for the replacement of the pier and bulkhead. The port wardens approved the application. The resident filed a petition for judicial review in the circuit court, which affirmed the port wardens' decision. The resident filed a notice of appeal to the court of special appeals. The court of special appeals found that it did not have jurisdiction to hear an appeal from a decision of the port wardens. The court of appeals held that the circuit court proceeding was a statutory judicial review action. The board of port wardens was not an agency under Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-202(b). Therefore, any right of appeal to the court of special appeals had to be found elsewhere, and no such right could be found in the Maryland Code, in the Anne Arundel County Code, or in the Annapolis City Code. Even if there were appellate jurisdiction, there was no merit in the resident's argument that the port wardens' decision was void ab initio. Because the resident had actual knowledge that the port wardens would consider the company's application at a public hearing, he lost nothing from the technical failures of notice about which he complained.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the judgment of the court of special appeals.
