Anne Arundel County v. Halle Dev., Inc.


No. 59, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


408 Md. 539; 971 A.2d 214; 2009 Md. LEXIS 60



May 6, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Judgment entered by Halle Dev., Inc. v. Anne Arundel Cty., 2013 Md. App. LEXIS 175 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., July 29, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Case No. C-2001-69418. Philip T. Caroom, JUDGE.
Cambridge Commons v. Anne Arundel County, 2006 Md. Cir. Ct. LEXIS 26 (June 5, 2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which permitted respondent property owners to proceed with a class action to obtain a refund of development impact fees paid to the county within a certain time period. The property owners brought suit seeking recovery of the impact fees collected by the county for the fiscal years 1988 through 1996.


OVERVIEW: The county was authorized to collect the impact fees via an ordinance. The trial court determined that because $ 4,719,359 in impact fees collected from the owners were not timely paid or encumbered for capital improvements, and the period to make capital improvements was not properly extended, the owners were entitled to refunds. The county argued that the trial court erred by not remanding the case to the county administrative officials for it to grant extensions and perform other tasks relative to the fees collected. The Court found that the trial court did not err in certifying the owners' class action under Md. R. 2-231(b). The Court found that although the county may face an onerous administrative burden in complying with the class member identification and individual notice requirements of a class action lawsuit due to its record-keeping practices, that burden did not render the class action unmanageable. The court further held that the trial court properly determined that the owners' action to recover the impact fees was not barred by the three-year statute of limitations set forth in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-101 (1974, 2006 Repl. Vol., 2008 Supp.).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People's Ins. Counsel Div. v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. 86, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


408 Md. 336; 969 A.2d 971; 2009 Md. LEXIS 51



April 15, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by People's Ins. Counsel Div. v. Allstate Ins. Co., 2011 Md. App. LEXIS 29 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Mar. 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Carol E. Smith, JUDGE.
People's Ins. v. Allstate, 406 Md. 112, 956 A.2d 201, 2008 Md. LEXIS 558 (2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maryland People's Insurance Counsel Division petitioned in the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) for judicial review of an order of the Maryland Insurance Commissioner approving a filing submitted by respondent insurance company. The court granted the insurance company's motion for dismissal. When the Division appealed, the insurance company petitioned for certiorari prior to any proceedings before the intermediate appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The insurance company notified the Maryland Insurance Commissioner, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 19-107 (2006), that it intended to stop accepting new homeowners insurance business in certain catastrophe prone areas in Maryland. When the Commissioner approved the filing, the Maryland People's Insurance Counsel Division petitioned for judicial review. The insurance company moved to dismiss the judicial review action, arguing that the Division did not have standing to seek judicial review under Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 2-215 (2003), because it was not a party to the hearing before the Commissioner and because the Commissioner's approval of the filing was not an action from which judicial review could be sought. The state high court found that the general powers conferred upon the Division in Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 6-301 et seq. (2004, 2006 Supp.), gave the Division the ability to be a party to hearings before the Commissioner and to seek judicial review therefrom. The court also held that the Commissioner's approval of the insurance company's non-write notice-filing was an action from which judicial review could be sought.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Newell v. Runnels


No. 48, September Term 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


407 Md. 578; 967 A.2d 729; 2009 Md. LEXIS 32; 28 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1632



March 13, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Worcester County). Theodore R. Eschenburg, JUDGE.
Runnels v. Newell, 179 Md. App. 168, 944 A.2d 1183, 2008 Md. App. LEXIS 40 (2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE IN PART AND AFFIRM IN PART THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT, CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION, AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE DIVIDED AS FOLLOWS - THIRTY PERCENT TO BE PAID BY CAROLINE COUNTY, AND SEVENTY PERCENT TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN NEWELL AND THE STATE OF MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maryland Court of Special Appeals on wrongful discharge and overtime wage claim summary judgment rulings reversed it for defendant State's Attorney but affirmed it as to defendant county on First Amendment claims, reversed it for the State's Attorney and defendant State on a corresponding state claim, entirely affirmed it as to abusive discharge, and reversed it for the county on the wage claims. The state's highest court granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The State's Attorney, newly-elected, fired the fired employees. The fired employees sued the State's Attorney, the State, and the county, alleging wrongful discharge because they had supported the State's Attorney's opponent in the general election, and the failure to pay overtime wages. They claimed violations of their free speech rights under the First Amendment, the corresponding state provision under Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 40, common law abusive discharge, and that the failure to pay overtime wages violated the Fair Labor Standards Act and Maryland Wage and Hour Law. The state's highest court found a triable issue existed as to the State's Attorney on the First Amendment, and as to the State's Attorney and State on the corresponding state claim, because the State's Attorney had the right to control office operations and political support being a job requirement. It also found that abusive discharge facts had to be further developed, and that triable factual issues about whether the county was the fired employees' joint employer and what the county knew about a pattern of overtime work precluded summary judgment on the state and federal overtime wage claims.


OUTCOME: The state's highest court on the First Amendment claim affirmed as to the State's Attorney, with the county not seeking review; it also affirmed as to the State's Attorney and State on the corresponding state claim, again with the county not seeking review, reversed as to the State's Attorney and State on the abusive discharge claim, with the county not seeking review, and affirmed as to the county on the state and federal overtime wage claims.

Trinity Assembly of God of Balt. City, Inc. v. People's Counsel for Balt. County


No. 27, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


407 Md. 53; 962 A.2d 404; 2008 Md. LEXIS 630



December 24, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). Lawrence R. Daniels, JUDGE.
Trinity Assembly of God v. People's Counsel for Balt. County, 178 Md. App. 232, 941 A.2d 560, 2008 Md. App. LEXIS 8 (2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed a circuit court's judgment holding that respondent, a county board of appeals, correctly applied the law when it denied petitioner church's request for variances from area and height limits that applied to identification signs under Baltimore County, Md., Zoning Regulations § 450 (sign law), the court granted the church's petition for a writ of certiorari to review whether the board erred.


OVERVIEW: Section 450 limited the area of an identification sign to 25 square feet and the height of a sign to 6 feet. The church sought to construct a sign that would be 250 square feet in face area and 25 feet high. The church challenged the board's application of the requirements for a variance and argued that the denial of the variance violated the Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act (RLUIPA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000cc et seq. The court held that the board applied the correct legal standards in denying the variance request and that substantial evidence supported the board's findings that the physical attributes of the church's property were not unique and that the denial of the variance would not cause practical difficulty for the church. The court held that neither the board's decision nor the sign law violated the RLUIPA because the denial of the church's variance request did not impose a substantial burden on the church's religious exercise where the church had numerous ways of publicizing its activities and evangelizing, the church already had two identification signs, and there was no evidence that church attendance was falling due to the lack of the proposed sign.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower courts' decisions.

Doe v. Montgomery County Bd. of Elections


No. 61, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


406 Md. 697; 962 A.2d 342; 2008 Md. LEXIS 626; 51 A.L.R.6th 621; 105 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 525



December 19, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected on January 06, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: On cross-motions for summary judgment filed by voters and county board, the Circuit Court, Montgomery County. Robert A. Greenberg, JUDGE.
Doe v. Montgomery County Bd. of Elections, 2008 Md. Cir. Ct. LEXIS 7 (2008)
Doe v. Montgomery County Bd. of Elections, 406 Md. 110, 956 A.2d 199, 2008 Md. LEXIS 507 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action under Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-209, plaintiff citizens challenged the validity of a referendum petition that had been certified for the ballot by defendant Montgomery County Board of Elections. The court granted cross-petitions for certiorari and expedited review from a decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Maryland, to answer three questions presented by the citizens and the Board.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the Board properly certified a referendum petition filed by the citizens that sought to overturn a bill enacted by the county council to add gender identity as a protected characteristic under the county's antidiscrimination laws. The circuit court dismissed the complaint as time-barred under Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-210(e), finding that, even if suit had been timely filed, the citizens had no legal basis for challenging the Board's certification decision. On certiorari, the court disagreed, holding that the citizens' complaint was timely filed within 10 days of the Board's final decision because the cause of action accrued on March 6, 2008, when the Board made its final certification decision rather than on February 20, 2008, when it accepted half of the petition signatures as valid. The amended complaint related back to the original complaint and was timely. The names of inactive voters should have been included in the total number of registered voters, and to the extent that Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 3-503 (2005) provided otherwise, the statute was unconstitutional. Because many signatures were invalid, the Board improperly certified the referendum.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court. The court entered summary judgment on behalf of the citizens.

VNA Hospice v. Dep't of Health & Mental Hygiene


No. 105, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


406 Md. 584; 961 A.2d 557; 2008 Md. LEXIS 625



December 11, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). Dana M. Levitz, JUDGE.
Dep't of Health & Mental Hygiene v. VNA Hospice ., 176 Md. App. 475, 933 A.2d 512, 2007 Md. App. LEXIS 134 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED AND CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maryland Department of Health and Mental Hygiene amended petitioner health care provider's hospice care license to exclude the provider from providing home-based hospice services in two counties. A circuit court reversed the decision. The Court of Special Appeals of Maryland reversed the circuit court's judgment, and directed the circuit court to affirm the Department's final decision. The provider filed a petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: In deciding to rescind that part of the provider's license relating to providing home-based hospice services in two counties, the Department rejected the provider's interpretation of § 19-906(c)(3) of the Health-General Article (2000, 2005 Repl. Vol.). The disputed statutory interpretation issue presented was whether the provider's provision of home-based bereavement services to family members of the dying or deceased persons, in the two counties during the year 2001, constituted the provision of home-based hospice services to a patient in those counties within the meaning of § 19-906(c)(3). The provider argued that the provision of bereavement services to family members qualified under the statute, whereas the Department contended that the only services which qualified under § 19-906(c)(3) were services rendered to the dying person. The state high court found that an interpretation of § 19-906(c)(3), which excluded bereavement services to a family, based upon a difference in phraseology between "to a patient" and "for a patient," was unreasonable. Therefore, the provider was performing home-based hospice services in the two counties during 2001.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was vacated, and the case was remanded to the intermediate appellate court with directions to affirm the judgment of the circuit court.

Chesek v. Jones


No. 117, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


406 Md. 446; 959 A.2d 795; 2008 Md. LEXIS 609



November 6, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County), Thomas J. Bollinger, JUDGE
Chesek v. Jones, 402 Md. 623, 938 A.2d 825, 2008 Md. LEXIS 22 (2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a committee co-chairperson, petitioned the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), for an order to compel testimony from appellant state employees. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The court granted the co-chairperson's' motion against one state employee in its entirety, and granted the motion in part and denied it in part as to the other employee. The co-chairperson filed a petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The Legislative Policy Committee of the Maryland General Assembly created a special committee to examine procedures, practices, and standards pertaining to the involuntary separation of state employees. In the resolution establishing the special committee, the Legislative Policy Committee expressly delegated all of its powers under Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 2-408 (2004 Repl. Vol.). The question presented was whether the special committee, which was formed pursuant to Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 2-407 (2004 Repl. Vol.), possessed subpoena power in the course of its duties. The state high court found that the provision granting the Legislative Policy Committee the authority to appoint a special committee in Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 2-407(b)(3) (2004 Repl. Vol.) (amended 2007) necessarily carried with it the implied power to delegate subpoena power to the special committee. Furthermore, one of the employees was required to answer the special committee's questions regarding the source of the payment of his attorney's fees as this information was not considered to be privileged.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the power of the special committee to issue subpoenas. The case was remanded as one of the employees was required to answer the special committee's questions regarding the source of the payment of his attorney's fees.

State v. Adams


No. 38, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


406 Md. 240; 958 A.2d 295; 2008 Md. LEXIS 579



October 15, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Adams v. Maryland, 129 S. Ct. 1624, 173 L. Ed. 2d 1005, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1986 (U.S., 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Adams v. Hershberger, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33656 (D. Md., Apr. 6, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Case No. CT 20,221; CT 20,494; CT 20,546; CT 20,723.
State v. Adams, 171 Md. App. 668, 912 A.2d 16, 2006 Md. App. LEXIS 260 (2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM IN PART AND REVERSE IN PART THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought certiorari review of a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) that affirmed a circuit court's decision to grant petitioner inmate's post-conviction petition. The State claimed that the inmate waived his challenge to advisory jury instructions, a Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 465 (1971) jurisdiction instruction, and that counsel was not ineffective for failing to object to the instructions.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's claim that advisory jury instructions violated the reasoning in Stevenson and Montgomery was rejected because those cases did not announce new law. By not objecting at trial or on direct appeal, claims based on Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 23 were waived. Although the lower courts erroneously analyzed the waiver issue as being governed by Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 7-106(c) (2001), caselaw and the plain error doctrine precluded review. The court declined to exercise discretion to review the waiver issue because of the potential for unfair prejudice to the State due to a 20-year delay. The inmate's objections to the jury instructions and special verdicts regarding jurisdiction were waived by a failure to object at trial or raise the issue on direct appeal. The ineffective assistance claim failed both prongs of the Strickland test. That claim concerned whether Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 465 (1971) addressed venue or expanded jurisdiction. Because either interpretation was reasonable, counsel's performance was not deficient for failing to object. Further, counsel properly preserved his argument that § 465 did not expand Maryland's territorial jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of special appeals that affirmed the grant of the postconviction petition and reversed the finding as to effective assistance of counsel. The case was remanded to that court with directions to affirm in part and reverse in part the circuit court's judgment and to remand to that court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Turner v. Kight


No. 5, September Term, 2008


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


406 Md. 167; 957 A.2d 984; 2008 Md. LEXIS 518



October 7, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Kight v. Turner, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3037 (U.S., Apr. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Turner v. Kight, 178 Md. App. 1, 938 A.2d 863, 2007 Md. App. LEXIS 156 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE JUDGMENT OF CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AND REMAND TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action, which plaintiff arrestee and defendants, Montgomery County and others, seemed to agree was a repetition of state-law claims filed in federal court, was filed in the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Those served moved to dismiss. The circuit court dismissed the claims and denied reconsideration. The Court of Special Appeals agreed with the trial court's conclusion as to 28 U.S.C.S. § 1367(d). The instant court granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The question before the court was whether petitioner's complaint was erroneously dismissed by the circuit court on the ground that the causes pleaded were barred by limitations. That question hinged on the proper construction to be given to 28 U.S.C.S. § 1367(d), which provided for the tolling of state statutes of limitations with respect to state-law claims (i) that were brought in a U.S. District Court, (ii) that were within the "supplemental jurisdiction" of that court, but (iii) over which the district court eventually declined to exercise jurisdiction. The instant court interpreted § 1367(d) differently than did the Circuit Court and the Court of Special Appeals. The court concluded that § 1367(d) did, indeed, suspend the running of limitations and did not merely extend the period, that the suspension remained in effect until 30 days after all federal proceedings, including appellate proceedings, were concluded, and that Md. R. 2-101(b) could be read in harmony with § 1367(d), as so construed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was reversed. The case was remanded to that court with instructions to reverse the judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County and remand to that court for further proceedings.

Harris v. State


No. 21, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


406 Md. 115; 956 A.2d 204; 2008 Md. LEXIS 511



September 11, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City), Thomas Ward, JUDGE
Harris v. State, 173 Md. App. 71, 917 A.2d 1162, 2007 Md. App. LEXIS 26 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR A NEW TRIAL. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state court of appeals issued a writ of certiorari in the instant criminal case to decide whether a trial court erred by denying defendant's motion for a new trial where the guilty verdicts were rendered by a jury which had never been sworn.


OVERVIEW: Both the trial transcript and the docket entries rebutted any presumption of regularity. The trial transcript clearly showed that the jury was not sworn before the jurors were dismissed for lunch. When the jury reconvened after lunch, the transcript revealed that the court proceeded directly with opening statements, without the oath being administered to the jury. According to the trial transcript, which the official reporter of the court certified as being complete and accurate, the jury was not sworn at any point during the trial. The docket entry stating that the jury was not sworn reinforced the accuracy of the transcript. Thus, any presumption of regularity was overcome in the instant case. The jury in defendant's case was never sworn. Defendant established that the jury was not sworn in violation of Md. R. 4-312(h), Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 5, and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 21, that there was no waiver of defendant's objection to the unsworn jury, and that, because the jury was never sworn, the harmless error doctrine was not applicable. Therefore, the court of appeals reversed on the ground that the jury was never sworn.


OUTCOME: Since the jury which convicted defendant was never sworn, defendant's convictions were reversed.

AT&T Communs. of Md., Inc. v. Comptroller of the Treasury


No. 111, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


405 Md. 83; 950 A.2d 86; 2008 Md. LEXIS 316



June 12, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Evelyn O. Cannon, JUDGE.
AT&T Communs. of Md., Inc. v. Comptroller of the Treasury, 176 Md. App. 22, 932 A.2d 748, 2007 Md. App. LEXIS 118 (2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE DECISION OF THE MARYLAND TAX COURT AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE TAX COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The telecommunications company appealed a sales and use taxes assessment by respondent, the Maryland Comptroller of the Treasury to the Maryland Tax Court. The Tax Court affirmed the assessment. A circuit court affirmed the assessment. The Court of Special Appeals of Maryland also affirmed the assessment. The telecommunications company filed a petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The State of Maryland, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 11-101(m)(5) (2004 Repl. Vol.), imposed sales and use taxes on charges made by out-of-state vendors to Maryland consumers of telecommunications information services beginning with the area code "900." The parties contested whether the telecommunications company, over whose long-distance lines the communications from out-of-state vendors were transmitted to Maryland consumers, was obligated to collect the tax from the Maryland consumers and, failing to have done that, to be responsible for payment of the tax to the Comptroller. The state high court found that the uncontested factual findings established only that the telecommunications company acted as a common carrier with regard to the 900 number transactions at issue. Thus, the telecommunications company could not be held responsible for the 900 number sales and use taxes on transactions between Maryland consumers and the information services vendors without violating the Commerce Clause of the U.S. Constitution. The Comptroller's assessment against the telecommunications company under Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 11-101(o)(2) (2004 Repl. Vol.) was not permissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with directions to reverse the judgment of the circuit court and to remand the case to the circuit court with directions to reverse the decision of the Maryland Tax Court and to remand the case to the tax court for further proceedings.


 

152 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Janice M. v. Margaret K.


No. 122, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


404 Md. 661; 948 A.2d 73; 2008 Md. LEXIS 255



May 19, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). Michael J. Finifter, JUDGE.
Janice M. v. Margaret K., 171 Md. App. 528, 910 A.2d 1145, 2006 Md. App. LEXIS 253 (2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother filed a petition for a writ of certiorari after the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed a circuit court's finding that respondent, the mother's former partner, was a de facto parent and was entitled to visitation with the mother's adopted child. The petition was granted to determine whether an exceptional circumstances standard, rather than a best interests standard, applied to visitation with a de facto parent.


OVERVIEW: The mother and partner had been in a committed same-sex relationship. The partner filed a complaint in the circuit court, seeking custody of the mother's adopted child or visitation. The circuit court denied her custody but found that she was a de facto parent and granted her visitation. The court of special appeals affirmed. The supreme court held that the circuit court erred in granting visitation to the partner on the ground that she was a de facto parent without first finding that the mother was an unfit parent or that sufficient exceptional circumstances existed to overcome the mother's liberty interest in the care, custody, and control of her child under the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. De facto parenthood was not recognized in Maryland. Therefore, the supreme court concluded that in order to overcome the constitutional rights of a legal parent to govern the care, custody, and control of his or her child, even a person who would qualify as a de facto parent, who sought visitation or custody, had to demonstrate exceptional circumstances as a prerequisite to a court's consideration of the best interests of the child as a factor in that decision.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment of the court of special appeals and remanded the case to that court with instructions to reverse the judgment of the circuit court and to remand the case to the circuit court to determine whether, based on all relevant facts, exceptional circumstances existed to overcome the mother's liberty interest in the care, custody, and control of the child.

Robinson v. State


No. 71, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


404 Md. 208; 946 A.2d 456; 2008 Md. LEXIS 187



April 15, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, DeLawrence Beard and Ann S. Harrington, JUDGES
In the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Case No. 104146.
Robinson v. State, 402 Md. 36, 935 A.2d 406, 2007 Md. LEXIS 681 (2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Montgomery County Circuit Court (Maryland) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of sexual abuse of a minor in violation of Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 3-602 (Cum. Supp. 2006). The state supreme court granted certiorari on its own initiative to hear defendant's appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for, inter alia, sexual abuse of a minor regarding the alleged sexual abuse of his niece. At the time of the alleged abuse, defendant was married to the niece's mother's sister. Between the time of the incident and trial, defendant and his wife divorced. However, he never raised the argument that his status did not fall within the Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 3-601(a)(3) (Cum. Supp. 2006) definition of "family member" or that Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 3-602 (Cum. Supp. 2006), regarding sexual abuse of a minor, was unconstitutional. A jury found him guilty of the sexual abuse of a minor. The state's highest court found that (1) his failure to raise the issue of whether Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 3-602 (Cum. Supp. 2006) was unconstitutional meant that the issue was not preserved for appellate review, (2) defense counsel's question about whether a "divorced uncle" qualified as a family member did not preserve for review a question about defendant's status since he was not a "divorced uncle" at the time of the incident, and (3) defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim had to be raised in a post-conviction proceeding rather than on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The state's highest court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

154 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Delawter


No. 63, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


403 Md. 243; 941 A.2d 1067; 2008 Md. LEXIS 30



February 13, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Frederick County. G. Edward Dwyer, Jr., JUDGE.
MVA v. Delawter, 401 Md. 172, 931 A.2d 1095, 2007 Md. LEXIS 617 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY REVERSED AS TO MEDICAL ADVISORY BOARD REFERRAL ISSUE. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE RULING OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Motor Vehicle Administration (MVA) filed a petition for a writ of certiorari, seeking review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Frederick County (Maryland) reversing an administrative law judge's decision to refer respondent licensee to the Medical Advisory Board (MAB) of the MVA for alcohol evaluation.


OVERVIEW: An officer who arrested the licensee for driving under the influence provided the licensee with a DR-15 Advice of Rights form, which advised the licensee of the potential administrative sanctions she faced. Four months later, the officer confiscated the licensee's driver's license, served her with an order of suspension, and issued her a temporary license. Although the circuit court found substantial evidence supporting the administrative law judge's decision to suspend the licensee's license for 25 days, the circuit court reversed the referral to the MAB because the licensee did not receive notice on the DR-15 form that by exercising her right to a hearing under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(f)(7) (1977, 2006 Repl. Vol.), she was subjecting herself to a possible referral to the MAB. Because a referral to the MAB was not an administrative sanction within the meaning of Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(b), the court held that the DR-15 Advice of Rights form did not need to include notice that an administrative law judge, after conducting a hearing requested by a driver to modify the suspension of the driver's license, could refer the driver to the MAB.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment as to the MAB referral and remanded the case with instructions to affirm the ruling of the administrative law judge.

Griffin v. Bierman


No. 79, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


403 Md. 186; 941 A.2d 475; 2008 Md. LEXIS 27



February 12, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Paul Garvey Goetzke, Judge.
Griffin v. Bierman, 402 Md. 36, 935 A.2d 406, 2007 Md. LEXIS 706 (2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mortgagor challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which refused to set aside a foreclosure sale initiated by appellees, substitute trustees under the deed of trust.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor defaulted on her loan. The trustees mailed concurrently to the mortgagor, by certified mail and first-class mail, a letter required by Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 7-105 (Repl. Vol. 2003), informing her that a foreclosure action "may be or has been" docketed. The trustee also mailed the mortgagor, again via both first-class and certified mail, the notice required by Md. R. 14-206(b)(2), informing the mortgagor of the time, date, and location of the public foreclosure sale. The mortgagor did not receive any letters. The property was sold at auction. The mortgagor claimed that her due process rights, guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24, were violated by the failure to receive advance notice of the sale. In affirming the trial court's decision, the court held that mortgagees were not required to personally serve property owners with notices of foreclosure to satisfy due process. The court also held that Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 7-105, and Md. R. 14-206 were not constitutionally infirm merely because they did not require the certified mail to be returned as undeliverable prior to requiring that notice be sent first class mail.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Colburn v. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr. Servs.


No. 41, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


403 Md. 115; 939 A.2d 716; 2008 Md. LEXIS 17



January 14, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Somerset County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. D. William Simpson, JUDGE.
Colburn v. Dep't of Corr., 400 Md. 646, 929 A.2d 889, 2007 Md. LEXIS 541 (Md., 2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SOMERSET COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONERS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Division of Corrections of the Maryland Department of Public Safety and Correctional Services (DPSCS) ruled that appellant correctional supervisors were not entitled to overtime compensation under the Fair Labor Standards Act (FLSA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 201 et seq. They appealed; an administrative law judge (ALJ) affirmed. They appealed to the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland), which affirmed. They sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The supervisors' employer, a correctional facility within the DPSCS, required them to work overtime and perform non-supervisory tasks in their overtime capacity that were normally assigned to correctional officers, but did not pay them overtime. The supervisors filed a grievance; the ALJ agreed with the DPSCS's position. The high court held that the supervisors were exempt employees under 29 U.S.C.S. § 213(a)(1) of the FLSA because they were employed as bona fide administrative or professional employees. They were deemed administrative or professional employees under 29 C.F.R. § 541.2 (2002) since they were paid salaries, exercised discretion and independent judgment, and performed office or non-manual work directly related to management policies. That Md. Code Ann., State Pers. & Pens. § 11-104, subjected them (and all state employees) to suspension without pay as a disciplinary sanction did not mean they were not salaried employees. They qualified for the administrative or professional employee exemption under 29 C.F.R. § 541.1(f) (2002) because they were engaged in management of the enterprise and supervised two or more employees.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

157 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Alavez v. Motor Vehicle Admin.


No. 28, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


402 Md. 727; 939 A.2d 139; 2008 Md. LEXIS 11



January 9, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Patrick Cavanaugh, JUDGE.
Alavez v. MVA, 399 Md. 595, 925 A.2d 634, 2007 Md. LEXIS 389 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner requested an administrative hearing after the Maryland Motor Vehicle Administration (MVA) cancelled his Maryland driver's license. An administrative law judge (ALJ) sustained the cancellation. The Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) affirmed the ALJ's ruling. Petitioner was granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a citizen of Mexico who had previously had a driver's license in California, Virginia, and New Jersey. Prior to coming to Maryland, petitioner's New Jersey license was withdrawn because he misrepresented facts on his application. Upon learning of New Jersey's withdrawal, MVA cancelled petitioner's Maryland license. The court of appeals concluded that the plain wording of Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-103.1 supported the MVA's decision and that nothing in § 16-103.1 created an exception where a cancellation in another state was for conduct that would not warrant that result in Maryland. Thus, the fact that Maryland would issue a driver's license to a person who was not a United States citizen was of no consequence. Petitioner also claimed that § 16-103.1 violated Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24. The court of appeals disagreed, noting that the fact that the New Jersey revocation was permanent did not make the Maryland reciprocity statute unconstitutional. The court of appeals also noted that petitioner's license was not suspended in New Jersey because he was an illegal residence, but because he forced documents to obtain a license, and Maryland would do the same.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Bowen v. City of Annapolis


No. 34, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


402 Md. 587; 937 A.2d 242; 2007 Md. LEXIS 738



December 14, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Ronald A. Silkworth, JUDGE.
City of Annapolis v. Bowen, 173 Md. App. 522, 920 A.2d 54, 2007 Md. App. LEXIS 45 (2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY TO ENTER AN APPROPRIATE DECLARATORY JUDGMENT IN CONFORMANCE WITH THIS OPINION. THE DECLARATORY JUDGMENT SHALL BE A SEPARATE DOCUMENT WHICH DECLARES THE RIGHTS OF THE PARTIES AND MAY INCLUDE SUCH ANCILLARY RELIEF AS NECESSARY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID ONE QUARTER BY PETITIONERS AND THREE QUARTERS BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retired officers, and others, filed a complaint against a city, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief relating to the city's denial of the officers' claims requesting increased pension benefits. A civil service board denied the claims. The trial court reversed the board. The Court of Special Appeals of Maryland reversed the trial court. The retired officers sought certiorari review, and their request was granted.


OVERVIEW: The city interpreted Annapolis, Md., Code § 3.36.150A1 as denying the officers increased pension benefits in tandem with raises given to their active duty counterparts. Initially, the appellate court held that the intermediate appellate court did not err in denying the officers' motion to dismiss. Annapolis, Md., Code § 3.16.150A limited the applicability of the appeal provisions solely to "permanent status civil service employees." The officers were non-active, retired persons, and thus not "permanent status employees." The trial court could have only acted on the complaint to review the board's actions by way of a common law or equity writ. The trial court erred by failing to enter a written declaration of the rights of the parties, but this error was not jurisdictional. Contrary to the city's position, Annapolis, Md., Code § 3.36.150A1 was clear and unambiguous, and supported the officers' position. The section meant just what it said, that the officers were entitled to receive increases in their pensions in tandem to any increases in salaries that active police officers and firefighters of the same rank and same number of years of service received from the city.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed as to its interpretation of Annapolis, Md., Code § 3.36.150A1. The case was remanded for the trial court to enter an appropriate declaratory judgment order and for further proceedings. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed in part.

In re Adoption/Guardianship of Rashawn H.


No. 7, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


402 Md. 477; 937 A.2d 177; 2007 Md. LEXIS 732



December 11, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Fredrick County) Theresa M. Adams, JUDGE.
In re Adoption of Rashawn Kevon H., 398 Md. 314, 920 A.2d 1058, 2007 Md. LEXIS 200 (2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE JUDGMENTS OF CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY AND REMAND TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN CONFORMANCE WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother appealed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed trial court judgments terminating her parental rights to two of her children. Respondent, a county Department of Social Services (DSS), had petitioned the trial court and had acquired an adjudication that the children were in need of assistance. The trial court terminated the mother's rights, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-313.


OVERVIEW: The children were six and five years of age at the time of the proceeding. The mother had several interrelated problems: a low intelligence, an oppressive childhood, life-long poverty, was evicted and disqualified from governmental housing assistance due to her drug-dealing mother, failed to maintain steady employment or housing, and other issues. The mother had basically surrendered the children to DSS upon having no place to take them and no means to care for them. The court found various problems with the trial court's considerations under § 5-313, namely that it found that it was not sure whether the children had any attachment left to the mother. Further, the trial court indicated that the mother did a pretty good job of maintaining communication with DSS, but that it was not sufficient to guarantee the safety and health of the children, without explaining the connection between any lack of communication and the safety and health of the children. Overall, the trial court did not relate its findings under § 5-313 to the presumption favoring continuation of the parental relationship or to any exceptional circumstance that would suffice to rebut that presumption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the special appellate court and remanded the case to that court with instructions for it to vacate the judgments of the trial court and remand the case to the trial court. On remand, the trial court was directed to make clear and specific findings with respect to each of the relevant statutory factors and permit the parties to present additional evidence.

Parker v. State


No. 37, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


402 Md. 372; 936 A.2d 862; 2007 Md. LEXIS 725



December 6, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Althea M. Handy, JUDGE.
Parker v. State, 393 Md. 245, 900 A.2d 751, 2006 Md. LEXIS 413 (2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY WITH RESPECT TO THE CONVICTION FOR POSSESSION OF A FIREARM, AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS AS SET FORTH IN THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, defendant was convicted of possessing a regulated firearm and possession with intent to distribute a controlled dangerous substance. Defendant was sentenced to five years, without parole on the firearm count and 12 years on the drug charge. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) vacated the trial court's judgments and remanded the case. Defendant's petition for a writ certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the Fourth Amendment and Maryland law required that the evidence seized should have been excluded from his trial because the police officers did not knock and announce their presence prior their search of a house. The supreme court concluded that, under the particular circumstances of the instant case, the evidence was excludable if there was a violation of Maryland's "knock and announce" principle. The supreme court noted that a judicial officer in Maryland, under Maryland law, could not issue a "no-knock" warrant. Rather, the propriety of the "no-knock" entry was to be reviewed and determined on the basis of the facts known to the officers at the time of entry, rather than at the time of the application for the warrant. Defendant also argued that the evidence supporting his handgun conviction was insufficient because the State never established that he had an interest in or residence in the house, or that he had ever been in proximity to the handgun. The supreme court agreed, noting, inter alia, that the evidence did not show whether defendant was residing in the home at the time or simply visiting a residence of the home.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals remanding the case for a new suppression hearing was affirmed. Defendant's conviction on the firearm count was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court with directions to reverse the judgment as to the conviction for possession of a firearm and for further proceedings.

Evans v. Burruss


No. 1, September Term, 2007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


401 Md. 586; 933 A.2d 872; 2007 Md. LEXIS 648



October 12, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Burruss v. Evans, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1312 (U.S., Feb. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Civil Case No. 260494), Louise G. Scrivener, JUDGE.
Evans v. Burruss, 398 Md. 313, 920 A.2d 1058, 2007 Md. LEXIS 198 (2007)



DISPOSITION: THE DECISION OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IS REVERSED IN PART AND AFFIRMED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE BOARD OF APPEALS OF MONTGOMERY COUNTY; COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent neighbors objected to the issuance of building permits to petitioner property owner. The appeals were dismissed by the county board of appeals. The neighbors petitioned for judicial review. The circuit court remanded the case to the board. The owner appealed to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, which reversed the circuit court, reinstated the board's dismissal, and remanded the case to the board. The owner filed for certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The owner received a county building permit to erect four amateur radio towers on his property. Upon seeing construction trucks, work being done, and holes being drilled on the owner's property, the neighbors, the abutting property owners, became aware, for the first time, of the permits that were issued for the erecting of the towers. The neighbors contended that they had a due process right to actual notice of the issuance of the building permits. The state supreme court found that the county code section applicable to the issuance of permits created no right of notice nor did it create any additional property rights in the neighbors that they did not have inherently. Further, because the county code section applicable to the issuance of permits as a ministerial act did not require the service of actual, personal notice to the neighbors, the failure to do that which was not required to be done was not a denial of due process. Furthermore, generally, the issuance of building permits and similar permits was a ministerial act. Finally, the issuance of the building permits to the owner for construction on his property created no additional property rights in the neighbors.


OUTCOME: The part of the intermediate appellate court's judgment that remanded the case to the county board to receive evidence as to whether the issuance of the building permit infringed upon the neighbors' property rights was reversed. The judgment of the intermediate appellate court as to the nonrenewal of the building permit and the timeliness or lack thereof was affirmed so that the decision of the county board was affirmed.


 

162 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Conaway v. Deane


No. 44, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


401 Md. 219; 932 A.2d 571; 2007 Md. LEXIS 575



September 18, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. M. Brooke Murdock, JUDGE.
Conaway v. Deane, 393 Md. 477, 903 A.2d 416, 2006 Md. LEXIS 516 (2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY REVERSED; STAY VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DECLARE CONSTITUTIONAL THE STATUTE AT ISSUE AND TO DENY INJUNCTIVE RELIEF TO APPELLEES. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant circuit court clerks denied marriage licenses to certain same-sex couples, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 2-201 (2006). The Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, same-sex couples and a homosexual male, but stayed enforcement of its ruling pending the resolution of the expected appeal, pursuant to Md. R. 2-632. The instant court issued a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The instant court found that because § 2-201 did not abridge the fundamental right to marriage, did not discriminate on the basis of sex in violation of Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 46, and did not otherwise implicate a suspect or quasi-suspect class, the marriage statute was subject to rational review. The State's legitimate interests in fostering procreation and encouraging the traditional family structure in which children were born were related reasonably to the means employed by Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 2-201 (2006). As Md. Const. Decl. Rights. art. 46 was not intended by the General Assembly and the Maryland voters who enacted and ratified the Maryland Equal Rights Amendment in 1972 to reach classifications based on sexual orientation, Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 2-201 (2006) did not draw an impermissible sex-based distinction. The statute prohibited equally both men and women from the same conduct. Same-sex marriage was not so deeply rooted in Maryland or the country as a whole that it was a fundamental right protected by Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24, in light of Maryland's history of limiting marriage to those unions between members of the opposite sex.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was reversed, the stay was vacated, and the case was remanded to the circuit court with directions to declare constitutional the statute at issue and to deny injunctive relief to plaintiffs. Costs were to be paid by plaintiffs.

Rhoads v. Sommer


No. 127, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


401 Md. 131; 931 A.2d 508; 2007 Md. LEXIS 496



August 27, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). Michael D. Mason, JUDGE.
Sommer v. Rhoads, 171 Md. App. 392, 910 A.2d 514, 2006 Md. App. LEXIS 244 (2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS. CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EVENLY BETWEEN PETITIONER AND RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed the ruling that a retainer agreement precluded preservation of respondent attorney's lien against petitioner former client's damage award and found that nothing showed that he had waived the lien, that the lien had not been lost, that it was not extinguished, and that her due process rights had not been violated. The state's highest court granted the former client's petition for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The former client was terminated from her employment. She hired the attorney to represent her in an employment discrimination lawsuit. The attorney filed a federal lawsuit on her behalf. Eventually, summary judgment was granted on nine of her 10 claims. A jury found for the former employer on the remaining claim. Thereafter, she filed a voluntary petition for bankruptcy. She was later granted a discharge in bankruptcy. After disagreements with the attorney, she pursued her case on her own and obtained a monetary judgment. The attorney then filed a complaint on behalf of himself and respondent law firm to enforce an attorney's lien. The trial court ruled that the retainer agreement precluded the attorney's lien. On appeal, the intermediate appellate court found that the language of the retainer agreement did not preclude an attorney lien pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Bus. Occ. & Prof. 10-501(a). On further review, the state's highest court found that the attorney had not waived the lien under the retainer agreement's language, the lien had not been lost or extinguished by the discharge in bankruptcy, and her due process rights had not been violated by imposition of the lien.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court's judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to that court with instructions to remand the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Patterson v. State


No. 83, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


401 Md. 76; 930 A.2d 348; 2007 Md. LEXIS 494



August 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Patterson v. Md., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2645 (U.S., Mar. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County). Michael P. Whalen, JUDGE.
Patterson v. State, 396 Md. 9, 912 A.2d 646, 2006 Md. LEXIS 855 (2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Special Court of Appeals (Maryland) affirmed the trial court's judgment and concluded that the search warrant involved in a search of a motel room was supported by probable cause and, thus, the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress drug evidence supporting his drug convictions was proper. The state's highest court granted defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari and the State's cross-petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: A police officer made a traffic stop of defendant's vehicle. Defendant then ran away. The officer briefly lost sight of defendant but was able to arrest him by a wooded area. A gun holster was recovered from underneath him. Police searching the chase area also found an ammunition magazine. Police then watched a motel room where defendant took temporary residence. Thirty-four days after the traffic stop, they executed a search warrant there. The search team found drugs and drug paraphernalia there. Defendant was arrested on drug charges. His motion to suppress was denied. The intermediate appellate court affirmed. The state's highest court found that the warrant issued by the magistrate was not supported by probable cause since the State's theory that defendant had returned and retrieved the gun from the chase scene was mere speculation; however, it also found the warrant was based on evidence sufficient to create disagreement between judges about whether probable cause existed. As a result, it found police officers were objectively reasonable in relying on the warrant under the Leon good-faith exception to support their belief that the gun was at defendant's temporary residence.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

John A. v. Bd. of Educ.


No. 132, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


400 Md. 363; 929 A.2d 136; 2007 Md. LEXIS 474

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court issued a writ of certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) before it decided the appeal filed by appellant parents from a decision entered by a circuit court, which affirmed an administrative law judge's (ALJ's) order dismissing the parents' due process complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction under the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act (IDEA), 20 U.S.C.S. §§ 1400 to 1419.

166 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Casey v. Mayor of Rockville


No. 85, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


400 Md. 259; 929 A.2d 74; 2007 Md. LEXIS 476



July 30, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). Eric M. Johnson, JUDGE.
Casey v. Rockville, 396 Md. 9, 912 A.2d 646, 2006 Md. LEXIS 851 (2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner trustee filed an action against respondents, a mayor and a city council, after respondents designated a bungalow belonging to the trust as historically and architecturally significant. The trial court remanded the case to respondents to consider the economic feasibility of preserving the bungalow. The Maryland Court of Special Appeals reversed the judgment remanding the matter. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate appellate court reasoned that respondents were not required to consider the economic infeasibility of preservation when deciding whether to designate the property as historic. The court agreed. Under Md. Ann. Code art. 66B, § 8.02, a local body had to consider whether the subject property had historical, archaeological, or architectural significance. It was only after property was designated historic and a development permit application was maintained that the statutory scheme, through Md. Ann. Code art. 66B, §§ 8.06(b), 8.09, and 8.10 (2003), required that economic feasibility and financial hardship be considered in determining whether a permit should be issued. Next, the regulatory takings claim was premature, as there had been no final denial of petitioner's demolition permit application. Finally, failing to consider economic impact was not a denial of due process. Respondents had given petitioner full and fair hearings on the issue of the historical/architectural significance of the property, and there remained an opportunity for petitioner to present evidence regarding economic feasibility in connection with the demolition permit application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals.

 

167 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Getty v. Carroll County Bd. of Elections


No. 139, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


399 Md. 710; 926 A.2d 216; 2007 Md. LEXIS 353



June 21, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Michael M. Galloway, JUDGE.
Getty v. Carroll County Bd. of Elections, 393 Md. 158, 899 A.2d 878, 2006 Md. LEXIS 335 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals brought suit against appellee county election board and voter, seeking to stay the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland)'s order that approved an agreement between the voter and board to adopt a redistricting plan creating five commissioner districts in the county, effectually creating a new method of election of commissioners. The appellate court issued a writ of certiorari on its own initiative.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court, in adopting the consent order that approved the plan to elect county commissioners by district rather than at-large, went beyond the functions of the judiciary and interfered with the legislature's authority to redistrict. In issuing the order, the circuit court assumed a role that belonged to the legislative and executive departments of state government under Md. Const. art. VII, §§ 1 and 2. No legislation served as the basis for the consent order as a house bill that would have adopted a county redistricting plan had failed to pass the state senate. That failure to adopt a redistricting plan in no way authorized the circuit court to take action. It was not the place of the appellate court to adopt a redistricting plan for the county as it was not permitted to act until the legislature had acted. In other words, the power of judicial review did not equate to the power to exercise functions that were explicitly vested in the other organs of government. Finally, the circuit court had no authority under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-409(a), to act as the initial controversy over the election was rendered moot when it approved the consent order.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's approval of the consent order was a clear violation of the Maryland Constitution.

Nader For President 2004 v. Md. State Bd. of Elections


No. 76, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


399 Md. 681; 926 A.2d 199; 2007 Md. LEXIS 351



June 21, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Philip T. Caroom, JUDGE
Nader for President 2004 v. Md. State Bd. of Elections, 383 Md. 216, 858 A.2d 483, 2004 Md. LEXIS 597 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Anne Arundel County Circuit Court (Maryland) entered a judgment that found a state statutory law and a state regulation requiring that petition signatures of registered voters to recognize appellant political party applicant be on the petition sheet for the county in which they were registered to vote were constitutional. After the political party appealed, the state's highest court issued a writ of certiorari to allow it to review the case.


OVERVIEW: The political party applicant filed a petition to form a new political party and nominate a certain person as its candidate for President of the United States. Appellee state elections board, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Elec. Law § 6-203 (2003), invalidated several signatures affixed to the nominating petition. As a result, the petition fell short of the required number of signatures. The political party applicant and the state elections board stipulated that a certain number of invalidated signatures--enough to meet the signature requirement--were invalidated solely on the basis that the signers, registered voters in the State, were registered in a county other than the one specified on the petition sheets they signed; in other words, they signed the petition sheet for the "wrong county." The sole issue in the case was whether, when the signatories were otherwise eligible to vote in Maryland, the State's invalidation of "wrong county" signatures was proper. The trial court found that conduct proper. On further review, the state's highest court found that the law was invalid in the present case since it disenfranchised voters without a valid constitutional basis for doing so.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

McDaniel v. Am. Honda Fin. Corp.


No. 108, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


400 Md. 75; 926 A.2d 757; 2007 Md. LEXIS 346



June 12, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case # CAL 00-21321. Steven I. Platt, JUDGE.
McDaniel v. Am. Honda, 396 Md. 12, 912 A.2d 648, 2006 Md. LEXIS 898 (2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Prince George's County Circuit Court (Maryland) entered a judgment that dismissed appellant lessees' first amended complaint, which alleged that the late fee assessed by appellee lessor regarding auto leases was an amount in excess of the legal rate of interest allowed by the state constitution, after concluding the late fee was not interest. The state's highest court granted the lessees' petition for writ of certiorari to review the ruling.


OVERVIEW: The lessees entered into commercial leases with the lessor to lease motor vehicles. Pursuant to the lease agreements, the lessor charged a late fee on any payment not received within 10 days after it was due. Each lessee contended that the lessor assessed, and each lessee paid, a single late fee for failing to remit timely a monthly amount due. Thereafter, the lessees filed a first-amended complaint asserting that the charge was an illegal amount of interest in violation of Md. Const. art. III, § 57, which stated the legal rate of interest unless the General Assembly provided otherwise. The trial court dismissed the first amended complaint for failing to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the late fees were permissibly imposed because the General Assembly had provided a law for imposition of them, Md. Code Ann., Com. Law § 14-2002(g)(1)(i) (Repl. Vol. 2000), Md. Const. art. III, § 57 thus did not apply, the late fees were not interest, no contracts were impaired, and the General Assembly did not impermissibly delegate rule-making authority in enacting Md. Code Ann., Com. Law § 14-2002(g)(1)(i) (Repl. Vol. 2000).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Clipper Windpower, Inc. v. Sprenger


No. 136, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


399 Md. 539; 924 A.2d 1160; 2007 Md. LEXIS 345



June 8, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Kaye A. Allison, JUDGE.
Clipper Windpower, Inc. v. Sprenger, 2006 Md. LEXIS 960 (Md., Mar. 9, 2006)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent landowners petitioned the circuit court for judicial review of a final order by petitioner, the Maryland Public Service Commission, granting petitioner applicant a certificate of public convenience and necessity for the construction of a wind turbine facility. The circuit court dismissed the actions. The Court of Special Appeals of Maryland reversed the judgment. The Commission and the applicant filed petitions for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose over the construction of a wind turbine facility. Although two of the landowners submitted citizen comment letters following the conclusion of an adjudicatory hearing conducted by the Commission, neither they, nor a conservation association, sought to intervene. One of the landowners then, on behalf of the association, requested a rehearing. After the Commission denied the request, the owners filed their petitions for judicial review under Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 3-202(a) (1998). The state supreme court found that the landowners failed timely to apply to intervene as parties, under Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 3-106 (1998), before the Commission and, therefore, the applications for rehearing were not properly submitted by "parties in interest," under Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. § 3-114(c) (1998). As a result, there was no timely application for rehearing under § 3-114(c). Additionally, the petitions for judicial review were untimely under Md. R. 7-203 because the time for filing a petition for judicial review was not stayed by the association's' application. Thus, the decisions of the Commission and the trial court were correct.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed, and the case was remanded to that court with instructions to affirm the judgment of the circuit court.

In re Roberto D. B.


No. 110, September Term, 2002


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


399 Md. 267; 923 A.2d 115; 2007 Md. LEXIS 269



May 16, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As corrected May 17, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Eric M. Johnson, JUDGE
In re Roberto D.B., 372 Md. 684, 814 A.2d 570, 2003 Md. LEXIS 10 (2003)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE STATE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father, joined by putative appellee gestational carrier, filed a petition asking the circuit court to issue "accurate" birth certificates that did not list the gestational carrier as the mother of his twins. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) rejected the petition. The father appealed and the Court of Appeals of Maryland, on its own motion, granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The father contracted with the carrier to carry an embryo. Two fertilized eggs were implanted in the carrier and she delivered twins. The carrier was listed as the "mother" of the children as a result of the hospital following the requirements of Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 4-208 (Supp. 2006). The issue on appeal was whether the name of the carrier had to be listed on the birth certificates for the twins. The father's primary contention, under the Maryland Equal Rights Amendment (ERA), was that the parentage statutes of Maryland did not afford equal protection of the law to men and women similarly situated because the parentage statutes allowed a man to deny paternity and did not allow a woman to deny maternity. The court of appeals held that Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 4-211 (Supp. 2006), did not preclude a court from issuing an order authorizing a birth certificate that did not list the mother's name. The trial court's implication of the best interest of the child standard was error, as the carrier wanted to relinquish her parental rights, not assert them, and there was no issue of unfitness as to the father.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Shepard


No. 88, September Term, 2006


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


399 Md. 241; 923 A.2d 100; 2007 Md. LEXIS 267



May 15, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to the Court of Special Appeals. Eric M. Johnson, JUDGE
MVA v. Shepard, 396 Md. 9, 912 A.2d 646, 2006 Md. LEXIS 854 (2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE RULING OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE PRESIDING OVER RESPONDENT'S LICENSE SUSPENSION HEARING. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Montgomery County Circuit Court (Maryland) entered a judgment that vacated the administrative law judge's ruling in a driver's license suspension case that found respondent driver to be in violation of Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1 (Supp. 2006) after he refused to take an alcohol concentration test following a traffic stop for speeding. The state supreme court granted petitioner state motor vehicle's petition for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The driver's license was suspended after he refused to take an alcohol concentration test following a traffic stop for speeding. The driver challenged the suspension. An administrative law judge (ALJ) found the driver to be in violation of Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1 (Supp. 2006). The ALJ's ruling was based on a form filed by the arresting police officer. That form indicated that early one morning, the police officer saw the driver operating his vehicle in excess of 132 miles per hour, that he stopped the vehicle, that there was a strong odor of alcohol on the driver's breath, that the driver had bloodshot and watery eyes, that the driver blew a preliminary breath test of 0.10, and that the driver admitted drinking two beers. On appeal, the trial court vacated the ALJ's ruling because it found that the arresting police officer had not stated the reason that field sobriety tests, which the driver failed, were not performed to the police officer's satisfaction. On further review, the state's highest court found that the administrative ruling was based on substantial evidence and was not rendered based on an erroneous conclusion of law.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with instructions to affirm the ruling of the administrative law judge presiding over the driver's license suspension hearing.
